Retraction after Time-Specific Manumission Testimony: Valuation Date
Ruling on retraction after time-specific manumission testimony.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi ruling that when witnesses retract after a judge's manumission ruling based on a past date, the value is assessed on the judgment day, and distinguish the retroactive effect for other legal consequences.

Core Idea
For retracted manumission testimony, the slave's value is assessed at judgment day, though freedom is retroactive for hudud and injuries.

This lesson examines a specific scenario in shahadat (testimony) where witnesses testify that a slave was manumitted at a past time, the judge rules accordingly, and then the witnesses retract. The Hanafi school distinguishes between the retroactive effect of freedom for certain legal consequences and the assessment of the guarantee (daman) for the witnesses. Understanding this distinction is crucial for applying rules of testimony and liability.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scenario
Recognize the elements: (1) witnesses testify to manumission at a specific past time, (2) judge rules manumission, (3) witnesses retract. Note the two legal consequences: the slave's status (free) and the witnesses' liability.
The passage focuses on the liability, but also mentions retroactive effects for hudud and injuries.
2
State the two-part ruling
First, for legal consequences like hudud and injury compensation, the slave is treated as free from the past date (Ramadan) because the judge's ruling retroactively establishes freedom. Second, for the guarantee (daman), the witnesses must pay the slave's value assessed on the day of judgment, not the past date.
This is the core distinction.
3
Explain the reasoning for value assessment
The loss to the master occurs when he is prevented from his property, which happens on the day of judgment when the judge's ruling takes effect. Therefore, the value is assessed at that time.
The text says: 'because the loss occurred on the day of judgment, because the prevention and obstruction between the master and his slave occurred on the day of judgment.'
4
Explain the reasoning for retroactive freedom
The judge's ruling is based on upright testimony, which is treated like direct observation. Thus, the freedom is established from the testified date (Ramadan) for legal consequences that depend on the status, such as hudud and injury compensation.
This is a separate principle from the guarantee.
5
Apply the ruling to a new scenario
Suppose witnesses testify manumission on 1 Jan 2020, judge rules on 1 June 2020, then retract. Slave commits a theft in Feb 2020. The slave's status for hadd is free (retroactive), so no hadd. For witnesses' guarantee, value is assessed on 1 June 2020.
This illustrates the practical separation.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ولو شهدا أنه أعتق عبده عام الأول في رمضان وقضى القاضي بعتقه ثم رجعا ضمنا قيمة العبد يوم أعتقه القاضي وحكمه في حدوده وجزاء جناية فيما بين رمضان إلى أن أعتقه القاضي حكم الحر لأن القاضي أثبت حريته من رمضان بالبينة، والثابتة بالبينة العادلة كالثابت بالمعاينة، وفي حق إيجاب الضمان يعتبر حراً يوم القضاء لأن التلف حصل يوم القضاء لأن المنع والحيلولة بين المولى وعبده حصل يوم القضاء.
And if they testify that he manumitted his slave in the previous year in Ramadan, and the judge ruled his manumission, then they retracted, they guarantee the value of the slave on the day the judge manumitted him. And his ruling in his [the slave's] limits and penalty for injury between Ramadan and the time the judge manumitted him is the ruling of a free person, because the judge established his freedom from Ramadan by the evidence, and what is established by upright evidence is like what is established by direct observation. And regarding the imposition of the guarantee, he is considered free on the day of judgment, because the loss occurred on the day of judgment, because the prevention and obstruction between the master and his slave occurred on the day of judgment.
Source pages p. 229

Commentary
This passage addresses a scenario where witnesses testify that a slave was manumitted in Ramadan of the previous year, and the judge rules in favor of the manumission (effective from that past date). Then the witnesses retract. The ruling: The witnesses must pay the value of the slave as of the day the judge pronounced the manumission (the day of judgment), not the earlier date. The reasoning: For legal consequences like limits (hudud) and injury compensation, the slave is treated as free from the earlier date (Ramadan) because the judge's ruling, based on upright testimony, retroactively establishes freedom from that date. However, for the purpose of imposing the guarantee on the witnesses, the loss is considered to occur on the day of judgment, because that is when the master lost access to his slave (the court order prevented him from using the slave). So the value is assessed at judgment day.

Key Terms
ضمان القيمة (daman al-qima): Guarantee of the market value of the slave at a specific time (here, the day of judgment).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
When witnesses retract after a time-specific manumission testimony, the slave's value is assessed on:
A) The date of alleged manumission
B) The date of testimony
C) The date of judgment
D) The date of retraction

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi law, when witnesses retract after a judge's manumission ruling based on a past date, the value for their guarantee is assessed on judgment day, not the alleged manumission date, because the loss occurs at judgment.

Liability of Retracting Tadbir and Manumission Witnesses
Ruling on retraction of tadbir and manumission witnesses with sequence.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to differentiate the liability of witnesses who retract tadbir and manumission testimony in both simultaneous and sequential scenarios, applying the Hanafi rule.

Core Idea
When tadbir and manumission testimonies conflict, liability depends on the sequence of judgments and the effect of each ruling.

This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq addresses a nuanced fiqh scenario: what happens when witnesses for tadbir and witnesses for absolute manumission both testify and then retract? The ruling distinguishes between simultaneous and sequential judgments, allocating liability based on the legal effect of each testimony.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two types of witnesses
Note that one set testifies to tadbir (deferred manumission) and the other to absolute (immediate) manumission. Their testimonies conflict in effect.
2
Distinguish simultaneous vs. sequential judgments
In simultaneous testimony, the tadbir judgment cannot stand because absolute manumission is incompatible. In sequential, the tadbir judgment is valid at its time.
3
Apply the rule for liability
For simultaneous: only manumission witnesses are liable. For sequential: tadbir witnesses liable for diminution, manumission witnesses liable for the mudabbar's value.
4
Reason through the talil
The tadbir judgment, when effective, creates a loss of ownership rights; the manumission testimony then causes total loss. Each set compensates for the specific loss caused.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ثم قال : ولو شهدا بالتدبير وآخران بالعتق فرجعوا فالضمان على شهود العتق لأن القضاء بالتدبير مع العتق لا يفيد لأن حكم التدبير بقاء الرق إلى وقت الموت، ولا يبقى الرق مع العتق البات فلا يقضى بالتدبير، فإن قضى بشهادة التدبير ثم شهد آخران بالعتق البات فقضى به ثم رجعوا ضمن شهود التدبير ما نقصه التدبير وشهود العتق قيمته مدبراً لأن القضاء بالتدبير يفيد حكمه لأنه ليس حالة القضاء بالتدبير شهادة قائمة بالعتق فأمكن القضاء بالتدبير، وشاهد العتق أزالا المدبر عن ملكه بغير عوض فيضمنان قيمته مدبراً اهـ.
Then he said: And if two testify to tadbir and two others to [immediate] manumission, and they retract, the liability is upon the witnesses of manumission, because the judgment of tadbir together with manumission is of no benefit, because the ruling of tadbir is the continuation of slavery until death, and slavery does not continue with absolute manumission, so tadbir is not judged. If he judged by the tadbir testimony, then two others testified to absolute manumission and he judged by it, then they retracted, the witnesses of tadbir guarantee what the tadbir diminished, and the witnesses of manumission guarantee its value as a mudabbar, because the judgment of tadbir had effect because at the time of judgment of tadbir there was no testimony of manumission standing, so tadbir could be judged. And the witnesses of manumission removed the mudabbar from his ownership without compensation, so they guarantee its value as a mudabbar. End.
Source pages p. 229

Commentary
This passage discusses a scenario where two witnesses testify that a slave was made mudabbar (a slave whose manumission is deferred until the master's death), and then two other witnesses testify to an immediate (absolute) manumission. Then both sets retract. The ruling: If the testimonies are simultaneous, the tadbir witnesses are ignored because tadbir is incompatible with absolute manumission; only the manumission witnesses are liable. However, if the tadbir testimony is heard first and the judge rules accordingly (establishing the slave as mudabbar), then later the absolute manumission witnesses testify and the judge rules (overriding the tadbir), and then all retract: The tadbir witnesses are liable for the diminution in value caused by the tadbir (since it restricted the owner's right to sell, etc.), and the manumission witnesses are liable for the full value of the slave as a mudabbar (i.e., the market value of a mudabbar, which is typically half the value of an absolute slave). The reasoning: The tadbir judgment was valid at its time because no contrary testimony existed. The manumission witnesses then caused the loss of the mudabbar without compensation, so they pay its value.

Key Terms
تدبير (tadbir): A contract where a master declares that his slave will be free upon the master's death. It is a form of deferred manumission.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If two witnesses testify to tadbir and later two others testify to absolute manumission, then all retract after both judgments, what is the liability of the tadbir witnesses?
A) They pay full value of the slave.
B) They pay the diminution caused by tadbir.
C) They pay half the value.
D) They are not liable.

Key Takeaway
When testimony for tadbir and manumission conflict, liability is apportioned based on the sequence of judgments and the legal effect each testimony had.

Witness Retraction in Tadbir: Guarantee and Correction of al-Zayla'i's Error
Continuation of tadbir ruling with details on payment and correction of earlier commentator

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to calculate the guarantee owed by retracting witnesses in a tadbir case when the master dies with no other property, and identify the correct view from al-Mabsut over al-Zayla'i's error.

Core Idea
Retracting tadbir witnesses guarantee only the freed portion (1/3 value), not the full value — al-Zayla'i's error corrected.

This passage from al-Bahr al-Raiq details the liability of witnesses who retract after testifying to tadbir. It presents the ruling from al-Muhit, corrects a misunderstanding by the commentator al-Zayla'i, and establishes the mufta bihi value of a mudabbar. Understanding this case helps you apply the principles of witness guarantee (daman al-shuhud) in partial manumission scenarios.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scenario and the witnesses' act
Witnesses testify that a slave is mudabbar; the judge rules based on that testimony; then the witnesses retract. Determine what loss their testimony caused.
Tadbir removes the master's right to sell, diminishing ownership.
2
Determine the loss caused by their testimony
The witnesses guarantee the diminution in value caused by the tadbir. If the master dies and the slave becomes partially free, the loss is crystallized.
3
Apply the rule when the master dies with no other property
Per the rule of wasiyyah (bequest), only one third of the slave is freed; the slave must earn to pay two thirds of his value to the heirs.
The slave does not become fully free.
4
Calculate the witnesses' liability
The witnesses guarantee one third of the value of the slave as mudabbar (the freed portion). They do not guarantee the full value.
This contradicts al-Zayla'i who said they guarantee the full value.
5
Correct the error and note the recovery mechanism
If the slave is unable to pay the two thirds, the heirs recover from the witnesses; the witnesses then recover that amount from the slave when able (per Sahibayn).
Al-Mabsut explicitly states only one third is guaranteed.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ثلثه عتق وفي العتابية : ولو شهد واحد بإقراره بالعتق أمس وآخر بإقراره بالعتق من سنة وقضى به ثم أقام الشاهدان بينة على إعتاقه من سنين برئا عن الضمان وهذا قولهما لأن عندهما الدعوى ليس بشرط .اهـ. يعني ثم رجعا بعد القضاء ثم برهنا ولم يذكر المؤلف رحمه الله التدبير والكتابة والاستيلاد والولاء؛ أما الأول ففي المحيط : لو شهدا أنه دبر عبده فقضى ثم رجعا ضمنا ما نقصه التدبير فإنه بالتدبير فات بعض المنافع من حيث التجارة بالإخراج عن ملكه فانتقض ملكه فضمنا نقصانه بتفويتهما، وإن مات المولى والعبد يخرج من وضمن الشاهدان قيمته مدبراً لأنهما أزالا الباقي عن ملك الورثة بغير عوض، فإن لم يكن له مال غير العبد عتق ثلثه وسعى في ثلثيه وضمن الشاهدان ثلث القيمة بغير عوض ولم يرجعا به على العبد، فإن عجز العبد عن الثلثين يرجع به الورثة على الشاهدين ويرجع به على العبد عندهما .اهـ. وبه علم أن ما ذكره الشارح الزيلعي من أن العبد إذا كان معسراً فإنهما يضمنان جميع قيمته مدبراً ويرجعان به عليه إذا أيسر سهو لما علمت أنه إنما يرجعان عليه بالثلثين وهو مصرح به لما في المبسوط، وصرح فيه بأنهما يضمنان ثلث قيمته مدبراً، وعليه يحمل ما في المحيط، وقدمنا أن الفتوى أن قيمته مدبراً نصف قيمته لو كان قناً.
One third of him is free. And in al-Atabiyya: And if one witness testifies to his admission of manumission yesterday and another testifies to his admission of manumission a year ago, and the judge rules by it, then the two witnesses establish evidence that he manumitted years ago, they are absolved from the guarantee. This is their statement because according to them, the claim is not a condition. End. Meaning: then they retracted after the judgment and then proved. And the author (may Allah have mercy on him) did not mention tadbir, kitaba, istilad, and wala. As for the first: In al-Muhit: If they testify that he made his slave mudabbar and the judge ruled, then they retract, they guarantee what the tadbir diminished. For by tadbir, some benefits are lost in terms of trade by taking him out of ownership, so his ownership is diminished, so they guarantee its decrease by the loss. And if the master dies and the slave exits [from his estate], and the two witnesses guarantee its value as mudabbar because they removed the remaining part from the ownership of the heirs without compensation. So if he has no property other than the slave, one third of him is free, and he seeks to earn for two thirds, and the two witnesses guarantee one third of the value without compensation and do not recover it from the slave. Then if the slave is unable to pay the two thirds, the heirs recover it from the two witnesses, and they recover it from the slave according to them. End. From this it is known that what the commentator al-Zayla'i mentioned, that if the slave is poor, then they guarantee all of its value as mudabbar and recover it from him when he becomes wealthy, is a mistake. For you know that they only recover from him the two thirds, and it is explicit in al-Mabsut. And it is explicit in it that they guarantee one third of its value as mudabbar, and on this basis what is in al-Muhit is interpreted. And we have mentioned that the fatwa is that its value as mudabbar is half of its value if it were a qin (absolute slave).
Source pages p. 230

Commentary
This passage continues the discussion of tadbir witnesses. It first mentions a related case from al-Atabiyya: If one witness testifies to an admission of manumission 'yesterday' and another to an admission 'a year ago', and the judge rules, then the witnesses later prove (with evidence) that the manumission actually occurred years ago, they are absolved. This is according to Abu Yusuf and Muhammad, for whom a claim (da'wa) is not a condition for the permissibility of evidence. The commentator notes that the author of Kanz al-Daqaiq did not mention tadbir, kitaba, istilad, and wala. The main tadbir case from al-Muhit: If witnesses testify that a slave was mudabbar, the judge rules, then they retract, they guarantee the diminution caused by tadbir (the loss of the master's right to sell, etc.). If the master dies and the slave is freed (as per tadbir), and the witnesses retract, they must pay the value of the slave as mudabbar to the heirs. But if the master has no other property besides this slave, then only one third of the slave is freed (according to the rule of wasiyyah), and the slave must work to pay two thirds of his value to the heirs. The witnesses guarantee one third of the value (the freed portion) without compensation, and they cannot recover from the slave. If the slave fails to pay the two thirds, the heirs recover from the witnesses, and the witnesses can then recover from the slave (according to the Sahibayn). The commentator corrects a mistake by al-Zayla'i: He thought that if the slave is poor, the witnesses guarantee the entire value as mudabbar and later recover from the slave; but the correct view (from al-Mabsut) is that they only guarantee one third, and they recover only two thirds from the slave if he becomes able. Also, the fatwa value of a mudabbar is half that of an absolute slave.

Key Terms
قن (qinn): An absolute slave who is fully owned, with no restrictions like tadbir or kitaba.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In the tadbir case where the master dies with no property except the slave, what portion of the value do the retracting witnesses guarantee?
A) The full value as mudabbar.
B) One third of the value as mudabbar.
C) Two thirds of the value.
D) Half the value.

Key Takeaway
Retracting tadbir witnesses guarantee only the freed portion (one third) when the master dies insolvent; al-Zayla'i's contrary view is corrected by al-Mabsut.

Retraction of Kitaba Testimony: Liabilities and Options
Ruling on retraction of kitaba testimony

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi rulings when witnesses retract kitaba testimony and explain the master's options and the disposition of excess payments.

Core Idea
Retracting witnesses guarantee the slave's value; master chooses between holding them or pursuing the kitaba.

When witnesses testify to a kitaba contract and then retract, their testimony is considered false, and they must compensate for any harm caused. This lesson examines the rules from al-Muhit regarding the master's options, the slave's status, and the treatment of any excess payment. It also corrects a common misprint in Fath al-Qadir about who gets the wala.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Scenario
Read the first scenario: two witnesses testify that a master made a kitaba with his slave for 1000 dirhams payable in one year, the judge rules, then they retract.
The kitaba price is 1000, but the slave's value is 500 (as per later subcase).
2
Determine the Witnesses' Liability
The witnesses guarantee the slave's value (500). The slave does not become free until he pays the 1000 to the witnesses. Upon payment, he is free and wala goes to the original master.
If the slave fails to pay, he returns to slavery, and the master returns the value taken from the witnesses.
3
Analyze the Master's Options
When the kitaba price (1000) exceeds the slave's value (500), the master can choose: either hold the witnesses liable for the value (500) and let the slave pay 1000 to the witnesses, or pursue the slave for the full kitaba price without holding the witnesses.
If the master chooses to hold witnesses, the witnesses give any excess (1000-500=500) in charity according to Abu Hanifa, but Abu Yusuf says it is lawful for them.
4
Examine the Correction in Fath al-Qadir
Note the correction: wala belongs to 'the one who made the kitaba' (the master), not 'those who testified' as a misprint had it.
This emphasizes that testimony does not transfer ownership or patronage.
5
Consider the Other Subcases
The passage also covers: the slave claiming kitaba, the master denying; and witnesses retracting after the slave has paid. In such cases, witnesses compensate the slave.
If the slave denies kitaba and the master claims it, the master's evidence is not accepted because it would create a contract the slave denies.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وأما الثاني ففي المحيط : شهدا أنه كاتب عبده على ألف إلى سنة فقضى ثم رجعا يضمنان قيمته ولا يعتق حتى يؤدي ما عليه إليهما، فإذا أداه عتق والولاء للذي كاتبه فإن عجز فرد في الرق كان لمولاه أن يرد ما أخذه على الشهود اهـ. وبه علم أن ما في فتح القدير من أن الولاء للذين شهدوا عليه بالكتابة سهو، والصواب للذي بدل الذين ويطيب لهما ما أخذا . المكاتب إن كان بدل الكتابة مثل قيمته أو أقل، وإن كان أكثر تصدقا بالفضل، وإن أراد المولى اتباع المكاتب ولا يضمنهم كان له ذلك، ذكره الشارح . وفي المحيط : شهدا أنه كاتب عبده على ألف إلى سنة وقيمته خمسمائة ثم رجعا يخير المولى بين تضمين الشاهدين وبين اتباع العبد بالكتابة إلى أجله فإن اختار المولى ضمان الشاهدين وقبض منهما القيمة لم يعتق المكاتب حتى يؤدي ألف إلى الشاهدين ويتصدقان بالفضل، وعند أبي يوسف يطيب له الفضل فإن تقاضي المولى المكاتب وهو يعلم برجوع الشاهدين أو لا يعلم فهو رضا بالكتابة، ولا يضمنان إلا إذا كانت المكاتبة أقل من القيمة فله أن يأخذ المكاتبة ويرجع عليهما بفضل القيمة اهـ. ولم يذكر الشارحون ما إذا شهدا على المكاتب ثم رجعا وفي المحيط : ادعى العبد أن مولاه كاتبه على ألف وأنه قيمته وقال المولى كاتبته على ألفين وأقام البينة وقضى ثم أداها ثم رجعوا ضمنوا للمكاتب، فإن أنكر المكاتب الكتابة وادعاها المولى على ألفين لم تقبل بينته عليه
As for the second, in al-Muhit: They testified that he made a kitaba contract with his slave for one thousand [dirhams] payable in one year, and the judge ruled, then they retracted. They guarantee his value, and he does not become free until he pays what is owed to them. When he pays, he becomes free, and the wala belongs to the one who made the kitaba. If he fails and is returned to slavery, his master may return what he took to the witnesses. End. From this it is known that what is in Fath al-Qadir, that the wala belongs to those who testified against him regarding the kitaba, is a mistake. The correct is 'for the one' instead of 'those', and what they took is lawful for them. The mukatab, if the kitaba price equals his value or less, [it is fine]; if it is more, they give the excess in charity. And if the master wants to pursue the mukatab and not hold them liable, he may do so, as mentioned by the commentator. And in al-Muhit: They testified that he made a kitaba contract with his slave for one thousand in one year, and his value is five hundred, then they retracted. The master is given the choice between holding the witnesses liable or pursuing the slave for the kitaba until its term. If the master chooses holding the witnesses liable and takes the value from them, the mukatab does not become free until he pays one thousand to the witnesses, and they give the excess in charity. According to Abu Yusuf, the excess is lawful for them. If the master demands from the mukatab knowing of the witnesses' retraction or not, it is consent to the kitaba, and they are not liable unless the kitaba price is less than the value; then he may take the kitaba price and recover the excess from them. End. And the commentators did not mention the case of testifying against the mukatab and then retracting. And in al-Muhit: The slave claimed that his master made a kitaba with him for one thousand and that he [the slave] was of that value, and the master said 'I made a kitaba for two thousand' and established evidence, and the judge ruled, then the slave paid, then they retracted; they guarantee for the mukatab. If the mukatab denies the kitaba and the master claims it for two thousand, his evidence against him is not accepted.
Source pages p. 230

Commentary
This passage covers the rules for witnesses who retract testimony about a kitaba contract (a contract where a slave purchases his freedom by paying installments). The main case: Two witnesses testify that a master made a kitaba with his slave for 1000 dirhams payable in one year. The judge rules accordingly, then the witnesses retract. The ruling: The witnesses guarantee the value of the slave (which is less than the kitaba price, as seen later). The slave does not become free until he pays the kitaba amount to the witnesses (since the witnesses now stand in place of the master? Actually careful: The judgment established the kitaba. After retraction, the witnesses must pay the value to the master. The slave pays the kitaba price to the witnesses (who then give any excess in charity, per Abu Hanifa, or keep it per Abu Yusuf). The wala remains with the original master. The passage also corrects a misprint in Fath al-Qadir: the wala belongs to 'the one who made the kitaba' (the master), not 'those who testified'. Then a subcase: If the slave's value is 500 and the kitaba price is 1000, the master may choose to either hold the witnesses liable for the value (500) and then the slave must pay 1000 to the witnesses, who give 500 excess in charity; or the master may continue to collect from the slave according to the kitaba, in which case the witnesses are not liable unless the kitaba price is less than the value, then the master can take the price and claim the excess from the witnesses. Another subcase: If a slave claims kitaba for 1000, the master claims for 2000, and the judge rules based on the master's evidence, then the slave pays and the witnesses retract, the witnesses must compensate the slave. If the slave denies kitaba and the master claims it for 2000, the master's evidence is not accepted because the slave is denying the basis.

Key Terms
كتابة (kitaba): A contract between a master and his slave whereby the slave purchases his freedom by paying a specified sum in installments.
مكاتب (mukatab): A slave who has entered into a kitaba contract and is working to earn his freedom.
ولاء (wala): Patronage rights that arise from manumission, entitling the manumitter to inherit from the freed slave.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In the scenario where two witnesses retract their kitaba testimony (kitaba price 1000, slave value 500), what happens if the master chooses to hold the witnesses liable?
A) The slave becomes free immediately without payment.
B) The witnesses pay 500 to the master, and the slave pays 1000 to the witnesses, who give the excess in charity.
C) The witnesses pay 1000 to the master, and the slave is free.
D) The master receives 500 from the witnesses and must release the slave for free.

Key Takeaway
Retracting witnesses guarantee the slave's value, and the master may choose between holding them liable or enforcing the kitaba against the slave.

Witness Retraction and Subsequent Proof of Manumission
Ruling on retraction of testimony with subsequent proof of manumission

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling when witnesses retract testimony of 'itq but later prove their testimony, and explain the intra-Hanafi difference on the requirement of da'wa.

Core Idea
Witnesses who retract are not liable if they later prove their testimony was true; da'wa is not a condition per Sahibayn.

This lesson examines a nuanced scenario in testimony (shahada): witnesses who have given testimony about a master's acknowledgment of manumission later retract, but then produce evidence that the manumission occurred earlier. We will see how the Hanafi school handles this, and note the important difference between Imam Abu Hanifa and his two students on whether a formal claim (da'wa) is a prerequisite for valid testimony.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scenario
One witness testifies to the master's acknowledgment of manumission yesterday, another to acknowledgment a year ago. Judgment is passed. Then the witnesses retract but later bring evidence that the actual manumission was years before.
2
State the ruling of the Sahibayn
According to Abu Yusuf and Muhammad, the witnesses are exempt from liability (daman) for their retraction because their testimony was eventually proven true.
This is the mufta bihi position in the passage.
3
Explain the rationale
The Sahibayn hold that a formal claim (da'wa) is not a condition for the validity of testimony. Thus, even if the witnesses retract, the truth that emerges later validates their original act.
The ruling relies on the principle that substantive truth overcomes procedural retraction.
4
Note the disagreement of Abu Hanifa
Abu Hanifa requires a da'wa (formal claim) for testimony to be valid. Without it, the testimony is invalid from the start, and retraction would render the witnesses liable for the consequences.
This intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf has practical implications for witness liability.
5
Apply the principle
In practice, under the Sahibayn's view, a witness can safely retract if they can later prove the truth of their earlier statement. Under Abu Hanifa, they would need a valid da'wa from the outset to avoid liability.
This shows the importance of procedural conditions in Hanafi law.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وفي العتابية : ولو شهد واحد بإقراره بالعتق أمس وآخر بإقراره بالعتق من سنة وقضى به ثم أقام الشاهدان بينة على إعتاقه من سنين برئا عن الضمان وهذا قولهما لأن عندهما الدعوى ليس بشرط .اهـ. يعني ثم رجعا بعد القضاء ثم برهنا ولم يذكر المؤلف رحمه الله التدبير والكتابة والاستيلاد والولاء؛
And in al-Atabiyyah: If one witness testified to his (the master's) acknowledgment of manumission yesterday, and another to his acknowledgment of manumission a year ago, and judgment was passed on it, then the two witnesses produced evidence of his manumission years ago, they are exempt from liability. This is their (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad's) position, because according to them, the claim (da'wa) is not a condition. End. Meaning, they retracted after judgment and then proved it. And the author (may Allah have mercy on him) did not mention tadbir, kitabah, istilad, and wala'.
Source pages p. 230

Commentary
This passage from Al-Atabiyyah presents a ruling on retraction of testimony regarding manumission ('itq). The scenario: two witnesses testify to different times of the master's acknowledgment of manumission—one says 'yesterday,' the other says 'a year ago.' The judge rules based on this, but later the witnesses themselves bring evidence that the actual manumission occurred years earlier. According to the Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani), they are exempt from liability (daman) for the retraction because their testimony was eventually corroborated. The reason: in their view, a formal claim (da'wa) is not a prerequisite for the validity of testimony; the truth may emerge later. Abu Hanifa differs, requiring a claim. The author then notes that the original author (of Kanz al-Daqa'iq) did not cover the cases of tadbir (stipulated emancipation after death), kitabah (contract of manumission), istilad (motherhood from master), and wala' (clientage), which will be discussed next.

Key Terms
الدعوى (al-da'wa): The formal claim or lawsuit required to initiate trial proceedings

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Sahibayn, why are the witnesses exempt from liability in the 'itq case?
A) Because they retracted before judgment
B) Because they proved their testimony true with new evidence
C) Because the master admitted the manumission
D) Because the judge made an error

Key Takeaway
Under the Sahibayn's view, witnesses who retract but later prove their testimony true are exempt from liability because da'wa is not a condition for testimony validity.

Witness Retraction in Tadbir: Liability for Diminution
Ruling on witness retraction in tadbir: liability and recourse.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to calculate the witnesses' liability when they retract after testifying to tadbir and apply the Sahibayn's rule on claiming back from the slave.

Core Idea
Witnesses who retract after tadbir testimony guarantee only the one-third freed part, not the full value.

When witnesses retract their testimony after judgment, they cause a loss that must be compensated. The tadbir case adds complexity because the slave's value is divided: one-third is freed from the estate, and two-thirds must be earned by the slave. This lesson unpacks the precise liability and the intra-Hanafi difference on whether witnesses can claim back from the slave.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Scenario
Understand the case: two witnesses testify that a master made his slave mudabbar (stipulated freedom upon death). Judgment is passed. Then the witnesses retract.
The retraction occurs after the court ruling.
2
Determine the Basic Liability
Because tadbir reduces the slave's marketability, the witnesses must guarantee the diminution in value. If the master dies and the slave is freed from one-third, the witnesses owe the full value as mudabbar to the heirs (since they deprived the heirs of the property).
The value as mudabbar is half the value as a regular slave (qinn) per fatwa.
3
Analyze the Solvency Scenario
If the master has no other assets, only one-third of the slave is freed; the slave must earn two-thirds. The witnesses guarantee only one-third of the value (the freed portion) and do not claim it back from the slave.
They are not liable for the two-thirds the slave owes.
4
Handle the Slave's Incapacity
If the slave cannot earn the two-thirds, the heirs claim it from the witnesses. Then the witnesses can claim that amount back from the slave according to the Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad).
Abu Hanifa's view is not mentioned here; the Sahibayn's position is the mufta bihi.
5
Correct a Common Mistake
Al-Zayla'i stated that witnesses guarantee the full mudabbar value and claim it back from the slave. The author corrects this: they only guarantee one-third and can only claim back two-thirds (when the heirs claim from them).
The authority is al-Mabsut and al-Muhit.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
أما الأول ففي المحيط : لو شهدا أنه دبر عبده فقضى ثم رجعا ضمنا ما نقصه التدبير فإنه بالتدبير فات بعض المنافع من حيث التجارة بالإخراج عن ملكه فانتقض ملكه فضمنا نقصانه بتفويتهما، وإن مات المولى والعبد يخرج من وضمن الشاهدان قيمته مدبراً لأنهما أزالا الباقي عن ملك الورثة بغير عوض، فإن لم يكن له مال غير العبد عتق ثلثه وسعى في ثلثيه وضمن الشاهدان ثلث القيمة بغير عوض ولم يرجعا به على العبد، فإن عجز العبد عن الثلثين يرجع به الورثة على الشاهدين ويرجعان به على العبد عندهما .اهـ. وبه علم أن ما ذكره الشارح الزيلعي من أن العبد إذا كان معسراً فإنهما يضمنان جميع قيمته مدبراً ويرجعان به عليه إذا أيسر سهو لما علمت أنه إنما يرجعان عليه بالثلثين وهو مصرح به لما في المبسوط، وصرح فيه بأنهما يضمنان ثلث قيمته مدبراً، وعليه يحمل ما في المحيط، وقدمنا أن الفتوى أن قيمته مدبراً نصف قيمته لو كان قناً.
As for the first (tadbir), in al-Muhit: If they testified that he (the master) made his slave mudabbar, and judgment was passed, then they retracted, they must guarantee what the tadbir diminished (in value). Because by tadbir some benefits are lost in terms of trade by removal from his ownership, so his ownership was diminished; they guarantee its diminution due to their causing it. If the master dies and the slave is to be freed (from one-third), the witnesses guarantee his value as mudabbar, because they removed the remainder from the heirs' ownership without compensation. If the master has no property other than the slave, one-third of the slave is freed, he must earn two-thirds, and the witnesses guarantee one-third of the value without compensation and do not claim it back from the slave. If the slave is unable to (earn) the two-thirds, the heirs claim it from the witnesses, and they (the witnesses) in turn claim it from the slave according to them (Sahibayn). End. And from this it is known that what the commentator al-Zayla'i mentioned—that if the slave is insolvent, they both guarantee the full mudabbar value and claim it back from him when he becomes wealthy—is an oversight, because as you have learned, they only claim back two-thirds, as is explicitly stated in al-Mabsut. And it is explicitly stated therein that they guarantee one-third of his value as mudabbar, and upon this is based what is in al-Muhit. And we have previously stated that the fatwa is that his value as mudabbar is half his value if he were a slave (qinn).
Source pages p. 230

Commentary
This passage from al-Muhit explains the liability of witnesses who retract after testifying that a master made his slave mudabbar (i.e., stipulated that the slave would be free upon the master's death). The ruling: they must guarantee the diminution in the slave's value caused by the tadbir—because tadbir removes the slave's marketability (some benefits are lost). If the master dies and the slave is freed from one-third of the estate, the witnesses must pay the full value as mudabbar to the heirs, since they deprived the heirs of that property. If the master has no other assets, only one-third of the slave is freed; the slave must earn two-thirds of his value. The witnesses guarantee one-third of the slave's value (as mudabbar) to cover that freed portion, and they cannot claim that from the slave. If the slave cannot earn the two-thirds, the heirs can claim from the witnesses, and the witnesses can then claim from the slave—this is the position of the Sahibayn. The commentator corrects al-Zayla'i, who mistakenly thought the witnesses guarantee the entire mudabbar value; they only guarantee the one-third freed part and claim back two-thirds from the slave. The fatwa is that a mudabbar slave's value is half of his value as a regular slave (qinn).

Key Terms
مُدَبَّر (mudabbar): A slave whom the master has declared will be free upon the master's death.
الضمان (al-daman): Liability to compensate for loss caused by retraction.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In the tadbir case, if the master has no other property, what portion of the slave's value do the witnesses guarantee?
A) The full mudabbar value
B) One-half the mudabbar value
C) One-third the mudabbar value
D) Two-thirds the mudabbar value

Key Takeaway
Witnesses who retract after tadbir testimony guarantee only the one-third freed portion of the mudabbar value and, per the Sahibayn, can claim back two-thirds from the slave if the heirs claim from them.

Retraction of Testimony on Kitabah: Master's Options
Ruling on witness retraction in kitabah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling when witnesses retract after testifying to a kitabah contract and apply the master's option to sue witnesses or pursue the slave.

Core Idea
When witnesses retract, wala' remains with the master; the slave is not free until he pays the full kitabah amount, and the master chooses between suing witnesses or the slave.

In this passage from al-Muhit, we examine a detailed ruling on witness retraction after they testified to a kitabah contract. The master is given an option, and the slave's freedom is conditional. We also see an intra-Hanafi difference on whether witnesses can keep any excess payment.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is witness retraction after testifying to kitabah. Ruling: witnesses guarantee the slave's value; slave not freed until he pays the kitabah amount to the witnesses.
2
Determine wala' ownership
Wala' belongs to the original master, not the witnesses.
Correction of a common error.
3
Master's option
The master can choose between suing the witnesses for the slave's value or pursuing the slave under the kitabah contract.
Choice is his, not compulsory.
4
Consequences of each choice
If he sues witnesses and receives value, the slave still must pay full kitabah to witnesses. If he pursues the slave, witnesses are not liable unless kitabah amount is less than value.
5
Note the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf
On whether witnesses can keep excess beyond the slave's value: the majority says give charity; Abu Yusuf says lawful.
The mufta bihi is charity.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وأما الثاني ففي المحيط : شهدا أنه كاتب عبده على ألف إلى سنة فقضى ثم رجعا يضمنان قيمته ولا يعتق حتى يؤدي ما عليه إليهما، فإذا أداه عتق والولاء للذي كاتبه فإن عجز فرد في الرق كان لمولاه أن يرد ما أخذه على الشهود ا هـ. وبه علم أن ما في فتح القدير من أن الولاء للذين شهدوا عليه بالكتابة سهو، والصواب للذي بدل الذين ويطيب لهما ما أخذا . المكاتب إن كان بدل الكتابة مثل قيمته أو أقل، وإن كان أكثر تصدقا بالفضل، وإن أراد المولى اتباع المكاتب ولا يضمنهم كان له ذلك، ذكره الشارح . وفي المحيط : شهدا أنه كاتب عبده على ألف إلى سنة وقيمته خمسمائة ثم رجعا يخير المولى بين تضمين الشاهدين وبين اتباع العبد بالكتابة إلى أجله فإن اختار المولى ضمان الشاهدين وقبض منهما القيمة لم يعتق المكاتب حتى يؤدي ألفاً إلى الشاهدين ويتصدقان بالفضل، وعند أبي يوسف يطيب له الفضل فإن تقاضي المولى المكاتب وهو يعلم برجوع الشاهدين أو لا يعلم فهو رضا بالكتابة، ولا يضمنان إلا إذا كانت المكاتبة أقل من القيمة فله أن يأخذ المكاتبة ويرجع عليهما بفضل القيمة اهـ.
As for the second (kitabah), in al-Muhit: If they testified that he (the master) made a kitabah contract with his slave for one thousand (dirhams) payable in one year, and judgment was passed, then they retracted, they guarantee his value, and the slave is not freed until he pays what he owes to them (the witnesses). When he pays, he is freed, and the wala' belongs to the one who made kitabah (the master). If he (the slave) becomes unable (to pay) and is returned to slavery, the master may return what he took from the witnesses. End. And from this it is known that what is in Fath al-Qadir—that the wala' belongs to those who testified against him regarding the kitabah—is an error. The correct is 'to the one who made kitabah' (i.e., the master), replacing 'those who'. And what they (witnesses) took is lawful for them. The mukatab: if the kitabah payment equals his value or less, (the witnesses keep it); if it is more, they give charity of the excess. If the master wishes to pursue the mukatab and not sue them (the witnesses), he may do so, as mentioned by the commentator. And in al-Muhit: If they testified that he made kitabah with his slave for one thousand in one year, and his value is five hundred, then they retracted, the master is given the choice between suing the witnesses (for value) and pursuing the slave under the kitabah until its term. If the master chooses to sue the witnesses and receives the value from them, the mukatab is not freed until he pays the one thousand to the witnesses, and they give charity of the excess. According to Abu Yusuf, the excess is lawful for them. If the master claims from the mukatab knowing of the witnesses' retraction or not knowing, it is consent to the kitabah, and they (witnesses) are not liable unless the kitabah payment is less than the value; then he may take the kitabah payment and claim the excess value from them. End.
Source pages p. 230

Commentary
This passage from al-Muhit covers retraction after testifying to a kitabah (contract of manumission where the slave pays installments). The ruling: the witnesses must guarantee the slave's value, and the slave does not become free until he pays the kitabah amount to the witnesses. When he pays, he is free and wala' (clientage) belongs to the original master (not to the witnesses). The commentator corrects a mistake in Fath al-Qadir that wala' goes to the witnesses. The witnesses can keep what they receive from the slave if it does not exceed the slave's value; if it exceeds, they must give the excess in charity (or, per Abu Yusuf, it is lawful for them). The master has an option: he can either claim the value from the witnesses (up to the slave's value) or pursue the slave under the kitabah contract. If he chooses the witnesses and takes the value, the slave still must pay the full kitabah to the witnesses (who then give charity of the excess). If the master pursues the slave, that is deemed consent to the kitabah, and the witnesses are not liable unless the kitabah amount is less than the slave's value, in which case the master can take the kitabah payment from the slave and claim the difference from the witnesses.

Key Terms
المكاتبة (al-mukatabah): A contract of manumission whereby the slave pays a sum in installments to the master
الولاء (al-wala'): Clientage relationship after manumission; inheritance rights belong to the master who freed the slave

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) The contract is void and the slave is free
B) The slave is not freed until he pays the kitabah amount to the witnesses
C) The slave is immediately free and owes nothing
D) The master must also pay the kitabah amount to the witnesses

Key Takeaway
When witnesses retract after kitabah testimony, the slave is not freed until he pays the full kitabah to the witnesses, and the master retains an option to sue either the witnesses or the slave.

Retraction in Istilad: Complex Liability for Umm Walad
Ruling on witness retraction after testifying that a slave-girl is umm walad

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to determine the liability of witnesses who retract their testimony that a slave-girl is umm walad, based on the timing of retraction, presence of a child, and the identity of heirs.

Core Idea
Witnesses who retract a testimony affecting a slave-girl's status as umm walad must compensate according to timing and heirs; the child's inheritance rights affect liability.

This passage from Badai' al-Sanai' presents a detailed ruling on the liability of witnesses who retract after testifying that a slave-girl is umm walad. The ruling is complex because it depends on whether the slave-girl has a child, when the retraction occurs (during the master's life or after his death), and who the heirs are. Understanding this helps you grasp how Hanafi law protects rights that change due to testimony.

Guided Path
1
Identify the core scenario
The witnesses testify that the master acknowledged the slave-girl gave birth to his child, the judge rules accordingly, then they retract. First, determine if the slave-girl has a child.
2
Calculate liability if no child and retraction during master's life
If no child and retraction during master's life, witnesses pay the diminution in value: the difference between her value as a regular slave (qinnah) and as umm walad (lower because she cannot be sold).
3
Calculate liability if no child and retraction after master's death
If the master dies, the slave-girl is freed, and witnesses pay the remainder of her value (full value as umm walad) to the heirs.
4
Calculate liability if the slave-girl has a child
If she has a child and witnesses retract during master's life, they guarantee the child's value plus the diminution. After master's death, if child is sole heir, no liability to child; witnesses can reclaim from child what master took. If child has a brother, witnesses pay the brother half of the remainder from their values and claim back from the child only what master took.
5
Consider retraction after master's death and testimony after death
If retraction occurs after master's death: if child has no partner, no liability; if child has a brother, witnesses pay brother half of the value of the child and half the slave's value, and cannot reclaim. If testimony was after death (claiming a slave is son of deceased), they guarantee values and half inheritance.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وأما الثالث ففي البدائع: شهدا على إقرار المولى أن هذه الأمة ولدت منه وهو ينكر فقضى القاضي بذلك ثم رجعا، فإن لم يكن معها ولد فرجعا في حياته ضمنا نقصان قيمتها بأن تقوم قنة وأم ولد لو جاز بيعها فيضمنان النقصان، فإن مات المولى عتقت وضمنا بقية قيمتها للورثة فإن كان معها ولد فرجعا في حياته ضمنا قيمة الولد مع ضمان نقصانها، فإن مات المولى بعده فإن لم يكن مع الولد شريك في الميراث لم يضمنا له شيئاً ورجعا على الولد بما قبض الأب منهما من تركته إن كانت وإلا فلا ضمان عليه، وإن كان معه أخ ضمنا له نصف البقية من قيمتهما ويرجعان على الولد بما أخذ الأب منهما لا بما قبض الأخ ولا يضمنان للأخ ما أخذه الولد من الميراث، فإن رجعا بعد وفاة المولى فإن لم يكن مع الولد شريك فلا ضمان عليهما وإلا ضمنا للأخ نصف البقية من قيمتهما ونصف قيمة الولد لا رائه ولا يرجعان على الولد هنا وإن كانت الشهادة بعد موت المولى بأن ترك ولداً وعبداً وأمة وتركة فشهدا أن هذا العبد ولدته هذه الأمة من الميت وصدقهما الولد والأمة لا الابن وقضى ثم رجعا ضمنا قيمة العبد والأمة ونصف الميراث اهـ.
As for the third (istilad), in al-Bada'i': If they testified to the master's acknowledgment that this slave-girl gave birth from him, while he (the master) denies it, and the judge ruled on that, then they retracted: if she has no child with her, and they retracted during his (the master's) lifetime, they guarantee the diminution of her value—she is valued as a slave-girl (qinnah) and as umm walad, as if her sale were allowed—so they guarantee the difference. If the master dies, she is freed, and they guarantee the remainder of her value to the heirs. If she has a child, and they retract during his lifetime, they guarantee the value of the child together with the guarantee of her diminution. If the master dies after that, and the child has no partner in inheritance, they do not guarantee anything to the child, and they claim back from the child what the father (the master) took from them from his estate—if there is an estate; otherwise, no liability on him. If he has a brother, they guarantee for the brother half of the remainder from their (the witnesses') values, and they claim back from the child what the father took from them, not what the brother received. And they do not guarantee for the brother what the child took from the inheritance. If they retract after the master's death: if the child has no partner, there is no liability on them; otherwise, they guarantee for the brother half of the remainder from their values and half the value of the child—not for him (the child?), and they do not claim back from the child here. And if the testimony is after the master's death—e.g., he left a child, a male slave, a female slave, and an estate, and they testified that this male slave was born of this female slave from the deceased, and the child and the female slave confirm it, but the son does not, and judgment is passed, then they retract—they guarantee the value of the male and female slaves and half the inheritance. End.
Source pages p. 231

Commentary
This long passage from al-Bada'i' (likely Badai' al-Sanai') details the liability of witnesses who retract after testifying that a slave-girl is umm walad (mother of her master's child), which grants her freedom upon the master's death. The ruling is complex and depends on several factors: whether she has a child, when the witnesses retract (during master's life or after his death), and who the heirs are. If no child and retraction during master's life: witnesses pay the difference in value between her as a regular slave and as umm walad (since her value is less as umm walad because she cannot be sold). If the master dies, she is freed, and witnesses pay the full value to heirs. If she has a child, witnesses also pay the child's value. After the master's death, if the child is the sole heir, witnesses are not liable to the child but can reclaim what the master took from them (if estate remains). If there is another heir (e.g., a brother), witnesses pay half the remaining value to that heir but can reclaim from the child what the master took, not what the brother received. If retraction occurs after the master's death, and the child is sole heir, no liability; if there is a brother, witnesses pay him half of the value of the child and half the slave's value, and cannot reclaim from the child. Finally, if testimony occurs post-death (witnesses claim a slave is the son of the deceased), they guarantee the values and half the inheritance.

Key Terms
أم ولد (umm walad): A slave-girl who bore a child to her master; she becomes free upon his death and cannot be sold.
الاستيلاد (istilad): The act of a master engendering a child on his slave-girl, making her umm walad.
ضمان (daman): Guarantee, liability, compensation.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If witnesses retract after the master's death and the slave-girl has a child who is the sole heir, what is the liability of the witnesses?
A) They pay the full value of the slave-girl to the child
B) They pay the diminution in value
C) They pay nothing, but can reclaim from the child what the master took from them
D) They pay the value of the child

Key Takeaway
The liability of witnesses who retract istilad testimony varies with the timing of retraction, presence of a child, and other heirs, reflecting the Hanafi principle of protecting changed legal statuses.

Retraction in Qisas: The Shubha Defence
Inter-madhhab dispute on witness retraction in qisas

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi position on witnesses' liability after retraction in a qisas case and evaluate the Shafi'i counter-argument using the principle of shubha.

Core Idea
Shubha prevents qisas but not property liability (diyah).

This passage presents a classic inter-madhhab dispute: what happens when witnesses retract their testimony after a qisas (retaliation) execution has already been carried out? The Hanafi school distinguishes between property claims (diyah) and corporal punishment (qisas), applying the principle that shubha (doubt) averts severe punishments but does not negate financial liability. Imam al-Shafi'i argues for qisas on the witnesses, equating them to coercers. You will learn why the Hanafis reject this analogy and how the rule 'hudud and qisas are averted by shubuhat' operates in practice.

Guided Path
1
Understand the scenario
Identify the factual situation: two (or more) witnesses testify in a qisas case, the victim's heir executes the retaliation, then the witnesses retract their testimony. The question is: what liability do the witnesses incur?
2
State the Hanafi ruling
According to the Hanafi school, the witnesses are liable for diyah (blood money) but are NOT subject to qisas themselves. This is the position of the matn (Kanz al-Daqaiq) and the commentary.
3
State the Shafi'i counter-position
Imam al-Shafi'i holds that the witnesses should be executed in qisas because their testimony caused the death indirectly, and they are like a coercer—indeed more so, because the wali (heir) is assisted by their testimony.
The coercer (mukrih) analogy is the core of the Shafi'i proof.
4
Analyse the Hanafi response
The Hanafi rebuttal is twofold: (1) The causal link is weak—testimony does not generally lead to death because the wali is recommended to forgive (afw) and accept diyah; (2) Even if there is a causal link, there is shubha (doubt) because the witnesses acted voluntarily but the execution was ordered by the judge. Shubha prevents qisas (following the principle 'idra'u al-hudud bi al-shubuhat').
The passage contrasts this with the coercer: the coercer directly threatens the victim's life, so his action generally leads to death.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf (practical consequence)
The practical difference: under the Hanafi view, the witnesses pay diyah (a financial penalty) and remain alive; under the Shafi'i view, they are executed in qisas. This dramatically affects the gravity of the witnesses' liability.
The Hanafi view also extends to related cases, such as witnesses retracting after testifying to a settlement (sulh) for a sum of money.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله: (وفي القصاص الدية ولم يقتصا) أي ضمن شاهد القصاص برجوعهما بعد الاستيفاء دية المشهود عليه ولا يقتص منهما. وقال الشافعي : يقتص منهما لوجود القتل تسبباً فأشبه المكره بل أولى لأن الولي يعان والمكره يمنع ولنا أن القتل مباشرة لم يوجد وكذا تسبباً لأن السبب ما يفضي إليه غالباً ولا يفضي لأن العفو مندوب بخلاف المكره لأنه يؤثر حياته ظاهراً، ولأن الفعل الاختياري مما يقطع النسبة ثم لا أقل من الشبهة وهي دارئة للقصاص بخلاف المال لأنه يثبت مع الشبهات أطلقه فيشمل ما إذا رجع الولي معهما أو لم يرجع لكن إن رجع معهما خير الولي بين تضمين الولي الدية أو الشاهدين كما لو جاء المشهود بقتله حياً، وأيهما ضمن لا يرجع على صاحبه عنده وعندهما له الرجوع عليه لأنهما عاملان له، واتفقوا على رجوعهما عليه في الخطأ وبيان الحجة من الجانبين في الشرح للزيلعي. وشمل ما إذا شهدوا به في النفس أو ما دونه، وقيد بالقصاص لأنهما لو شهدا بالعفو عن القصاص ثم رجعا لم يضمنا لأن القصاص ليس بمال ولو شهدا أنه صالحه من دم العمد على ألف ثم رجعا لم يضمنا أيهما كان المنكر للصلح، وقيل إذا كان القاتل منكراً فالصحيح أنهم يضمنون له الألف، والصحيح جواب الكتاب وتمامه في المحيط وفيه : شهدا أنه صالحه على عشرين ألفاً والقاتل يجحد فقضى ثم رجعا ضمنا الفضل على الدية وقيل الصحيح أن يضمنا جميع المال. قال الطالب صالحتك على ألف وقال الخصم لا بل عن خمسمائة فالقول للمدعى عليه
His saying: (And in qisas, the diyah, and they are not subjected to qisas) means: the witnesses of qisas, upon their retraction after execution, guarantee the diyah (blood money) of the person against whom they testified, and they are not subjected to qisas (retaliation). Al-Shafi'i said: They are subjected to qisas because they caused killing indirectly, so they are like a coercer (mukrih), indeed more so, because the legal guardian (wali) is assisted (by them) while the coercer is prevented. Our argument: direct killing did not occur, nor indirect, because the cause (sabab) is that which generally leads to the result, and it does not generally lead (to death), because forgiveness (afw) is recommended, unlike the coercer, because the coercer affects the victim's life apparently. Also, because the voluntary act cuts the attribution; then there is at least a shubha (doubt) which prevents qisas, unlike property, because property is established despite shubuhat. This is general, including whether the wali retracted with them or not. But if the wali retracts with them, the wali is given the choice between suing the wali (another? unclear) or suing the witnesses for the diyah, just as if the person testified to have been killed alive comes. And whichever is sued, he does not claim back from his companion according to him (Abu Hanifa?), while according to them (Sahibayn), he can claim back because both are working for him. And they agreed on their claim back in case of mistake (khatab). And the proof from both sides is in al-Zayla'i's commentary. And it includes whether they testified regarding life or less. And it is restricted to qisas because if they testified to forgiveness (afw) from qisas and then retracted, they do not guarantee because qisas is not property. And if they testified that he reconciled from intentional homicide for one thousand, then retracted, they do not guarantee whichever was the denier of the reconciliation. It is said: if the killer is the denier, the correct is that they guarantee the one thousand. And the correct is the answer of the book, and its completion is in al-Muhit. And in it: They testified that he reconciled for twenty thousand while the killer denied, so judgment was passed, then they retracted; they guarantee the excess beyond the diyah. It is said that the correct is that they guarantee the entire property. The claimant said: I reconciled with you for one thousand, and the opponent said: No, rather for five hundred; the statement is of the defendant.
Source pages p. 231

Commentary
This passage presents an inter-madhhab dispute regarding witnesses who retract after testifying in a qisas (retaliation) case, after the execution has already been carried out. The Hanafi position: the witnesses must pay diyah (blood money) to the victim's heirs, but they are not subject to qisas themselves. Imam al-Shafi'i argues that they should be subjected to qisas because their testimony caused the killing indirectly, and they are like a coercer (mukrih)—in fact, more so, because the legal guardian is assisted by their testimony while a coercer is restrained. The Hanafi response is twofold: first, their testimony does not generally lead to death because the victim's heirs are recommended to forgive (afw) and accept diyah, so the causal link is weak; second, there is a shubha (doubt) in their action because they acted voluntarily but the killing was executed by the state, and shubha prevents qisas (as per the principle that hudud and qisas are averted by doubts). However, it does not prevent liability for property (diyah), which is established even in cases of doubt. The passage also discusses nuances: if the wali (heir) retracts along with the witnesses, he has a choice to sue either the witnesses or another party. There is an intra-Hanafi difference on whether the witnesses can claim back from the person they sued. The text also addresses related cases: if witnesses testify to a reconciliation (sulh) for a sum and then retract, liability depends on who denied the reconciliation. In some cases, they guarantee the excess over diyah; in others, the entire sum. This is a complex area with multiple opinions.

Key Terms
القصاص (al-qisas): Retaliation in kind for murder or wounding
الشبهة (al-shubha): Doubt or semblance of right that prevents imposition of hadd or qisas

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Hanafis, why are witnesses not subject to qisas after retracting in a qisas case?
A) Because they did not directly kill
B) Because there is shubha and the causal link is weak
C) Because the judge is responsible
D) Because the victim's family can still forgive

Key Takeaway
Shubha averts qisas but not diyah; witnesses who cause an execution through retracted testimony are only financially liable in the Hanafi school.

Liability of Retracting Witnesses in Pardon Cases
Ruling on witness liability after retraction in pardon cases

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the liability rules for witnesses who retract after testifying about a pardon for murder or wound, and apply them to different scenarios.

Core Idea
Retracting witnesses pay full compensation if their testimony caused a financial loss after judgment.

When witnesses testify to a pardon in a murder or wound case, and then retract, the question arises: who bears the loss? This lesson examines the Hanafi ruling that witnesses must compensate from their own wealth, including payment periods and inheritance consequences.

Guided Path
1
Identify the original testimony
The witnesses testified that the victim's family pardoned the offender for blood money (diyah) or wound compensation (arsh). This testimony, if accepted, would relieve the offender of liability.
The pardon is related to 'blood involving property' meaning a case where financial compensation is due.
2
Recognize the retraction after judgment
After the judge issues a ruling based on their testimony, the witnesses retract. This retraction makes their initial testimony false, and the financial loss that occurred (the offender's release from liability) must be compensated.
Hanafi law distinguishes between retraction before and after judgment; only after judgment triggers full liability.
3
Determine the amount of compensation
For murder (even if pardon for intentional murder), the witnesses must pay full diyah (blood money). For intentional wound involving property, they pay the full arsh (wound compensation). For accidental murder or wound, they pay the proportional amount (e.g., half for a hand).
The text cites al-Bada'i' for accidental cases.
4
Apply payment terms and inheritance rules
The compensation is paid over three years for murder cases and one year for wound cases. The witnesses pay from their own wealth. They are not required to perform expiation (kaffarah), and they are not excluded from inheriting from the deceased (if they are heirs).
This is from al-Siraj al-Wahhaj in the text.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
شهدا على العفو عن دم فيه مال أو جرح عمد فيه مال ثم رجعا ضمنا الدية وأرش الجراحة في ثلاث سنين أو سنة .اهـ. وفي البدائع : شهدا بالقتل خطأ ثم رجعا ضمنا الدية في مالهما، وكذا إذا شهدا بقطع يد خطأ ضمنا نصفها وكذا إذا شهدا بسرقة فقطع ثم رجعا اهـ. وفي السراج الوهاج أن الدية التي على الشاهدين تكون في مالهما في ثلاث سنين ولا كفارة عليهما ولا يحرمان الميراث بأن كانا ولدي المشهود عليه فإنهما يرثانه اهـ
They testified to a pardon for a murder involving property or an intentional wound involving property, then they retracted: they guarantee the blood money and the compensation for the wound in three years or one year... It is finished. And in al-Bada'i: They testified to accidental murder then retracted: they guarantee the blood money from their own wealth. Likewise if they testified to accidental cutting of a hand, they guarantee half of it. Likewise if they testified to theft and [the hand] was cut, then retracted... It is finished. And in al-Siraj al-Wahhaj: The blood money that is upon the two witnesses is from their wealth in three years, and there is no expiation upon them, and they are not prevented from inheritance such that if they were sons of the person testified against, they inherit from him. It is finished.
Source pages p. 232

Commentary
This passage presents rulings from the Hanafi school on the liability of witnesses who retract after testifying in cases involving blood money. The key principle is that when witnesses retract, they must compensate the loss they caused. The text first states that if two witnesses testify to a pardon in a murder case (where the victim's heirs had a right to blood money) or a wound case involving property, then retract, they guarantee the full blood money (diyah) for murder or the proportional compensation (arsh) for wounds. The payment is spread over three years for murder and one year for wounds. Then it quotes al-Bada'i' adding that if witnesses testify to accidental murder (qatl khata') and then retract, they guarantee the blood money from their own wealth. Similarly for accidental cutting of a hand, they guarantee half the blood money. For theft leading to amputation, they retract and guarantee the value. Finally, al-Siraj al-Wahhaj clarifies that the blood money is paid over three years from the witnesses' own wealth, no expiation is required, and they are not disinherited even if they are heirs of the testifier. This is a ruling statement without explicit proof but based on the established principle that witnesses are liable for the consequences of their testimony.

Key Terms
شهود (shuhūd): Witnesses who testify in court; here they retract after testifying about a pardon.
رجوع عن الشهادة (rujū' 'an al-shahādah): Retraction of testimony after the court has passed judgment; triggers liability.
دية (diyah): Blood money paid as compensation for homicide or injury; in this passage, the amount due when witnesses retract after testifying about a pardon for murder.
أرش (arsh): Compensation for wounds or injuries; for intentional wounds, the arsh is proportionally calculated.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) They are not liable because the pardon was valid.
B) They guarantee the full blood money (diyah) in three years.
C) They must pay half the blood money for accidental murder.
D) They are disinherited if they are heirs of the deceased.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi fiqh, witnesses who retract after their testimony about a pardon has been accepted in judgment must compensate the full financial loss from their own wealth, over three years for murder and one year for wounds, without being disinherited or required to perform expiation.

Liability of Retracting Subordinate Witnesses: Intra-Hanafi Dispute
Intra-Hanafi dispute on liability apportionment among multiple retracting subordinate witnesses.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the intra-Hanafi dispute between Abu Yusuf and Muhammad regarding liability distribution among retracting subordinate witnesses and state the mufta bihi position.

Core Idea
Liability of retracting subordinate witnesses is divided proportionally to the number of original witnesses they represent, not equally.

This passage delves into a nuanced intra-Hanafi dispute on how to apportion liability when multiple subordinate witnesses retract after a judgment. The dispute centers on whether liability should be proportional to the weight of testimony (number of original witnesses) or equal among testifying groups. The passage also highlights the tension between qiyas and istihsan in deriving the final ruling, with the preferred position being the istihsan-based proportional division.

Guided Path
1
Identify the General Principle
Start by understanding the basic rule: subordinate witnesses are liable for the loss caused by their testimony because the court relied on it. This is the foundation for all subsequent calculations.
This principle is stated at the beginning: 'because the testimony was given in the court session, so the loss is attributed to them.'
2
Analyze the First Scenario
Consider the case from al-Muhit: two groups, one representing four original witnesses, the other representing two. Note the difference between Abu Yusuf (proportional) and Muhammad (equal). Identify each scholar's reasoning.
Abu Yusuf divides two-thirds to the group of four and one-third to the group of two. Muhammad says half each.
3
Examine Complex Scenarios from al-Jami'
Work through the intricate examples in al-Jami', where the amount claimed per original witness varies. Observe how the liability fractions (e.g., three-eighths) are derived.
These calculations reflect the istihsan approach, which considers the exact number of original witnesses represented.
4
Contrast Qiyas and Istihsan
Understand the methodological difference: qiyas (as in al-Mabsut) leads to equal division when the number of testifying subordinates is equal, while istihsan leads to proportional division based on original witness count.
The text states: what is in al-Mabsut is the answer based on qiyas, and what is in al-Jami' is the answer based on istihsan.
5
Determine the Mufta Bihi
Conclude which position is relied upon in fatwa. The text indicates the istihsan-based answer is considered the most correct (al-ashah).
This tarjih is supported by later Hanafi authorities such as the author of al-Bahr al-Raiq.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : (وإن رجع شهود الفرع ضمنوا لأن الشهادة في مجلس القضاء صدرت منهم فكان التلف مضافاً إليهم. وفي المحيط : شهدا على شهادة أربعة وآخران على شهادة شاهدين وقضى ثم رجعوا فعلى شاهدي الأربعة ثلثا الضمان وعلى الآخرين الثلث عند أبي يوسف. وقال محمد: على الفريقين نصفان. الجامع : شهدا على شهادة شاهدين لرجل على آخر بألف وشهد آخران على شهادة واحد عليه بألف فقضى بشهادتهم ثم رجع أحد اللذين شهدا على شهادة الشاهدين وأحد اللذين شهدا على شهادة واحد فعليهما ثلاثة أثمان الحق ثمنان على الأول وثمن على الآخر، ولو لم يرجع إلا واحد من الفريق الأول ضمن الربع ، ولو رجع بعد هذا الفريق الآخر كلهم ضمنا ربعاً آخر، ولو شهد كل فريق على شهادة شاهدين ورجع واحد من هذا وواحد من ذلك ضمنا ثمنين ونصفاً. وذكر في المبسوط النصف، وعن الكرخي يضمنان الربع، وعن عيسى بن أبان الثلث، والأصح أن المذكور في المبسوط جواب القياس، والمذكور في الجامع جواب الاستحسان اهـ.
His saying: (And if the subordinate witnesses retract, they guarantee) because the testimony was given in the court session, so the loss is attributed to them. In al-Muhit: Two testified to the testimony of four, and another two to the testimony of two witnesses, and judgment was passed, then they retracted: upon the two of the four is two-thirds of the liability, and upon the other two is one-third according to Abu Yusuf. And Muhammad said: upon the two groups is half each. In al-Jami': Two testified to the testimony of two witnesses for a man against another for a thousand, and another two testified to the testimony of one witness against him for a thousand, then judgment was passed based on their testimony, then one of those who testified to the testimony of the two witnesses and one of those who testified to the testimony of one retracted: upon them is three-eighths of the right: two-eighths upon the first and one-eighth upon the other. And if only one from the first group retracted, he guarantees one quarter. And if after this the other group all retracted, they guarantee another quarter. And if each group testified to the testimony of two witnesses, and one from this and one from that retracted, they guarantee two and a half eighths. And in al-Mabsut it is mentioned as one half, and from al-Karkhi they guarantee one quarter, and from Isa ibn Aban one third, and the most correct is that what is mentioned in al-Mabsut is the answer based on qiyas, and what is mentioned in al-Jami' is the answer based on istihsan. It is finished.
Source pages p. 232

Commentary
This passage discusses the liability of subordinate witnesses (shuhud al-far') who retract after judgment. The principle is that since they gave testimony in court, they are directly responsible for the loss. The text then provides detailed scenarios of multiple subordinate witnesses representing different numbers of original witnesses. In a case where two groups testify on behalf of four and two original witnesses respectively, Abu Yusuf holds that the liability is divided as two-thirds for the first group and one-third for the second, because each group's share corresponds to the number of original witnesses they represent. Muhammad holds that both groups share equally because they are equal in number (two each). The text then gives more complex examples from al-Jami' involving different amounts claimed. Finally, it contrasts the rulings based on qiyas (analogy) and istihsan (juristic preference). The opinion in al-Mabsut (half liability for one retractor from each group) is based on qiyas, while the more detailed calculation in al-Jami' (three-eighths, etc.) is based on istihsan, which is considered the more correct position.

Key Terms
شهود الفرع (shuhūd al-far'): Subordinate witnesses who testify on behalf of original witnesses, i.e., they bear witness to the testimony of others.
القياس (al-qiyās): Analogical reasoning used to derive a ruling for a new case from an existing case due to a common effective cause.
الاستحسان (al-istiḥsān): Juristic preference that sets aside the obvious analogy in favor of a more equitable ruling based on specific evidence or public interest.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In the scenario where two subordinate witnesses testify on behalf of four original witnesses and another two on behalf of two, what is Abu Yusuf's ruling on liability distribution?
A) Half and half
B) Two-thirds and one-third
C) All four are jointly liable
D) Only the first group is liable

Key Takeaway
The preferred Hanafi position divides retracting subordinate witnesses' liability proportionally to the number of original witnesses they represent, based on istihsan rather than qiyas.
