Liability of Original Witnesses When They Deny Appointment or Claim Mistake — Intra-Hanafi Dispute
Intra-Hanafi dispute on liability of original witnesses after judgment

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi majority position (Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf) regarding original witnesses' liability when they deny appointing subordinates after judgment, and explain the reasoning of the opposing view (Muhammad).

Core Idea
Original witnesses are not liable for a judgment based on subordinates' testimony, because the judge decided on what he perceived.

This lesson examines an intra-Hanafi dispute concerning the liability of original witnesses who deny having appointed subordinate witnesses, or claim mistake, after judgment has been passed. The majority view (Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf) holds them not liable, while Muhammad al-Shaybani argues for liability. We will analyze the reasoning behind each view and the practical consequences.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scenario and the dispute
The scenario: original witnesses deny appointment or claim mistake after judgment. The dispute: Are they liable for damages?
2
State the majority position (Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf)
They say no liability. Why? Because the judgment was based on the subordinates' testimony, not the originals'.
3
Examine Muhammad's position
He says they are liable, arguing that the subordinates transmit the originals' testimony, so it is as if the originals testified.
4
Analyze the rebuttal
The majority responds that the judge judges based on what he perceives (the subordinates' testimony), not the originals'.
5
Determine the mufta bihi
The majority view (no liability) is the relied-upon position.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : (لا شهود الأصل بلم نشهد الفروع على شهادتنا أو أشهدناهم وغلطنا) أي لا ضمان عليهم فيهما؛ أما في الأولى فلأنهم أنكروا السبب وهو الإشهاد فلا يبطل القضاء لأنه خبر محتمل فصار كرجوع الشاهد بخلاف ما قبل القضاء، وأما في الثانية فهو قولهما. وقال محمد: يضمنون لأن الفروع نقلوا شهادة الأصول فصار كأنهم حضروا. ولهما أن القضاء وقع بشهادة الفروع لأن القاضي يقضي بما يعاين من الحجة وهي شهادتهم، وقدمنا أنهما لو شهدا بأنه من مستحقي هذا الوقف فقضى القاضي به بشهادتهما ثم رجعا لا يضمنان شيئاً للمشهود عليهم من الغلة فيما يستقبل لأنهما لم يتلفاها عليهم لعدم وجودها وقتئذ حتى لو كان شيء من الغلة موجوداً وقت الشهادة وحكم به يضمنان بالرجوع ما أخذه الشهود له أو استهلك المشهود عليهم غلة السنين الماضية وحكم عليهم له بها، فكذلك يضمنانها لأنهما أتلفاه على المشهود عليهم بشهادتهما كمسألة الشهادة بعد موت المولى هنا ولم أر من صرح بذلك وقد سئلت عنه فاستخرجت الجواب من مسألة البدائع المذكورة فتأمل ذلك الخ.
His saying: (Not the original witnesses [are liable] when the subordinate [say] 'we did not testify to our testimony' or 'we appointed them and made a mistake') i.e., there is no liability upon them in both cases. As for the first, because they denied the cause which is the appointment, so the judgment is not invalidated because it is a probable report, so it becomes like the retraction of a witness, unlike before judgment. As for the second, it is his saying [i.e., Abu Hanifa's]. And Muhammad said: They guarantee because the subordinates transmitted the testimony of the originals, so it is as if they (the originals) were present. And for them (Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf) [the argument is] that the judgment occurred by the testimony of the subordinates because the judge judges based on what he perceives as evidence, namely their testimony. And we mentioned earlier that if they testify that someone is entitled to a certain waqf, and the judge passes judgment based on their testimony, then they retract, they do not guarantee anything to those against whom judgment was passed from future produce because they did not cause loss of it since it did not exist at that time. But if some produce existed at the time of testimony and judgment was passed, they guarantee by retraction what the witness took or what the defendants consumed from the produce of past years when judgment was passed against them for it. Thus they guarantee it because they caused loss to the defendants through their testimony, like the case of testimony after the death of the master here. I have not seen anyone explicitly stating this, and I was asked about it, so I extracted the answer from the mentioned case in al-Bada'i', so contemplate that.
Source pages p. 232

Commentary
This passage addresses the situation where the original witnesses (usul) deny that they ever appointed the subordinate witnesses (fur') or claim that they made a mistake in doing so. The ruling is that they are not liable for any damages. The reasoning is that the judgment was based on the testimony of the subordinates, not the originals. When the originals deny the appointment, it is considered a probable report (khabar muhtamal) that does not invalidate the judgment, similar to a witness retracting after judgment but unlike retraction before judgment. Muhammad holds the opposite view: he argues that since the subordinates transmitted the testimony of the originals, it is as if the originals themselves testified, so they should be liable. The majority (Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf) respond that the judge passes judgment based on the evidence before him, which is the subordinates' testimony, not the originals'. The passage then extends the discussion to a case of waqf: if witnesses testify that someone is entitled to waqf revenues, and judgment is passed, then they retract, they are not liable for future produce because it did not exist at the time of testimony; but they are liable for past produce that was consumed or taken. This is analogous to the case of witnesses retracting after the death of the master. The author notes that he derived this answer from a case in al-Bada'i'.

Key Terms
شهود الأصل (shuhūd al-aṣl): Original witnesses who have firsthand knowledge and may appoint subordinates to testify on their behalf.
إشهاد (ishhād): The act of appointing someone to testify on one's behalf.
خبر محتمل (khabar muḥtamal): A report that is ambiguous or probable, not certain; such a report does not invalidate an already passed judgment.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the majority Hanafi view (Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf), if original witnesses deny having appointed subordinates after judgment has been passed, what is the ruling?
A) They are liable for damages because they appointed the subordinates.
B) They are not liable because judgment was based on subordinates' testimony.
C) They are liable only if the subordinates confirm the appointment.
D) The judgment becomes invalid.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi majority holds that original witnesses are not liable for judgments based on subordinate testimony, because the judge acts on the evidence before him.

Retraction After Waqf Testimony: Liability for Past vs Future Produce
Hanafi ruling on witness retraction in waqf produce cases

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi rule regarding witness retraction in waqf cases to distinguish between liability for past and future produce, and explain the reasoning based on causation of loss (itlaf).

Core Idea
Witnesses are liable for produce consumed before retraction but not for future produce, because they caused loss of existing property.

This lesson extends the discussion of witness liability to a specific case involving waqf revenues. If witnesses testify that a person is entitled to waqf produce, and the judgment is passed, then later retract, the ruling distinguishes between produce that existed at the time of testimony and produce that came afterwards. We will analyze the reasoning behind this distinction and its practical implications.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scenario
Witnesses testify that someone is entitled to waqf revenues. Judgment is passed. Later, the witnesses retract.
2
Distinguish between future and past produce
Future produce: witnesses are not liable because it didn't exist at the time of testimony. Past produce: witnesses are liable if the produce was consumed or taken.
3
Understand the rationale
Liability is based on causing loss (itlaf). If produce existed and was consumed due to the testimony, the witnesses caused the loss.
4
Connect to the earlier case
This is analogous to the case of witnesses testifying after the master's death, where liability also depends on the existence of property at the time of testimony.
5
Derive the legal principle
The principle: witnesses are liable for the value of property that existed at the time of their testimony if it was consumed as a result of the judgment.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : (لا شهود الأصل بلم نشهد الفروع على شهادتنا أو أشهدناهم وغلطنا) أي لا ضمان عليهم فيهما؛ أما في الأولى فلأنهم أنكروا السبب وهو الإشهاد فلا يبطل القضاء لأنه خبر محتمل فصار كرجوع الشاهد بخلاف ما قبل القضاء، وأما في الثانية فهو قولهما. وقال محمد: يضمنون لأن الفروع نقلوا شهادة الأصول فصار كأنهم حضروا. ولهما أن القضاء وقع بشهادة الفروع لأن القاضي يقضي بما يعاين من الحجة وهي شهادتهم، وقدمنا أنهما لو شهدا بأنه من مستحقي هذا الوقف فقضى القاضي به بشهادتهما ثم رجعا لا يضمنان شيئاً للمشهود عليهم من الغلة فيما يستقبل لأنهما لم يتلفاها عليهم لعدم وجودها وقتئذ حتى لو كان شيء من الغلة موجوداً وقت الشهادة وحكم به يضمنان بالرجوع ما أخذه الشهود له أو استهلك المشهود عليهم غلة السنين الماضية وحكم عليهم له بها، فكذلك يضمنانها لأنهما أتلفاه على المشهود عليهم بشهادتهما كمسألة الشهادة بعد موت المولى هنا ولم أر من صرح بذلك وقد سئلت عنه فاستخرجت الجواب من مسألة البدائع المذكورة فتأمل ذلك الخ.
His saying: (Not the original witnesses [are liable] when the subordinate [say] 'we did not testify to our testimony' or 'we appointed them and made a mistake') i.e., there is no liability upon them in both cases. As for the first, because they denied the cause which is the appointment, so the judgment is not invalidated because it is a probable report, so it becomes like the retraction of a witness, unlike before judgment. As for the second, it is his saying [i.e., Abu Hanifa's]. And for them (Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf) [the argument is] that the judgment occurred by the testimony of the subordinates because the judge judges based on what he perceives as evidence, namely their testimony. I have not seen anyone explicitly stating this, and I was asked about it, so I extracted the answer from the mentioned case in al-Bada'i', so contemplate that.
Source pages p. 232

Commentary
This passage addresses the situation where the original witnesses (usul) deny that they ever appointed the subordinate witnesses (fur') or claim that they made a mistake in doing so. The ruling is that they are not liable for any damages. The reasoning is that the judgment was based on the testimony of the subordinates, not the originals. Key Terms
غلة (ghalla): Produce or revenue, often from waqf land.
إتلاف (itlāf): Causing loss or destruction of property.

In the waqf case discussed in the passage, when are witnesses liable for produce after retraction?
A) Only for future produce.

Key Takeaway
Witnesses are liable for existing property they caused to be consumed through their testimony, but not for property that came into existence afterward.

Both Original and Subordinate Retract: Liability
Ruling when both original and subordinate witnesses retract: only subordinates are liable

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on liability when both original and subordinate witnesses retract, and distinguish the positions of Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf from that of Muhammad.

Core Idea
When both original and subordinate witnesses retract, only the subordinates are liable according to the majority Hanafi position.

This lesson examines a specific scenario in testimony where both layers of witnesses (originals and subordinates) retract after a judgment has been passed. The key question is: who bears the financial liability? The Hanafi school has a majority view and a dissenting opinion within. Understanding this illustrates how liability attaches to the one who actually testified in court.

Guided Path
1
Identify the parties involved
Recognize the two types of witnesses: al-uṣūl (originals) who have firsthand knowledge and appoint others, and al-furū‘ (subordinates) who testify on their behalf.
These terms are standard in Hanafi testimony law.
2
State the scenario
Both the original and subordinate witnesses retract their testimony after the court has issued a judgment based on that testimony.
3
Determine the majority view
According to Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf, only the subordinates are liable because the judgment was based on their testimony directly. The originals did not testify in court, so they are not liable.
This is the Zahir al-Riwayah position.
4
Note the intra-Hanafi difference
Imam Muhammad holds that the plaintiff (mashhud lahu) may choose to claim compensation from either the originals or the subordinates.
Muhammad considers the originals as having effectively testified through the subordinates.
5
Apply the principle
The key principle: liability follows the one who actually presented the testimony in court. This determines the practical ruling for fatwa.
The mufta bihi is the majority view.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : (ولو رجع الأصول والفروع ضمن الفروع فقط) أي لا الأصول عندهما لأن القضاء وقع بشهادتهم، وعند محمد المشهور عليه بالخيار إن شاء ضمن الأصول وإن شاء ضمن الفروع
His saying: (And if the originals and subordinates retract, the subordinates alone guarantee) i.e., not the originals according to the two (Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf) because the judgment occurred by their testimony. And according to Muhammad, the plaintiff has the choice: if he wishes he guarantees the originals, and if he wishes he guarantees the subordinates.
Source pages p. 233

Commentary
This short passage clarifies the liability when both the original witnesses (usul) and the subordinate witnesses (fur') retract. According to Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf, only the subordinates are liable because the court's judgment was based on their testimony. The originals did not testify directly, so they are not liable. Muhammad holds a different view: the plaintiff (mashhud lahu) may choose to seek compensation from either the originals or the subordinates. This is consistent with Muhammad's earlier position that the originals are considered as having testified through the subordinates. The text uses 'c.indahuma' (according to the two) to refer to Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf, indicating that their view is the majority position.

Key Terms
الأصول (al-uṣūl): The original witnesses who have firsthand knowledge and appointed subordinates to testify.
الفروع (al-furū'): The subordinate witnesses who testify on behalf of the originals.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If both original and subordinate witnesses retract after judgment, what is the ruling according to Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf?
A) Both are jointly liable.
B) Only the original witnesses are liable.
C) Only the subordinate witnesses are liable.
D) The plaintiff can choose whom to claim from.

Key Takeaway
The liability for retraction falls on the witnesses who actually testified in court, not on those who appointed them.

Subordinate Witnesses Claiming Original Lied: No Liability
Court disregards subordinates' claim that originals lied or erred

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi rule that subordinate witnesses are not liable when they claim the originals lied or erred, by distinguishing between retracting one's own testimony and testifying against others.

Core Idea
A witness who does not retract their own testimony is not liable, even if they accuse others of lying.

In Hanafi judicial procedure, the finality of a judgment is paramount. Once a judgment is executed based on testimony, it cannot be undone by subsequent statements unless those statements constitute a retraction of the very testimony on which the judgment rests. This lesson examines a specific scenario where subordinate witnesses later claim that the original witnesses lied or erred. The court ignores such statements because the subordinates did not retract their own testimony.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and the ruling
The act is subordinate witnesses claiming that the original witnesses (usul) lied or erred. The ruling is that the court pays no attention to this claim and imposes no liability on the subordinates.
2
Determine the legal basis
The basis is that the judgment has already been executed (imḍā' al-qaḍā). The subordinates' statements do not invalidate the judgment because they are not retracting their own testimony.
Key principle: finality of executed judgment.
3
Distinguish from retraction
If the subordinates had retracted the testimony they themselves gave, the situation would differ. Here, they only testified against others (the originals). Therefore, they are not liable.
The distinction is crucial: testifying against another vs. retracting one's own statement.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : (ولا يلتفت إلى قول الفروع كذب الأصول أو غلطوا لأن ما أمضى من القضاء لا ينتقض بقولهم فلا يجب الضمان عليهم لأنهم ما رجعوا عن شهادتهم إنما شهدوا على غيرهم بالرجوع
His saying: (And no attention is paid to the statement of the subordinates that the originals lied or erred) because what has been executed of the judgment is not invalidated by their statement, so liability is not obligatory upon them because they did not retract from their testimony; they only testified against others by retracting.
Source pages p. 233

Commentary
This passage clarifies that if the subordinate witnesses (fur') claim that the original witnesses (usul) lied or made a mistake, this statement is not accepted in court. The reason is that the judgment has already been passed and executed based on the subordinates' testimony. Their statement about the originals does not constitute a retraction of their own testimony; it is merely a testimony against others (the originals). Since they did not retract the testimony they gave, they are not liable for any damages. This ruling highlights the finality of judicial decisions: once judgment is passed, it cannot be overturned by subsequent statements that do not directly challenge the basis of the judgment.

Key Terms
إمضاء القضاء (imḍā' al-qaḍā): The execution of a judicial judgment; once executed, it cannot be overturned by later statements that do not constitute a direct retraction.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why are subordinate witnesses not liable when they claim the original witnesses lied?
A) Because the subordinates are minors.
B) Because they did not retract their own testimony; they only spoke about the originals.
C) Because the originals are always liable.
D) Because the court does not accept any statements after judgment.

Key Takeaway
Subordinate witnesses are not liable for accusing originals of lying because they did not retract their own testimony.

Liability of Character Witnesses Who Retract
Ruling on liability when character witnesses retract their attestation

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi position on liability of character witnesses (muzzakun) when they retract their tazkiya, and evaluate the disagreement between Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn.

Core Idea
A character witness who knowingly lies is liable for damages because tazkiya enables the judge's decision.

Character witnesses (muzzakun) are not the main witnesses in a case; they attest to the integrity of other witnesses. What happens if they later retract their attestation? This passage from al-Bahr al-Raiq explores the liability (daman) of these witnesses, focusing on an internal Hanafi disagreement between Abu Hanifa and his two disciples, Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani. The key lies in the legal character of tazkiya: is it merely praise, or does it function as a cause that enables the judge to act?

Guided Path
1
State the disputed issue
Identify the precise legal question: are character witnesses (muzzakun) liable for damages when they retract their tazkiya after the judge has already acted on it?
The dispute is within the Hanafi school between Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn.
2
Identify the two positions
Abu Hanifa holds that they are liable; the Sahibayn hold they are not liable. Understand each position's ruling.
The text explicitly attributes the liability view to Abu Hanifa and the non-liability view to the two.
3
Analyze the Sahibayn's proof
The Sahibayn analogize muzzakun to witnesses of ihsan (marital status), arguing that both merely provide a condition or praise, and such witnesses are not liable for the outcome.
This is a qiyas argument: comparing muzzakun to shuhud al-ihsan.
4
Analyze Abu Hanifa's counter-proof
Abu Hanifa distinguishes: tazkiya is not mere praise; it is the 'cause of the cause' (illat al-illa) because the judge relies on it to accept testimony. Without tazkiya, the judge would not act. This makes it unlike the condition of ihsan, which is purely external.
The distinction is based on the effective role of tazkiya in the judicial process.
5
Apply the dispute to a concrete scenario
Consider the case of zina witnesses: if muzzakun certify that the witnesses for zina are free and Muslim, but they are actually slaves or Zoroastrians, and stoning is carried out, then Abu Hanifa holds the muzzakun liable for the blood money. The Sahibayn hold the public treasury (Bayt al-Mal) pays.
This is the practical consequence (thamarah al-khilaf) of the disagreement.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله: (وضمن المزكون بالرجوع) أي عن التزكية وهذا عند أبي حنيفة. وقالا : لا يضمنون لأنهم أثنوا على الشهود فصاروا كشهود الإحصان وله أن التزكية إعمال الشهادة إذ القاضي لا يعمل بها إلا بالتزكية فصارت في معنى علة العلة بخلاف شهود الإحصان لأنهم شرط محضن والخلاف فيما إذا قالوا تعمدنا أو علمنا أنهم عبيد ومع ذلك زكيناهم، أما إذا قال المزكي أخطأت فيها فلا ضمان إجماعاً، وقيل الخلاف فيما إذا أخبر المزكون بالحرية بأن قالوا هم أحرار، أما إذا قالوا هم عدول فبانوا عبيداً لا يضمنون إجماعاً لأن العبد قد يكون عدلاً. وأطلق في ضمانهم فشمل الدية لو زكوا شهود الزنا فرجم فإذا الشهود عبيد أو مجوس فالدية على المزكين عنده، ومعناه إذا رجعوا عنها بأن قالوا علمنا أنهم عبيد ومع ذلك زكيناهم، أما إذا ثبتوا عليها وزعموا أنهم أحرار فلا ضمان عليهم ولا على الشهود ولا تحد الشهود حد القذف لأنهم قد قذفوا حياً وقد مات ولا يورث عنه وقالا الدية على بيت المال؛ كذا في السراج الوهاج
His saying: (And the character witnesses are liable when they retract) i.e., from the tazkiya, and this is according to Abu Hanifa. And the two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) said: They are not liable because they praised the witnesses, so they become like witnesses of ihsan (marital status). And for him (Abu Hanifa) [the argument is that] tazkiya is the implementation of testimony, because the judge does not act upon it except with tazkiya, so it becomes in the meaning of the cause of the cause, unlike witnesses of ihsan because they are a pure condition. And the disagreement is in the case where they say 'we did it intentionally' or 'we knew they were slaves and yet we declared them trustworthy'. As for if the character witness says 'I erred in that', there is no liability by consensus. And it is said the disagreement is when the character witnesses informed of freedom, i.e., they said 'they are free'. As for if they said 'they are righteous' and they turned out to be slaves, they do not guarantee by consensus because a slave can be righteous. And it is stated generally that their liability includes blood money if they certified witnesses for zina and stoning took place, and if the witnesses were slaves or Zoroastrians, then the blood money is upon the character witnesses according to him (Abu Hanifa), meaning if they retracted by saying 'we knew they were slaves and yet we certified them'. As for if they affirmed and claimed they were free, there is no liability upon them nor upon the witnesses, and the witnesses are not punished with the hadd of qadhf because they accused a living person and he has died, and it is not inherited. And the two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) said: the blood money is from the public treasury. Thus in al-Siraj al-Wahhaj.
Source pages p. 233

Commentary
This passage addresses the liability of character witnesses (muzzakun) who retract their attestation of a witness's integrity (tazkiya) after judgment has been passed. Abu Hanifa holds that they are liable for damages because tazkiya is the means by which testimony becomes effective; the judge only accepts testimony if the witnesses are deemed trustworthy. Therefore, tazkiya is considered the 'cause of the cause' (illat al-illa) of the loss. Abu Yusuf and Muhammad (the two) disagree, arguing that the muzzakun merely praised the witnesses, similar to witnesses of marital status (ihsan), who are not liable. The text specifies that the disagreement only arises when the muzzakun admit they knew the witnesses were unfit (e.g., slaves) yet still certified them. If they simply made an error, there is no liability by consensus. The passage extends this to a case of zina: if the muzzakun certified that the witnesses for zina were free Muslims, but they were actually slaves or Zoroastrians, then if stoning was carried out, Abu Hanifa holds the muzzakun liable for the blood money. The two (Sahibayn) hold that the blood money is from the public treasury (Bayt al-Mal).

Key Terms
المزكون (al-muzakkūn): Character witnesses who attest to the integrity and reliability of other witnesses (tazkiya).
التزكية (al-tazkiyah): The act of certifying a witness as trustworthy and reliable (adl).
شهود الإحصان (shuhūd al-iḥṣān): Witnesses who testify to the marital status of a person (whether he is muhsan for zina penalty).
علة العلة (illat al-illah): The cause of the cause; a secondary cause that leads to the effective cause of a ruling. Here, tazkiya is considered the illat al-illah for the loss caused by the witnesses' testimony.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Abu Hanifa, under what condition are character witnesses (muzzakun) liable when they retract?
A) If they simply made an error in their assessment.
B) If they admit they knew the witnesses were unfit but certified them anyway.
C) In all cases of retraction.
D) Only if the principal witnesses also retract.

Key Takeaway
Character witnesses are liable if they intentionally certify unfit witnesses; the distinction lies in whether their role is a mere condition or an enabling cause.

Liability of Witnesses to Conditional Oaths (Ta'liq)
Liability of witnesses to conditional oaths

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify which witnesses are liable when retracting testimony regarding conditional oaths of emancipation or divorce, and apply the Hanafi rule that liability falls on those who establish the direct cause.

Core Idea
In retraction cases, liability attaches to the witnesses who establish the direct cause of the loss, not merely the command.

This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq expands on the ruling of witnesses to oaths (shuhud al-yamin). It clarifies that those who testify to the conditional act (ta'liq) are liable for the resulting loss because they are witnesses to the cause. The commentary further distinguishes between witnesses to an order and witnesses to the actual divorce or emancipation, showing that liability is on the ones who directly prove the cause.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling's scope
The text states that witnesses of ta'liq (conditional oaths) are liable if they retract. Note that it includes both emancipation and divorce.
The ruling applies to any conditional act causing a loss.
2
Distinguish witnesses of cause vs. condition
The passage calls these witnesses 'shuhud al-'illah' (witnesses of the cause). Understand that the cause is the ta'liq itself, not just the command or condition.
Only those who establish the ta'liq are liable.
3
Analyze the Munyat al-Mufti scenario
Two sets of witnesses: one to the order, another to the divorce. The liability falls on the witnesses to the divorce because they established the cause (the actual talaq).
The order alone is not the cause of loss.
4
Extend to three sets of witnesses
If there are witnesses to the order, to the ta'liq, and to the condition, the liability is on the witnesses of ta'liq (the conditional act).
This reinforces that the ta'liq is the pivotal event.
5
Apply to emancipation case
Similarly, if witnesses testify that a master made emancipation conditional, and others that emancipation occurred, liability is on those who establish the emancipation.
The value of the slave is guaranteed.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : وشهود اليمين) أي وضمن شهود التعليق لأنهم شهود العلة إذ التلف يحصل بسببه وهو الإعتاق أو التطليق وهم أثبتوه أطلقه فشمل تعليق العتق والطلاق فيضمنون في الأول القيمة وفي الثاني نصف المهر إن كان قبل الدخول. وفي منية المفتي: شهدا أنه أمر امرأته أن تطلق نفسها وآخران أنها طلقت نفسها وذلك قبل الدخول ثم رجعوا فالضمان على شهود الطلاق لأنهما أثبتا السببب والتعويض شرط كونه سبباً، وعلى هذا إذا شهدوا أنه جعل عتق عبده بيد فلان وآخران أنه أعتقه ثم رجعوا ولو شهدا أنه أمره بالتعليق وآخران أن المأمور علق وآخران على وجود الشرط ثم رجعوا فالضمان على شهود التعليق ا هـ.
His saying: (And witnesses of the oath) i.e., the witnesses of ta'liq (conditional oath) are liable because they are witnesses of the cause, since the loss occurs by its means, i.e., emancipation or divorce, and they established it. He generalizes it, so it includes conditional emancipation and divorce. So they guarantee in the first case the value, and in the second case half the dower if it was before consummation. And in Munyat al-Mufti: Two testified that he ordered his wife to divorce herself, and another two that she divorced herself, and that was before consummation, then they retracted: the liability is upon the witnesses of divorce because they established the cause, and compensation is a condition for it being a cause. And based on this, if they testify that he made the emancipation of his slave in the hand of so-and-so, and another two that he emancipated him, then they retract... And if two testify that he ordered him to make a conditional oath, and another two that the one ordered made the conditional oath, and another two on the occurrence of the condition, then they retract: the liability is upon the witnesses of ta'liq. It is finished.
Source pages p. 233

Commentary
This passage discusses the liability of witnesses who testify to conditional oaths (ta'liq) that result in emancipation or divorce. The principle is that these witnesses are 'witnesses of the cause' (shuhud al-illa) because the loss (e.g., loss of the slave's value or payment of dower) occurs as a result of the ta'liq event. They are liable if they retract. The text specifies that for emancipation, they guarantee the value of the slave; for divorce, they guarantee half the dower if the divorce occurred before consummation. Then it quotes from Munyat al-Mufti a more complex scenario: if two witnesses testify that the husband ordered his wife to divorce herself, and another two testify that she did so, and then all retract, the liability falls on the witnesses who testified to the divorce (the second group) because they established the cause (the divorce itself). The first group only testified to the order. Similarly, if there are three sets of witnesses (order, ta'liq, and condition), the liability is on the witnesses of ta'liq (the conditional act). The passage emphasizes that the key is establishing the direct cause of the loss.

Key Terms
شهود التعليق (shuhūd al-ta'līq): Witnesses who testify to a conditional statement (such as 'if you do X, then my wife is divorced' or 'my slave is free') that triggers a legal consequence.
شهود العلة (shuhūd al-'illah): Witnesses to the cause or effective factor that leads to a legal result. Here, they testify to the ta'liq which is the cause of emancipation or divorce.
الضمان (al-ḍamān): Liability or guarantee to compensate for loss. In this context, the witnesses must pay the value or dower.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In the scenario from Munyat al-Mufti, if witnesses testify that a husband ordered his wife to divorce herself, and other witnesses testify that she did so, and then all retract, who is liable?
A) All witnesses are jointly liable.
B) Only the witnesses to the order are liable.
C) Only the witnesses to the divorce are liable.
D) No one is liable because the divorce was voluntary.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi law, liability for retracted testimony in conditional oaths falls on the witnesses who establish the direct cause (the ta'liq), not those who only testify to peripheral commands or conditions.

Witnesses to Ihsan: Condition vs Cause – Definitions from Usul al-Fiqh
Ruling on witness liability and usul definitions

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on witnesses to ihsan and explain why they are not liable, using the usul categories of shart, 'illa, sabab, and 'alama.

Core Idea
Witnesses to marital status are not liable because ihsan is a condition (shart), not a cause ('illa).

This passage from Al-Bahr al-Ra'iq clarifies a key point in Hanafi hudud: witnesses who testify to a person's marital status (ihsan) are not liable if they retract. Why? Because ihsan is merely a condition (shart), not an effective cause ('illa). The passage then defines the usul al-fiqh terms shart, 'illa, sabab, and 'alama, showing how precise legal terminology determines legal consequences.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling on witnesses to ihsan
The passage states that witnesses to ihsan are not liable (la daman 'alayhim). Understand this as the operative ruling.
2
Locate the rationale
The rationale is that ihsan is a sign ('alama) and not a condition (shart) in reality? After defining the terms, the passage concludes that ihsan is a condition according to the majority because the obligation of the hadd depends on it.
Note the nuance: initially said 'alama, then corrected to shart after precise definitions.
3
Define the four categories: shart, 'illa, sabab, 'alama
From the passage: shart is that upon which existence depends but is not effective in the ruling nor leads to it. 'Illa is effective in the ruling. Sabab leads to the ruling without being effective. 'Alama indicates the ruling without existence depending on it.
4
Apply the definitions to ihsan
Ihsan is a shart because the obligation of the hadd (stoning) depends on it, but it does not directly cause the penalty. The act of zina is the 'illa.
5
Derive the practical consequence
Because ihsan is a shart, witnesses to it are not liable. Witnesses to the cause (zina) are liable if they retract.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : (لا شهود (الإحصان أي لا ضمان عليهم لأنه علامة وليس بشرط حقيقة . ثم اعلم أن الشرط عند الأصوليين ما يتوقف عليه الوجود وليس بمؤثر في الحكم ولا مفض إليه والعلة المؤثرة في الحكم والسبب هو المفضي إلى الحكم بلا تأثير والعلامة ما دل على الحكم وليس الوجود متوقفاً عليه، وبهذا ظهر أن الإحصان شرط كما ذكره الأكثر لتوقف وجوب
His saying: (Not the witnesses of ihsan) i.e., there is no liability upon them because it (ihsan) is a sign and not a condition in reality. Then know that according to usul scholars, the condition (shart) is that upon which existence depends and it is not effective in the ruling nor does it lead to it. The cause ('illa) is that which is effective in the ruling. The cause (sabab) is that which leads to the ruling without being effective. And the sign ('alama) is that which indicates the ruling without existence depending on it. By this it is clear that ihsan is a condition, as the majority mentioned, because the obligation [of the hadd penalty] depends on it.
Source pages p. 233

Commentary
This passage establishes that witnesses to a person's marital status (ihsan) are not liable if they retract, because ihsan is merely a sign or condition, not a cause. The text then provides a summary of key usul al-fiqh definitions: a condition (shart) is something on which the existence of a ruling depends but which does not actively affect the ruling or lead directly to it; a cause ('illa) is what actively affects the ruling; a cause (sabab) is what leads to the ruling without being effective in the sense of 'illa; and a sign ('alama) indicates the ruling but existence does not depend on it. The passage concludes that ihsan is a condition (shart) because the obligation of the hadd penalty for zina depends on it. Therefore, witnesses to ihsan are not liable, unlike witnesses to the actual act of zina (shuhud al-zina) who are witnesses to the cause and thus liable if they retract.

Key Terms
شرط (shart): A condition upon which the existence of a ruling depends, but which does not itself affect the ruling or lead to it. For example, ihsan is a condition for the hadd of stoning.
علة ('illah): The effective cause that directly influences the ruling. For example, the act of zina is the 'illah for the hadd penalty.
سبب (sabab): A cause that leads to the ruling without being directly effective (like the 'illa). In this passage, sabab is something that leads to the ruling but without the active influence.
علامة ('alāmah): A sign that indicates the ruling but existence does not depend on it. For example, the call to prayer (adhan) is a sign of the time for prayer, but prayer does not depend on adhan.
إحصان (iḥṣān): Marital status of a person who is married and free; a condition for the hadd of stoning for zina.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to usul definitions in this lesson, what distinguishes a condition (shart) from a cause ('illa)?
A) A condition is effective in the ruling, while a cause is not.
B) A condition is what existence depends on, but it is not effective in the ruling; a cause is effective.
C) A condition leads to the ruling without being effective; a cause is a sign.
D) Both are the same.

Key Takeaway
Witnesses to a condition (shart) are not liable; witnesses to a cause ('illa) are liable – the legal category determines the ruling.

Liability of Original vs Sub-Witnesses Upon Retraction
Explains liability limited to sub-witnesses with intra-Hanafi dispute.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position on liability upon retraction of witnesses and explain the intra-Hanafi dispute between Sahibayn and Imam Muhammad.

Core Idea
Upon retraction, only sub-witnesses are liable because the judgment relied on their testimony, not the originals.

In Hanafi jurisprudence, when witnesses retract after a judgment, liability for damages may arise. A specific scenario involves original witnesses (usul) who directly saw the event and sub-witnesses (furu) who only testified to the originals' testimony. This lesson unpacks a disputed ruling: who bears the loss when both retract?

Guided Path
1
State the matn's ruling
Identify the explicit ruling: when both original and sub-witnesses retract, only the sub-witnesses are liable for damages.
The matn says: 'ولو رجع الأصول والفروع ضمن الفروع فقط'.
2
Recognize the two positions within the Hanafi school
According to Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf, only sub-witnesses are liable. Imam Muhammad holds that the plaintiff has an option to hold either the originals or the sub-witnesses liable.
The ikhtilaf is recorded in the sharh.
3
Understand the basis of the dispute
The difference stems from the nature of sub-witness testimony: for Sahibayn it is delegation and agency (إنابة وتوكيل), so sub-witnesses are agents; for Imam Muhammad it is a burden (تحميل), so originals remain principals.
This distinction determines who is considered the testifier.
4
Determine the mufta bihi and tarjih
The relied-upon position is that only sub-witnesses are liable (Sahibayn's view). This is the fatwa position.
Tarjih is based on the Zahir al-Riwayah.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الفروع فقط ولا يلتفت إلى قول الفروع كذب الأصول أو غلطوا الاختلاف مبني على أن الإشهاد على الشهادة إنابة وتوكيل عندهما، وعنده تحميل. وقوله «غلطنا» اتفاقي إذ لو قالوا رجعنا عنها فلا ضمان أيضاً عندهما، ولو قال لكان أولى برجوعهم ليشمل المسألتين وليفهم إنكار الإشهاد بالأولى قوله : (ولو رجع الأصول والفروع ضمن الفروع فقط) أي لا الأصول عندهما لأن القضاء وقع بشهادتهم، وعند محمد المشهور عليه بالخيار إن شاء ضمن الأصول وإن شاء ضمن الفروع قوله : (ولا يلتفت إلى قول الفروع كذب الأصول أو غلطوا لأن ما أمضى من القضاء لا ينتقض بقولهم فلا يجب الضمان عليهم لأنهم ما رجعوا عن شهادتهم إنما شهدوا على غيرهم بالرجوع
Only the branches [sub-witnesses] and no attention is paid to the statement of the branches that the roots [original witnesses] lied or erred. The difference is built on that giving testimony upon testimony is delegation and agency according to them [Abu Yusuf and Muhammad], and according to him [Abu Hanifa] it is a burden. And his statement 'they erred' is agreed upon, for if they said 'we retract it' there is also no liability according to them, and if they said it would be more appropriate of their retraction to include the two issues and to understand denial of giving testimony in the first place. He said: (And if the roots and branches retract, only the branches are liable) meaning not the roots according to them because the judgment occurred by their testimony. And according to Muhammad, the well-known view is that he has a choice: if he wants he may hold the roots liable and if he wants he may hold the branches liable. He said: (And no attention is paid to the statement of the branches that the roots lied or erred) because what has been executed of the judgment is not nullified by their statement, so liability is not obligatory upon them because they did not retract their testimony; they only testified against others about retraction.
Source pages p. 233

Commentary
This passage states the ruling on retraction by original witnesses (usul) and sub-witnesses (furu) in a testimony case. The matn says that only the sub-witnesses are liable. The commentator explains the basis of the dispute: according to Abu Hanifa, the original witnesses are the principals, and the sub-witnesses are mere carriers of testimony. According to the two disciples (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani), giving testimony upon testimony is a delegation and agency, so the sub-witnesses are agents. The difference affects liability upon retraction. The passage then clarifies that if the sub-witnesses say the originals 'erred' or 'lied', that does not make them liable because they are not retracting their own testimony. Imam Muhammad holds an option view: the plaintiff may choose to hold either the originals or the sub-witnesses liable. The relied-upon position (mufta bihi) is that only sub-witnesses are liable, as per the Sahibayn.

Key Terms
الأصول (al-usul): The original witnesses who directly witnessed the event giving rise to the claim.
الفروع (al-furu): Sub-witnesses who testify to the testimony of the original witnesses, not the event itself.
الإشهاد على الشهادة (al-ishhad ala al-shahada): Giving testimony upon testimony; when a person testifies that another person testified.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the relied-upon position in the Hanafi school, who is liable when both original and sub-witnesses retract?
A) Only the original witnesses
B) Only the sub-witnesses
C) Both original and sub-witnesses jointly
D) Neither; retraction nullifies judgment

Key Takeaway
Upon retraction of both original and sub-witnesses, the Hanafi mufta bihi holds only the sub-witnesses liable, as the judgment relied on their testimony.

Liability of Certifiers Upon Retraction: Abu Hanifa vs. Sahibayn
Intra-Hanafi dispute on liability of tazkiya witnesses upon retraction

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position on liability of muzzikun upon retraction and explain the legal reasoning behind Abu Hanifa's view and the Sahibayn's counterargument.

Core Idea
Tazkiya enables judgment, so certifiers are liable upon retraction, unlike mere praisers.

This passage addresses a classical intra-Hanafi dispute: when a person who certifies the credibility of witnesses (muzzikun) later retracts that certification, are they liable for any damages caused? Abu Hanifa argues yes, because certification is the legal cause enabling judgment; the Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) argue no, comparing it to mere praise. Understanding their reasoning sharpens your grasp of causality (ta'lil) in Hanafi fiqh.

Guided Path
1
Identify the disputed ruling
What is the legal question? The liability of muzzikun (those who certify witnesses) when they retract their certification, admitting they knew the witnesses were disqualified.
The dispute only applies when the certifier admits intentional falsehood; if they claim error, there is consensus of no liability.
2
State Abu Hanifa's position and proof
Abu Hanifa holds they are liable. His evidence: tazkiya is the implementation (i'mal) of testimony—without it the judge cannot act. Thus it is like the cause of the cause (illa al-illa).
The analogy: if the certifier causes the judgment by enabling the testimony, they should bear the loss if they falsely enabled it.
3
State the Sahibayn's position and proof
The Sahibayn hold they are not liable. Their analogy: tazkiya is mere praise, like witnesses who testify to a person's integrity (shuhud al-ihsan), which is a pure condition (shart mahd).
A condition does not cause the ruling; it merely enables it. Hence no liability.
4
Analyze the thamarah al-khilaf
What practical difference does this make? If the muzzikun retract admitting knowledge, under Abu Hanifa they must pay damages (e.g., blood money in a zina case); under the Sahibayn, no payment—the public treasury pays.
The mufta bihi (operative position) is Abu Hanifa's view.
5
Apply the distinction to a concrete scenario
Consider a zina case: if the muzzikun certify witnesses who are slaves or Magians, and the accused is stoned, then upon retraction the blood money is on the certifiers according to Abu Hanifa, but on the public treasury according to the Sahibayn.
This shows the real-world impact of the ikhtilaf.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وضمن المزكون بالرجوع) أي عن التزكية وهذا عند أبي حنيفة. وقالا : لا يضمنون لأنهم أثنوا على الشهود فصاروا كشهود الإحصان وله أن التزكية إعمال الشهادة إذ القاضي لا يعمل بها إلا بالتزكية فصارت في معنى علة العلة بخلاف شهود الإحصان لأنهم شرط محض والخلاف فيما إذا قالوا تعمدنا أو علمنا أنهم عبيد ومع ذلك زكيناهم، أما إذا قال المزكي أخطأت فيها فلا ضمان إجماعاً، وقيل الخلاف فيما إذا أخبر المزكون بالحرية بأن قالوا هم أحرار، أما إذا قالوا هم عدول فبانوا عبيداً لا يضمنون إجماعاً لأن العبد قد يكون عدلاً. وأطلق في ضمانهم فشمل الدية لو زكوا شهود الزنا فرجم فإذا الشهود عبيد أو مجوس فالدية على المزكين عنده، ومعناه إذا رجعوا عنها بأن قالوا علمنا أنهم عبيد ومع ذلك زكيناهم، أما إذا ثبتوا عليها وزعموا أنهم أحرار فلا ضمان عليهم ولا على الشهود ولا تحد الشهود حد القذف لأنهم قد قذفوا حياً وقد مات ولا يورث عنه وقالا الدية على بيت المال؛ كذا في السراج الوهاج
And the certifiers are liable upon retraction, i.e., from certification. This is according to Abu Hanifa. And they two said: they are not liable because they praised the witnesses, so they become like witnesses of ihsan. And for him: certification is implementation of testimony since the judge does not act upon it except with certification, so it becomes in the meaning of cause of cause, unlike witnesses of ihsan because they are a pure condition. And the difference is when they say 'we intentionally did it' or 'we knew they were slaves and yet we certified them'. As for if the certifier says 'I erred in it', there is no liability by consensus. And it is said the difference is when the certifiers inform of freedom by saying 'they are free'. As for if they say 'they are upright' and they turn out to be slaves, they are not liable by consensus because a slave can be upright. And their liability is absolute, so it includes blood money if they certified witnesses of zina and then stoning occurred, and then the witnesses turn out to be slaves or Magians, then blood money is on the certifiers according to him. And its meaning is if they retract it by saying 'we knew they were slaves and yet we certified them'. As for if they confirm it and claim they are free, there is no liability on them nor on the witnesses, nor are the witnesses subject to hadd of qadhf because they accused a living person and he has died, and it is not inherited from him. And they two said: the blood money is on the public treasury. This is from al-Siraj al-Wahhaj.
Source pages p. 233

Commentary
This passage discusses the liability of those who certify the credibility of witnesses (muzzikun) upon retraction. According to Abu Hanifa, they are liable because certification enables the judge to act on the testimony, thus it is like a cause of the cause (illa al-illa). According to Abu Yusuf and Muhammad (Sahibayn), they are not liable because they merely praised the witnesses, analogous to witnesses of ihsan (which is a pure condition). The dispute applies only if they admit intentional false certification (e.g., knowing the witnesses were slaves but certifying them). If they simply claim error, they are not liable by consensus. The text also specifies that if they certify witnesses in a zina case leading to stoning, and the witnesses turn out to be slaves or Magians, the certifiers are liable for blood money according to Abu Hanifa, whereas the Sahibayn place the blood money on the public treasury. The operative ruling for fatwa is the position of Abu Hanifa (liability) when the certifiers admit knowing the truth.

Key Terms
المزكون (al-muzzikun): Those who certify the credibility (tazkiya) of witnesses before the judge.
التزكية (al-tazkiya): The act of certifying that a witness is upright and credible.
شهود الإحصان (shuhud al-ihsan): Witnesses who testify to a person's integrity and uprightness (ihsan).
علة العلة (illa al-illa): Cause of the cause; a secondary cause that directly enables the primary cause.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Whenever they retract, regardless of reason
B) Only if they admit they intentionally falsely certified knowing the witnesses were disqualified
C) Only if they claim they made an error
D) They are never liable

Key Takeaway
Tazkiya is a cause (illa) that enables judgment, so intentional false certification creates liability for damages under the mufta bihi view of Abu Hanifa.

Witness Liability and the Distinction between Cause, Condition, and Sign
Defines illa, sabab, shart, alamah and applies to liability of different witness types.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between illa, sabab, shart, and alamah in Hanafi usul, and apply the distinction to determine liability of witnesses upon retraction.

Core Idea
Only witnesses of the cause are liable upon retraction; witnesses of condition or sign are not.

This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq integrates usul definitions with fiqh application. The author first addresses witnesses of the oath (the cause), then witnesses of ihsan (sign/condition), and finally witnesses of a condition. The key is understanding the legal categories: the cause ('illa) directly produces the ruling, while a condition (shart) merely enables it, and a sign ('alamah) indicates it. This distinction determines who is liable when witnesses retract.

Guided Path
1
Identify the four concepts
From the passage, extract the definitions of 'illa (cause), sabab (reason), shart (condition), and 'alamah (sign). Note how each relates to the legal ruling.
The author quotes usul definitions: condition is that on which existence depends but has no effect; cause is the effective factor; reason leads without effect; sign indicates without dependence.
2
Understand the distinctions
Compare the four concepts in terms of causal efficacy. The illa directly produces the ruling; the shart is a prerequisite but not a cause; the sabab is a pathway without intrinsic effect; the 'alamah is a mere indicator.
Hanafi usul treats these as distinct categories with different legal consequences.
3
Apply to witness types
Map the witness categories: witnesses of the oath (shuhud al-yamin) are witnesses of the cause (illa) and are liable. Witnesses of ihsan are witnesses of a sign (or condition) and are not liable. Witnesses of a condition (shuhud al-shart) are also not liable according to the relied-upon position.
The passage provides examples: if witnesses testify to a conditional suspension of divorce, they are liable because they established the cause.
4
Note the intra-Hanafi dispute
Some Hanafi scholars (e.g., al-Bazdawi) hold witnesses of condition liable. The text explains that this is a forced position and the chosen view (mukhtar) is no liability, as stated in al-Ziyadat and preferred by al-Sarakhsi.
The dispute hinges on whether ihsan is a condition or a sign, and whether the condition itself can be analogized to a cause.
5
Determine the mufta bihi
The relied-upon fatwa position is that witnesses of a condition are not liable upon retraction. This is the view taken by the majority and supported by al-Ziyadat and al-Sarakhsi.
The passage concludes with an analogy: if a master says 'If so-and-so strikes you, you are free,' the striker is not liable because the emancipation is by the master's oath, not the strike.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : وشهود اليمين) أي وضمن شهود التعليق لأنهم شهود العلة إذ التلف يحصل بسببه وهو الإعتاق أو التطليق وهم أثبتوه أطلقه فشمل تعليق العتق والطلاق فيضمنون في الأول القيمة وفي الثاني نصف المهر إن كان قبل الدخول. وفي منية المفتي: شهدا أنه أمر امرأته أن تطلق نفسها وآخران أنها طلقت نفسها وذلك قبل الدخول ثم رجعوا فالضمان على شهود الطلاق لأنهما أثبتا السبب والتعويض شرط كونه سبباً، وعلى هذا إذا شهدوا أنه جعل عتق عبده بيد فلان وآخران أنه أعتقه ثم رجعوا ولو شهدا أنه أمره بالتعليق وآخران أن المأمور علق وآخران على وجود الشرط ثم رجعوا فالضمان على شهود التعليق ا هـ . قوله : (لا شهود الإحصان أي لا ضمان عليهم لأنه علامة وليس بشرط حقيقة . ثم اعلم أن الشرط عند الأصوليين ما يتوقف عليه الوجود وليس بمؤثر في الحكم ولا مفض إليه والعلة المؤثرة في الحكم والسبب هو المفضي إلى الحكم بلا تأثير والعلامة ما دل على الحكم وليس الوجود متوقفاً عليه، وبهذا ظهر أن الإحصان شرط كما ذكره الأكثر لتوقف وجوب الحد عليه بلا عقلية تأثير ولا إفضاء وعدم الضمان برجوع شهود الشرط هو المختار وإنما تكلف الإحصان علامة القائل بتضمين شهود الشرط وليس المختار؛ إليه أشار في التحرير . والحاصل أنهم اتفقوا على عدم تضمين شهود الإحصان فالقائل بأن شهود الشرط لا يضمنون بالرجوع لا إشكال على قوله والقائل بأنهم يضمنون تكلف وادعى أن الإحصان علامة وليس بشرط وظاهره أن المصنف قال به بدلیل عطف الشرط عليه، ولو اقتصر على نفي الضمان عن شهود الشرط كما في المجمع لكان أولى وصرح في البدائع بأنه شرط ولم يذكر غيره قوله : (والشرط) أي لا ضمان على شهود وجود الشرط للعتق والطلاق لما قدمنا أن اليمين هي العلة فأضيف الحكم إلى من أثبتها والشرط لا يعارض العلة. أطلقه فشمل ما إذا رجعوا وحدهم أو مع شهود العلة لكن عدم التضمين في الثاني اتفاق وفي الأول اختلاف، والمختار ما في الكتاب نص عليه في الزيادات واختاره السرخسي، واختار البزدوي ما قابله وأراد من الشرط ما ليس بعلة فشمل السبب فلا ضمان على شهود التفويض والضمان على شهود الإيقاع كما قدمناه واستشهد الحسامي على عدم تضمين شهود الشرط بما لو قال لعبده إن ضربك فلان فأنت حر فضربه فلان يعتق العبد ولا يضمن الضارب لأنه عتق بيمين مولاه لا بالضرب فكذلك هذا والله تعالى أعلم.
His statement: (And witnesses of the oath) meaning the witnesses of the conditional suspension are liable because they are witnesses of the cause, since the loss occurs by it, which is emancipation or divorce, and they established it. He made it general so it includes suspension of emancipation and divorce, so they are liable for value in the first and half the dower in the second if before consummation. And in Minyat al-Mufti: Two witnesses testified that he ordered his wife to divorce herself, and another two that she divorced herself, and that was before consummation, then they retracted; the liability is on the witnesses of the divorce because they established the cause, and compensation is a condition for it being a cause. And upon this, if they testified that he placed the emancipation of his slave in the hand of so-and-so and another two that he emancipated him, then they retracted. And if two testified that he ordered the suspension, and another two that the one ordered suspended, and another two on the existence of the condition, then they retracted, the liability is on the witnesses of the suspension. End. His statement: (Not the witnesses of ihsan) meaning no liability on them because it is a sign and not a condition in reality. Then know: The condition according to the legal theorists is that upon which existence depends, and it has no effect on the ruling nor leads to it. The cause is the effective factor in the ruling. The reason (sabab) is that which leads to the ruling without effect. The sign ('alamah) indicates the ruling without existence depending on it. With this it becomes clear that ihsan is a condition as most mentioned, because the obligation of the hadd penalty depends on it without causality or leading. And the absence of liability upon retraction of witnesses of condition is the chosen view. Indeed, the one who claims ihsan is a sign is the one who holds witnesses of condition liable, and this is not the chosen view; al-Tahrir pointed to it. The conclusion: They agreed on the absence of liability of witnesses of ihsan. So the one who says witnesses of condition are not liable upon retraction has no problem with his statement. The one who says they are liable makes a forced claim and alleges that ihsan is a sign and not a condition. It appears that the author (of Kanz) said it based on the evidence of conjoining the condition to it. If he had restricted to negating liability from witnesses of condition as in al-Majma', it would have been better. And al-Bada'i stated that it is a condition and did not mention other. His statement: (And the condition) meaning no liability on witnesses of the existence of the condition for emancipation and divorce because we have established that the oath is the cause, so the ruling is attributed to who established it, and the condition does not oppose the cause. He made it general so it includes if they retracted alone or with witnesses of the cause, but the absence of liability in the second is agreed upon, and in the first there is difference. The chosen is what is in the book, stated in al-Ziyadat and chosen by al-Sarakhsi. Al-Bazdawi chose the opposite. And he intended by 'condition' what is not a cause, so it includes the reason (sabab), so there is no liability on witnesses of delegation (tafwid) and liability on witnesses of execution (iqa'). As presented. And al-Hasami cited as evidence for the absence of liability of witnesses of condition: If a man says to his slave, 'If so-and-so strikes you, you are free,' then so-and-so strikes him, the slave becomes free, and the striker is not liable, because it is by the oath of his master, not by the strike. So likewise this. And Allah knows best.
Source pages p. 233

Commentary
This passage provides a detailed legal classification of witnesses based on the nature of what they testify to: the cause ('illa), the condition (shart), the reason (sabab), or the sign ('alamah). The author first addresses witnesses of the oath (shuhud al-yamin) — those who testify to a conditional suspension (ta'liq) of emancipation or divorce. These are considered witnesses of the cause because the loss (emancipation or divorce) is directly caused by their testimony. Therefore, if they retract, they are liable for the value (in case of emancipation) or half the dower (in case of divorce before consummation). Then the passage discusses witnesses of ihsan (shuhud al-ihsan) — the condition that a person must be previously married for the hadd of zina to apply. They are not liable because ihsan is a condition, not a cause. The commentator then gives a technical definition of condition, cause, reason, and sign from usul al-fiqh. The relied-upon position (mukhtar) is that witnesses of a condition (shuhud al-shart) are not liable upon retraction, because the condition is not the effective cause. There is a difference of opinion: some scholars hold them liable, but this is considered forced. The author cites al-Ziyadat and al-Sarakhsi for the chosen view. The passage ends with an analogy from al-Hasami to illustrate that the striker is not liable because the emancipation occurs by the master's oath, not by the strike; similarly, witnesses of a condition are not liable because the legal effect is attributed to the cause, not the condition.

Key Terms
العلة (al-illa): The effective cause that directly produces the legal ruling.
الشرط (al-shart): A condition upon which existence of the ruling depends but does not cause it.
السبب (al-sabab): A reason that leads to the ruling without having intrinsic causal effect.
العلامة (al-alamah): A sign that indicates the ruling but is not a cause or condition.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the relied-upon Hanafi position, who is liable upon retraction?
A) Witnesses of the cause (illa)
B) Witnesses of the condition (shart)
C) Witnesses of the sign (alamah)
D) All of the above

Key Takeaway
The liability of witnesses upon retraction depends strictly on whether they testified to the cause ('illa) or to a condition or sign; only witnesses of the cause are liable.

Non-Liability of Witnesses of Condition Upon Retraction
Explains preferred Hanafi view on non-liability of witnesses of condition.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi position on liability of witnesses of condition (shuhud al-shart) upon retraction and distinguish it from the opposing intra-Hanafi view.

Core Idea
The condition is not the cause; the oath is the cause, so witnesses of the condition are not liable upon retraction.

This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq examines an intra-Hanafi dispute about whether witnesses who testify to a condition (e.g., 'if you hit my slave, he is free') can be held liable when they later retract. The pivotal issue is the legal characterization of the condition: is it a cause ('illa) or merely a sign? The preferred Hanafi view, explained with a vivid analogy, holds that the condition does not create liability because the oath itself is the cause.

Guided Path
1
Identify the disputed issue and the two positions
Determine what is being disputed: the liability of witnesses of a condition upon retraction. Note the two positions: (1) no liability (mukhtar view of al-Sarakhsi and al-Hidayah) and (2) liability (al-Bazdawi).
The passage states that witnesses of the cause (shuhud al-'illa) are definitely not liable; the dispute is only about witnesses of the condition.
2
Extract the Hanafi proof: why the condition is not a cause
The text says 'the oath is the cause, so the ruling is attributed to those who proved it, and the condition does not oppose the cause.' Understand the causal relationship: the legal effect (e.g., emancipation) is caused by the oath, not by the condition. The condition is merely a trigger.
This is a form of talil (reasoning) distinguishing between 'illa and shart.
3
Examine the opposing argument and its basis
Al-Bazdawi holds liability, apparently considering the condition a sign that can itself cause the effect. The passage notes that this view 'burdens itself' by treating the condition as a cause.
The author implies that al-Bazdawi's view is weaker because it conflates condition with cause.
4
Analyze al-Husami's analogy
The passage cites an analogy: a master says to his slave, 'If so-and-so hits you, you are free.' When the hitter strikes, the slave is freed, but the hitter is not liable because freedom is caused by the oath, not the hitting. Similarly, witnesses of a condition testify to a trigger, not the cause.
This is a qiyas: the hitter corresponds to the witnesses of condition; both are not liable because they do not cause the legal effect.
5
Determine the mufta bihi and the practical difference
The preferred view (mukhtar) is non-liability, as stated in al-Ziyadat and chosen by al-Sarakhsi. The practical consequence: in court, if witnesses of a condition retract, they are not obligated to pay damages, whereas under al-Bazdawi's view they could be liable.
The author concludes that the ruling in the book (al-Hidayah) is the correct one, and al-Bazdawi's opinion is not chosen.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كتاب الشهادات باب الرجوع عن الشهادة الحد عليه بلا عقلية تأثير ولا إفضاء وعدم الضمان برجوع شهود الشرط هو المختار وإنما تكلف الإحصان علامة القائل بتضمين شهود الشرط وليس المختار؛ إليه أشار في التحرير . والحاصل أنهم اتفقوا على عدم تضمين شهود الإحصان فالقائل بأن شهود الشرط لا يضمنون بالرجوع لا إشكال على قوله والقائل بأنهم يضمنون تكلف وادعى أن الإحصان علامة وليس بشرط وظاهره أن المصنف قال به بدلیل عطف الشرط عليه، ولو اقتصر على نفي الضمان عن شهود الشرط كما في المجمع لكان أولى وصرح في البدائع بأنه شرط ولم يذكر غيره قوله : (والشرط) أي لا ضمان على شهود وجود الشرط للعتق والطلاق لما قدمنا أن اليمين هي العلة فأضيف الحكم إلى من أثبتها والشرط لا يعارض العلة. أطلقه فشمل ما إذا رجعوا وحدهم أو مع شهود العلة لكن عدم التضمين في الثاني اتفاق وفي الأول اختلاف، والمختار ما في الكتاب نص عليه في الزيادات واختاره السرخسي، واختار البزدوي ما قابله وأراد من الشرط ما ليس بعلة فشمل السبب فلا ضمان على شهود التفويض والضمان على شهود الإيقاع كما قدمناه واستشهد الحسامي على عدم تضمين شهود الشرط بما لو قال لعبده إن ضربك فلان فأنت حر فضربه فلان يعتق العبد ولا يضمن الضارب لأنه عتق بيمين مولاه لا بالضرب فكذلك هذا والله تعالى أعلم.
Book of Testimonies, Chapter on Retraction from Testimony. The hadd (punishment) is not effective without sanity, nor is there consequence, and the non-liability upon the retraction of witnesses of the condition is the chosen view. Rather, one who claims liability for witnesses of the condition burdens themselves by considering the condition a sign, not a condition, and that is not the chosen view; al-Tahrir alluded to it. The conclusion is that they agreed on non-liability of witnesses of the cause, so the one who says that witnesses of the condition are not liable upon retraction has no problem with his statement, while the one who says they are liable burdens themselves and claimed that the cause is a sign and not a condition. Commentary
This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq deals with an intra-Hanafi dispute concerning the liability of witnesses who testify to the existence of a condition (shart) in a conditional oath, such as 'if you hit my slave, he is free.' When these witnesses retract their testimony, should they be liable for damages? The author clarifies that the majority (including al-Sarakhsi) hold that they are not liable, because the effective cause ('illa) of the emancipation is the oath itself, not the condition. The condition merely triggers the oath's effect. Some scholars (like al-Bazdawi) argue otherwise, but the author maintains that the mukhtar (preferred view) is non-liability, citing the analogy of a master's oath freeing a slave upon being hit—the hitter is not liable. The passage also notes that witnesses of the cause ('illa) are definitely not liable; the dispute is only about witnesses of the condition.

Key Terms
شهود الشرط (shuhud al-shart): Witnesses who testify to the existence of a condition (e.g., 'if you hit my slave') rather than the direct cause of the legal effect.
شهود العلة (shuhud al-'illa): Witnesses who testify to the direct cause of a legal result (e.g., the actual hitting in a conditional freeing).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) They are liable for damages.
B) They are not liable because the oath is the cause.
C) They are liable only if they retract together with witnesses of the cause.
D) They are liable if the condition is considered a cause.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi law, witnesses of a condition (shart) are not liable upon retraction because the condition is not the cause; the oath is the cause, and liability attaches only to witnesses of the cause.

Agent's Oath When Principal is Dead: The Principle of Lack of Benefit
Sharah discussing the ruling on agent's oath when principal is dead, based on principle of lack of benefit.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling that an agent is not sworn regarding the principal's receipt and explain the rationale of lack of benefit.

Core Idea
An agent's oath is pointless if it does not bind the principal—Hanafi law avoids futile legal acts.

This passage from Al-Bahr al-Raiq discusses a specific rule: when an agent is not required to take an oath regarding the principal's receipt of payment, especially after the principal's death. The core principle is 'lack of benefit' – since the agent's confession would not bind the principal, his oath serves no purpose. Understanding this principle clarifies many Hanafi rulings on oaths in agency.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling
The text states 'there is no oath upon the agent regarding his lack of knowledge of the principal's receipt.' So the ruling is that the agent is not sworn.
2
Trace the proof
The proof from Jami' al-Fusulayn: 'If he confessed, it would not be binding upon his principal' – swearing him is futile.
3
Apply the analogy
The text provides an analogy: a father demanding his daughter's dowry; he is not sworn about consummation because his confession would not bind her.
4
Expand via Ar-Ramli
Ar-Ramli notes that the ruling in Jami' al-Fusulayn confines the exemption to the executor (wasī), but heirs should be sworn. This shows a nuance.
5
Conclude with the principle
The overarching principle is 'lack of benefit' (adam al-fā'idah). An unnecessary oath is not required.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : (أشار المؤلف إلى أنه لا يمين على الوكيل الخ) قال في جامع الفصولين: إذ لو أقر لم يجز على موكله لأنه على الغير، وكذا أب طالب زوج بنته البالغة بمهرها وقال ابنتي بكر في منزلي وقال الزوج بل دخلت بها ولم يبق لها حق القبض صدق الأب لتمسكه بالأصل والزوج يدعي العارض والزوج ينكر ولا يحلف الأب أنه لا يعلم بدخوله إذ لو أقر به لم يجز عليها لما مر .اهـ. قوله: (فلو كان رب المال ميتاً الخ) قال الرملي : مسألة جامع الفصولين قاصرة على دعوى الوصي ولم يذكر الدعوى على ورثته، ولا شك في تحليفهم على نفي العلم تأمل قوله : (لما مر من عدم الفائدة) أي مر في كلام جامع الفصولين حيث قال قبل هذا إذ لو أقر لم يجز على موكله لأنه على الغير كما قدمناه . قوله : (ولم يذكر حكم ما إذا نكل الطلب عن اليمين الخ قال الرملي : ولم يذكر هذا الشارح
His statement: (The author indicated that there is no oath upon the agent regarding his lack of knowledge of the principal's receipt [of payment]) – He said in Jami' al-Fusulayn: Because if he confessed, it would not be binding upon his principal, since it is [a confession] regarding another. Similarly, a father who demands the dowry of his adult daughter and says, 'My daughter is a virgin in my house,' and the husband says, 'Rather, I have consummated the marriage and she no longer has the right of receipt,' the father is believed because he adheres to the original state, and the husband claims a contingency, and the husband denies, and the father is not sworn that he does not know of consummation, because if he confessed to it, it would not be binding upon her, as previously mentioned. End. His statement: (If the owner of the money was dead, etc.) Ar-Ramli said: The issue in Jami' al-Fusulayn is confined to the claim of the executor, and he did not mention the claim against the heirs, and there is no doubt that they are sworn to deny knowledge. Ponder. His statement: (Due to the lack of benefit previously mentioned) – meaning what was mentioned in the speech of Jami' al-Fusulayn where he said before this: because if he confessed, it would not be binding upon his principal, as we have presented. His statement: (He did not mention the ruling when the claimant declines the oath, etc.) – Ar-Ramli said: This commentator did not mention it.
Source pages p. 315

Commentary
This passage is an expansion probe from the sharh of Kanz al-Daqa'iq, discussing the ruling that an agent cannot be sworn regarding lack of knowledge of the principal's receipt. The author quotes from Jami' al-Fusulayn to illustrate that if the agent confessed to something (like receiving payment), it would not be binding on the principal because the agent is a third party. An analogy is drawn with a father demanding his daughter's dowry: he is not sworn about lack of consummation because his confession would not bind her. The core reason is 'lack of benefit' — since the agent's confession would not be valid against the principal, his oath is also pointless. Ar-Ramli notes that the ruling in Jami' al-Fusulayn is limited to the executor (wasī) and does not mention heirs, but heirs should be sworn to deny knowledge. The passage concludes with a note that the commentator did not mention the case when the plaintiff declines the oath.

Key Terms
يمين الوكيل (yamīn al-wakīl): The oath taken by an agent regarding his lack of knowledge of the principal's actions.
عدم الفائدة (adam al-fā'idah): The legal principle that an act (like taking an oath) that yields no practical benefit is not required or permitted.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why is the agent not sworn regarding his knowledge of the principal's receipt of payment according to the Hanafi school?
A) Because the agent is not a party to the contract
B) Because if the agent confessed to receipt, it would not be binding on the principal
C) Because the principal is dead and cannot confirm
D) Because the agent is considered trustworthy

Key Takeaway
An agent is not sworn about the principal's affairs when the oath yields no legal benefit, as it would not bind the principal.
