General Rules for Identifying the Defendant in Property Claims
Defining the defendant in property claims

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the rules for determining the proper defendant in claims of absolute ownership, lease, mortgage, sharecropping, ghasb, and sale, and apply them to given scenarios.

Core Idea
The proper defendant varies by claim type and possession status.

This lesson covers the first set of rules from the Hanafi manual on who must be present as the defendant (khasm) when a third party claims ownership or related rights. It clarifies when the owner alone suffices and when both owner and possessor are required.

Guided Path
1
Identify the claim type
Classify the claim as absolute ownership, ghasb, sharecropping, pre-emption, etc.
2
Determine the possessor's role
Identify whether the possessor is a lessee, mortgagee, sharecropper, buyer, etc.
3
Apply the rule for absolute ownership
If claim is absolute ownership against a lessee or mortgagee, both owner and possessor must be present unless the claimant purchased from the owner before the lease.
Then the owner alone suffices.
4
Apply the rule for ghasb, sharecropping, and sale
For ghasb, owner's presence is not required. For sharecropping, presence depends on seed ownership or standing crop. In sale before delivery, both seller and buyer are needed for pre-emption.
For corrupt sale, after possession buyer is defendant; before, seller.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ولا بد من بيان من يكون خصماً في الدعوى ليعلم المدعى عليه، وقد أغفله الشارحون وهو مما لا ينبغي فأقول في دعوى الخارج ملكاً مطلقاً في عين في يد مستأجر أو مرتهن لا بد من حضرة المالك وذي اليد إلا إذا ادعى الشراء منه قبل الإجارة، فالمالك وحده يكون خصماً، وتشترط حضرة المزارع إن كان البذر منه أو كان الزرع نابتاً وإلا لا. وفي دعوى الغصب عليه لا تشترط حضرة المالك وفي البيع قبل التسليم لا بد في دعوى الاستحقاق والشفعة من حضرة البائع والمشتري والمشتري فاسداً بعد القبض خصم لمن يدعي الملك فيه، وقبل القبض الخصم هو البائع وحده وأحد الورثة ينتصب خصماً عن الكل، فالقضاء عليه قضاء على الكل وعلى الميت، وقيده في الجامع بكون الكل في يده وأن البعض في يده فبقدره والموصى له ليس بخصم في إثبات الدين إنما هو خصم في إثبات الوصاية أو الوكالة إلا إذا كان موصى له بما زاد على الثلث ولا وارث فهو كالوارث، واختلف المشايخ في إثبات الدين على من في يده مال الميت وليس بوارث ولا وصي ولا تسمع دعوى الدين على الميت على غريم الميت مديوناً أو دائناً. والخصم في إثبات النسب خمسة: الوارث، والوصي، والموصى له والغريم للميت أو على الميت وقف على صغير له وصي ولرجل فيه دعوى يدعيه على متولي الوقف لا على الوصي لأن الوصي لا يلي القبض، ولا تشترط حضرة الصبي عند الدعوى عليه وتكفي حضرة وصيه ديناً أو عيناً، باشره الوصي أو لا، ولا يشترط حضرة العبد والأمة عند دعوى المولى أرشه ومهرها، ولو ادعى على صبي محجور عليه استهلاكاً أو غصباً وقال لي بينة حاضرة تسمع دعواه وتشترط حضرة الصبي مع أبيه أو وصيه وإلا نصب القاضي له وصياً. وتشترط حضرته عند الدعوى مدعياً أو مدعى عليه، والصحيح أنه لا تشترط حضرة الأطفال الرضع عند الدعوى. والمستأجر خصم لمن يدعي الإجارة في غيبة المالك على الأقرب إلى الصواب وليس بخصم على الصحيح لمن يدعي الإجارة أو الرهن أو الشراء، والمشتري خصم للكل كالموهوب له وفي دعوى العين المرهونة تشترط حضرة الراهن والمرتهن وتصح الدعوى على الغاصب وإن لم تكن العين في يده فلذا كان للمستحق الدعوى على البائع وحده وإن كان المبيع في يد المشتري لكونه غاصباً، والمودع أو الغاصب إذا كان مقراً بالوديعة أو الغصب لا ينتصب خصماً للمشتري وينتصب لوارث المودع أو المغصوب منه ومن اشترى شيئاً بالخيار فادعاه آخر يشترط حضرة البائع والمشتري والمشتري باطلاً لا يكون خصماً للمستحق، وإذا استحق المبيع بالملك المطلق وقضى به فبرهن البائع على النتاج وبرهن على المشتري في غيبة المستحق ليدفع عنه الرجوع بالثمن اختلف المشايخ فيه والأصح أنه لا تشترط حضرته ومنهم من قال : المختار اشتراطها.
It is necessary to clarify who is the defendant in a claim so that the defendant is known. The commentators have neglected this, which is not appropriate. I say: In the claim of an outsider for absolute ownership of a property in the hand of a lessee or mortgagee, the presence of the owner and the possessor is necessary unless he claims purchase from him before the lease, then the owner alone is the defendant. The presence of the sharecropper is required if the seed was from him or the crop was growing; otherwise not. In a claim of usurpation (ghasb) against him, the presence of the owner is not required. In sale before delivery, in claims of right and pre-emption, the presence of the seller and buyer is necessary. The buyer in a corrupt sale after possession can be defendant for one claiming ownership; before possession, the defendant is solely the seller. One heir stands as defendant for all; judgment against him is judgment against all and against the deceased. This is restricted in al-Jami' to when all are in his hand, and if part is in his hand then to that extent. The legatee is not a defendant in proving a debt; he is defendant only in proving executorship or agency unless he was bequeathed more than one-third and there is no heir, then he is like an heir. The scholars differed regarding proving a debt against one who has the deceased's property but is not an heir, executor, or legatee. The claim of a debt against the deceased is not heard against the debtor of the deceased whether the deceased was a debtor or creditor. The defendant in proving lineage are five: the heir, the executor, the legatee, the creditor of the deceased, or debtor to the deceased. An endowment for a minor having an executor—a man with a claim in it claims against the endowment trustee (mutawalli), not the executor, because the executor does not take possession. The presence of the minor is not required when claiming against him; the presence of his executor suffices, whether the executor himself acts or not. The presence of a male slave or female slave is not required when the master claims their indemnity or dower. If one claims against a minor under interdiction for destruction or usurpation and says 'I have a present witness,' his claim is heard; the presence of the minor with his father or executor is required; otherwise, the judge appoints an executor for him. His presence is required whether he is plaintiff or defendant. The correct view is that the presence of nursing infants is not required in claims. The lessee is a defendant for one claiming the lease in the absence of the owner, according to the closer to correctness; but he is not a defendant in the correct view for one claiming the lease, pawn, or purchase. The buyer is a defendant for all, like the donee. In a claim of the pawned property, the presence of the pawner and pawnee is required. A claim against the usurper is valid even if the property is not in his hand; hence the rightful owner may claim against the seller alone even if the sold item is in the buyer's hand because the seller is a usurper. The depositary or usurper, if he admits the deposit or usurpation, does not stand as defendant for the buyer; but stands for the heir of the depositor or the person from whom it was usurped. If one buys with an option and another claims it, the presence of the seller and buyer is required. The buyer in a void sale is not a defendant for the rightful owner. If the sold item is claimed by absolute ownership and judgment is given, then the seller proves the offspring and the buyer proves in the absence of the rightful claimant to repel the recourse for the price—the scholars differed; the correct view is that his presence is not required; some said the chosen view is that it is required.
Source pages p. 331

Commentary
This passage provides a comprehensive list of who constitutes a proper defendant (khasm) in various types of claims, as derived from Hanafi fiqh. The author begins by stressing the importance of identifying the defendant—a point neglected by earlier commentators. He then enumerates rules: For a claim of ownership by an outsider against a lessee or mortgagee, both the owner and the possessor must be present unless the outsider claims to have purchased from the owner before the lease, in which case only the owner is the defendant. In sharecropping, the presence of the sharecropper is needed if he provided seed or the crop is standing. For claims of usurpation, the owner's presence is not required. In pre-emption and claims of right in a sale before delivery, the seller and buyer must both be present. A buyer in a corrupt sale after possession becomes the defendant for ownership claims, but before possession only the seller is defendant. One heir can represent all heirs; judgment against him applies to all and to the deceased, provided the heir holds all the property; if only part, his representation is limited to that part. The legatee is not a defendant for proving a debt but is for proving executorship or agency, unless the bequest exceeds one-third and there are no heirs, making him like an heir. Scholars differed on proving debts against a non-heir possessor of the deceased's property; the claim is not heard against the deceased's debtor. For proving lineage, five can be defendants: heir, executor, legatee, creditor, and debtor. For an endowment with a minor's executor, one must sue the mutawalli, not the executor. A minor's presence is not needed if his executor appears. Slaves need not appear when masters claim their damages or dower. If a minor under interdiction is sued for destruction or usurpation, he must appear with his father or executor, or the judge will appoint one. Infants are excepted. The lessee is a defendant for a lease claim but not for pawn or purchase claims. The buyer is a defendant for all claims, like a donee. In pawned property claims, both pawner and pawnee must appear. Claims against a usurper are valid even if he no longer possesses the item; the rightful owner can sue the seller alone if the seller is deemed a usurper. A depositary or usurper who admits is not a defendant for the buyer but is for the heir. For a sale with option, both seller and buyer must be present. A void buyer is not a defendant. If a sold item is claimed by absolute ownership and judgment is given, then the seller may prove offspring and the buyer may prove in the claimant's absence to avoid paying back the price; the correct view is that the claimant's presence is not required.

Key Terms
خصم (khasm): The party against whom a legal claim is brought; the defendant.
حضرة (hadrtah): The physical presence of a party in court at the time of claim.
المدعى عليه (al-mudda‘ā ‘alayh): The defendant, the person against whom a claim is made.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In a claim of absolute ownership against a mortgagee, who must be present as defendants?
A) Owner only
B) Mortgagee only
C) Both owner and mortgagee
D) Neither

Key Takeaway
The proper defendant in property claims depends on the nature of the claim and the possessor's relationship to the property.

Special Cases: Heirs, Legatees, Guardians, and Others as Defendants
Special rules for heirs, legatees, and others

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify who can serve as defendant in claims involving heirs, legatees, executors, minors, slaves, lessees, buyers, and pawners, and apply the rules to practical scenarios.

Core Idea
Representation and possession determine who is the proper defendant in special cases.

This lesson continues from the previous one, covering more complex scenarios involving multiple parties, representation, and fiduciary relationships. It explains when one heir can represent all, the role of a legatee, and the requirements for minors, slaves, lessees, and others.

Guided Path
1
Identify the special party
Determine if the case involves heirs, legatees, executors, minors, slaves, lessees, etc.
2
Determine representation
Check if one heir can represent all, or if a legatee represents only for executorship.
3
Apply presence requirements
For minors, presence of guardian suffices; for slaves, master's presence not required; for lessees, depends on claim type.
4
Note exceptions and disputes
Some cases have differing opinions among scholars; the mufta bihi is identified.

Sufficiency of Three Witnesses in Boundary Claims
Ruling on number of witnesses for boundary claims

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on the number of witnesses required for a boundary claim and identify the intra-Hanafi differences.

Core Idea
Three witnesses suffice for boundary claims because majority overcomes doubt, but Zufar and Abu Yusuf differ.

When a plaintiff claims a property with specific boundaries, the number of witnesses needed to prove the claim varies. The primary Hanafi position holds that three witnesses are sufficient because a majority overcomes uncertainty. However, some Hanafi scholars like Zufar and Abu Yusuf had differing views. This lesson clarifies the relied-upon position.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is claiming property with boundaries. The ruling is that three witnesses suffice to prove the claim.
2
Understand the basis
Three witnesses form a majority (al-akthar), which provides stronger evidence than two. This is the reasoning given in the text.
Majority principle: three is a clear majority over two.
3
Note the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf
Zufar disagreed with the specific number, and Abu Yusuf held that two witnesses suffice, as recorded in al-Khaniyah.
Abu Yusuf's view is a minority within the school.
4
Determine the mufta bihi
The relied-upon position (mufta bihi) is that three witnesses suffice, as indicated by the text's primary ruling.
The text does not adopt Abu Yusuf's view.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله: (وكفت ثلاثة لوجود الأكثر خلافاً لزفر، وعند أبي يوسف يكتفى باثنين كما في الخانية، بخلاف ما إذا غلط في الرابع لأنه يختلف المدعى به ولا كذلك بتركه. وفي جامع الفصولين وإنما يثبت الغلط بإقرار الشاهد أني غلطت فيه، أما لو ادعاه المدعى عليه لا تسمع ولا تقبل بينته لأن دعوى غلط الشاهد من المدعى عليه إنما يكون بعد دعوى المدعي وجواب المدعى عليه والمدعي عليه حين أجاب المدعي فقد صدقه أن المدعي بهذه الحدود فيصير المدعي بدعوى الغلط مناقضاً بعده أو نقول: تفسير دعوى الغلط أحد الحدود أن يقول المدعى عليه أحد الحدود ليس ما ذكره الشاهد أو يقول صاحب الحد ليس بهذا بالاسم الذي ذكره الشاهد وكل ذلك نفي والشهادة على النفي لا تقبل.
His statement: (And three suffice because of the existence of the majority, contrary to Zufar. And according to Abu Yusuf, two suffice, as in al-Khaniyah. Contrary to if he errs in the fourth because the claimed item differs, and not so by leaving it. And in Jami' al-Fusulayn: Error is only proven by the witness's admission saying 'I erred therein'. As for if the defendant claims it, it is not heard and his evidence is not accepted, because the defendant's claim of the witness's error only comes after the plaintiff's claim and the defendant's response, and the defendant when he answered the plaintiff has affirmed that the plaintiff is claiming these boundaries, so the plaintiff by claiming error afterwards becomes contradictory. Or we say: The interpretation of the claim of error in one boundary is that the defendant says 'one of the boundaries is not what the witness mentioned' or says 'the owner of that boundary is not by that name which the witness mentioned', and all that is negation, and testimony on negation is not accepted.
Source pages p. 339

Commentary
This passage discusses two issues: (1) the number of witnesses required for a claim with boundaries. Three witnesses suffice because they form a majority, and this is contrary to Zufar who required a specific number. Abu Yusuf held two suffice. The text also notes that if a witness errs in the fourth boundary, the claimed item differs, so error in the fourth is not like leaving it (not specifying). (2) The second part from Jami' al-Fusulayn deals with how error in a witness's testimony is established. Error is only accepted if the witness admits it himself. If the defendant claims the witness erred, it is not accepted because the defendant has already affirmed the boundaries by his response, and claiming error would contradict his earlier affirmation. Additionally, the defendant's claim is essentially a negation, and testimony on negation is not accepted in Hanafi law.

Key Terms
الغلط في الشهادة (al-ghalat fi al-shahadah): Error in testimony, specifically in the boundaries mentioned.
النفي (al-nafy): Negation; testimony on negation is not accepted.
الحدود (al-hudud): Boundaries of a property that are specified in a claim.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, how many witnesses are sufficient for a property boundary claim?
A) One
B) Two
C) Three
D) Four

Key Takeaway
Three witnesses suffice for boundary claims; this is the mufta bihi position despite ikhtilaf.

Establishing Error in Witness Testimony: Only Witness Admission
Ruling on procedure when a witness errs in boundaries

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the condition for establishing error in testimony and explain why the defendant cannot claim the witness's error.

Core Idea
Error in testimony is proven only by the witness's own admission; the defendant's claim of error is rejected as negation.

When a witness makes an error in a boundary, the only way to establish that error is if the witness himself admits it. The defendant cannot claim the witness erred because doing so would contradict his earlier affirmation of the boundaries or amount to a negation, and testimony on negation is not accepted. This lesson unpacks the reasoning behind this rule.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act being ruled
The act is establishing that a witness erred in his testimony regarding boundaries.
2
Note the condition for proving error
Error is proven only by the witness's own admission: 'I erred therein'.
No other evidence is accepted for this.
3
Understand why defendant's claim is rejected
Two reasons: (a) the defendant, by answering the plaintiff, has already affirmed the boundaries, so claiming error is contradictory; (b) the defendant's claim is essentially a negation (denying that a boundary is as stated), and testimony on negation is not accepted.
This prevents endless disputes.
4
Apply the principle to similar cases
If the witness errs in the fourth boundary, the claimed item changes, so it is different from simply leaving it unspecified.
Error in fourth boundary is thus a substantive error.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله: (وكفت ثلاثة لوجود الأكثر خلافاً لزفر، وعند أبي يوسف يكتفى باثنين كما في الخانية، بخلاف ما إذا غلط في الرابع لأنه يختلف المدعى به ولا كذلك بتركه. وفي جامع الفصولين وإنما يثبت الغلط بإقرار الشاهد أني غلطت فيه، أما لو ادعاه المدعى عليه لا تسمع ولا تقبل بينته لأن دعوى غلط الشاهد من المدعى عليه إنما يكون بعد دعوى المدعي وجواب المدعى عليه والمدعي عليه حين أجاب المدعي فقد صدقه أن المدعي بهذه الحدود فيصير المدعي بدعوى الغلط مناقضاً بعده أو نقول: تفسير دعوى الغلط أحد الحدود أن يقول المدعى عليه أحد الحدود ليس ما ذكره الشاهد أو يقول صاحب الحد ليس بهذا بالاسم الذي ذكره الشاهد وكل ذلك نفي والشهادة على النفي لا تقبل.
His statement: (And three suffice because of the existence of the majority, contrary to Zufar. And according to Abu Yusuf, two suffice, as in al-Khaniyah. Contrary to if he errs in the fourth because the claimed item differs, and not so by leaving it. And in Jami' al-Fusulayn: Error is only proven by the witness's admission saying 'I erred therein'. As for if the defendant claims it, it is not heard and his evidence is not accepted, because the defendant's claim of the witness's error only comes after the plaintiff's claim and the defendant's response, and the defendant when he answered the plaintiff has affirmed that the plaintiff is claiming these boundaries, so the plaintiff by claiming error afterwards becomes contradictory. Or we say: The interpretation of the claim of error in one boundary is that the defendant says 'one of the boundaries is not what the witness mentioned' or says 'the owner of that boundary is not by that name which the witness mentioned', and all that is negation, and testimony on negation is not accepted.
Source pages p. 339

Commentary
This passage discusses two issues: (1) the number of witnesses required for a claim with boundaries. Three witnesses suffice because they form a majority, and this is contrary to Zufar who required a specific number. Abu Yusuf held two suffice. The text also notes that if a witness errs in the fourth boundary, the claimed item differs, so error in the fourth is not like leaving it (not specifying). (2) The second part from Jami' al-Fusulayn deals with how error in a witness's testimony is established. Error is only accepted if the witness admits it himself. If the defendant claims the witness erred, it is not accepted because the defendant has already affirmed the boundaries by his response, and claiming error would contradict his earlier affirmation. Additionally, the defendant's claim is essentially a negation, and testimony on negation is not accepted in Hanafi law.

Key Terms
الغلط في الشهادة (al-ghalat fi al-shahadah): Error in testimony, specifically in the boundaries mentioned.
النفي (al-nafy): Negation; testimony on negation is not accepted.
الحدود (al-hudud): Boundaries of a property that are specified in a claim.
الرابع (al-rabi): The fourth boundary; error here changes the claimed item.

Key Terms from Source Passage

A) By the defendant's claim
B) By other witnesses
C) By the witness's own admission
D) By the judge's inspection

Precedence of External Claimant's Evidence
Hanafi vs Shafi'i dispute on evidence precedence

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi position on preferring the external claimant's evidence over the possessor's, and evaluate the Shafi'i counter-argument using qiyas.

Core Idea
The external claimant's evidence is stronger because it reveals what possession conceals.

This passage presents a classic Hanafi-Shafi'i dispute over whose evidence is stronger when both parties claim absolute ownership of property. The Hanafi school rules for the external claimant, while al-Shafi'i rules for the possessor. Understanding this dispute hinges on the nature of possession as evidence (amara) and the scope of analogical reasoning.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi ruling
Identify that Hanafis rule for the external claimant's evidence over the possessor's in absolute ownership disputes.
The matn says: 'بينة الخارج أحق' (the external's evidence is more deserving).
2
Present the Shafi'i position and analogy
Al-Shafi'i argues that the possessor's evidence is supported by possession, making it stronger, analogous to cases like offspring and marriage.
He uses qiyas: the possessor's evidence is like the husband's evidence for paternity, etc.
3
Analyze the Hanafi rebuttal
Hanafis respond that the external's evidence establishes more than possession does; possession only indicates absolute ownership, while the external's evidence can show a specific right.
The analogy fails because in offspring/marriage, the hand does not indicate the relationship, whereas in property, the hand already indicates ownership.
4
Consider the condition of dates
If both parties have dated documents, the external wins if his date is equal or earlier; if the possessor's date is earlier, he wins. Also, if the external claims absolute ownership and the possessor claims purchase, the external wins regardless of dates.
These nuances are taken from al-Zahiriya.
5
Identify the practical difference
The thamarah al-khilaf: a Hanafi judge rules for the external claimant; a Shafi'i judge rules for the possessor.
This shows how a single rule can lead to opposite outcomes.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : (ولا) بينة لذي اليد في الملك المطلق وبينة الخارج أحق) وقال الشافعي : القاضي مع يقضى ببينة ذي اليد لاعتضادها باليد فيتقوى الظهور فصار كالنتاج والنكاح وذي الملك الإعتاق والاستيلاد أو التدبير ولنا أن بينة الخارج أكثر إثباتاً وإظهاراً لأن قدر ما أثبته اليد لا يثبته بينة ذي اليد إذ اليد دليل مطلق الملك بخلاف النتاج لأن اليد لا تدل عليه، وكذا على الإعتاق وأختيه وعلى الولاء الثابت بها قيد بالملك المطلق لما سيأتي وأطلقه وهو مقيد بما إذا لم يؤرخا أو أرخا وتاريخ الخارج مساو أو أسبق، أما إذا كان تاريخ ذي اليد أسبق فإنه يقضى له كما سيأتي في الكتاب بخلاف ما إذا ادعى الخارج الملك المطلق وذو اليد الشراء من فلان وبرهنا أورخا وتاريخ ذي اليد أسبق فإنه يقضى للخارج كما في الظهيرية .
He said: (And the evidence of the possessor is not [accepted] in absolute ownership, and the evidence of the external claimant is more deserving). Al-Shafi'i said: The judge should rule by the evidence of the possessor because it is supported by possession, thus the appearance becomes stronger, so it becomes like the case of offspring, marriage, and the owner's [evidence regarding] emancipation, the child of a slave-girl, or the contract of writing. Our proof: The evidence of the external claimant is stronger in establishing and manifesting [ownership] because what the hand (possession) establishes is not established by the evidence of the possessor, since the hand is only evidence of absolute ownership, unlike the case of offspring because the hand does not indicate it. Similarly, regarding emancipation and its two sisters, and regarding the wala' established by them. It is restricted to absolute ownership as will come. It is unrestricted but is restricted to when they did not date [documents] or they dated and the external's date is equal or earlier. However, if the possessor's date is earlier, then judgment is for him as will come in the book. Contrary to the case where the external claims absolute ownership and the possessor claims purchase from so-and-so, and they bring evidence with dates, and the possessor's date is earlier, then judgment is for the external as in al-Zahiriya.
Source pages p. 349

Commentary
This is an inter-madhhab dispute. The matn of Kanz al-Daqa'iq states that the evidence of the possessor (dhu al-yad) is not accepted in a claim of absolute ownership, and the evidence of the external claimant (al-kharij) is more deserving. Al-Shafi'i opposed, arguing that the possessor's evidence should be preferred because it is supported by possession, strengthening the appearance of ownership. He draws an analogy to cases like childbirth (the child is attributed to the husband based on marriage), marriage (the wife's claim of dower is supported by the contract), and the owner's own testimony regarding emancipation, istilad, and tadbir. The Hanafi scholars respond by pointing out that the external claimant's evidence is stronger because it establishes something beyond what possession indicates. The hand (yad) only indicates absolute ownership in a general sense, but the external's evidence can show that the property was once his, which possession does not negate. The analogy to offspring and marriage is invalid because in those cases, the hand does not indicate the relationship; rather, the relationship is established by a contract. The ruling is further conditioned by dates: if the possessor's document is earlier, he wins; but if the external claims absolute ownership and the possessor claims a specific purchase, and the possessor's document is earlier, the external still wins because his claim is more comprehensive. This is recorded in al-Zahiriya.

Key Terms
بينة الخارج (bayyinat al-kharij): The evidence presented by the external claimant who does not currently possess the property.
ذو اليد (dhu al-yad): The person who currently has possession (yad) of the property, i.e., the possessor.
اليد (al-yad): Possession, which is a proof (amara) of ownership but not definitive.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, when both the possessor (dhu al-yad) and the external claimant present evidence for absolute ownership, whose evidence is given precedence?
A) The possessor's evidence is always given precedence.
B) The external claimant's evidence is given precedence if the dates are equal or the external's date is earlier.
C) The possessor's evidence is given precedence if it is supported by witnesses.
D) The judge decides based on his own knowledge.

Key Takeaway
The external claimant's evidence prevails unless the possessor has an earlier dated proof.

Offering the Oath Three Times: Recommended, Not Obligatory
Ruling on number of oath offers

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state that offering the oath three times is recommended (nadb) and that a ruling after one offer is valid, and explain the analogy with the apostate's respite.

Core Idea
The Hanafi judge may rule on nukul after a single oath offer; repeating three times is mustahabb, not wajib.

This lesson examines the ruling on how many times the judge should offer the oath. The matn states ' عرض اليمين ثلاثاً ندباً ' meaning offering it three times is recommended. The commentary clarifies that the sound position of the madhhab is that a ruling after one offer is valid, and the repetition is for caution and to exhaust excuses, analogous to giving an apostate three days to repent.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling on offering the oath three times
The matn explicitly says offering the oath three times is recommended (nadb). This is a hukm taklifi at the level of nadb (recommended), not wajib.
2
Understand the rationale for the recommendation
The repetition is for increased caution and to give the defendant every opportunity to swear voluntarily, thereby avoiding the consequence of nukul.
It is like giving a chance to reconsider.
3
Recognise the sound position of the madhhab
According to the correct view (al-sahih), if the judge rules after only one offer, the ruling is valid and enforceable. The three offerings are mustahabb, not mandatory.
Al-Zaylai and others report that Abu Yusuf and Muhammad held it mandatory, but the sound view is as stated.
4
Note the analogy with the apostate's respite
Just as giving an apostate three days to repent is recommended but not obligatory, similarly offering the oath three times is recommended to maximise the chance of resolution.
This analogy is explicitly mentioned in the commentary from al-Zaylai.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كتاب الدعوى

نكاح ورجعة وفيء واستيلاد ورق ونسب وولاء وحد ولعان ويستحلف السارق فإن القرض ثم وجد الإبراء والإيفاء .اهـ. فإن قلت : هل يقضي بالنكول عن اليمين لنفي التهمة كالأمين إذا ادعى الرد أو الهلاك فحلف فنكل وعن اليمين التي للاحتياط في مال الميت كما قدمناه؟ قلت: أما الأول فنعم كما في القنية وأما الثانية فلم أره .اهـ. قوله: (وعرض اليمين ثلاثاً ندباً) أي وعرض القاضي على وجه الاستحباب بأن يقول له القاضي إني أعرض عليك ثلاثاً فإن حلفت وإلا قضيت عليك بما ادعاه، وهذا الإنذار لإعلامه بالحكم إذ هو موضع الخفاء وتكرار العرض لزيادة الاحتياط والمبالغة في إبداء العذر وأما المذهب فإنه لو قضى بالنكول بعد العرض مرة جاز وهو الصحيح والأول أولى.

قوله : (ولا يستحلف في نكاح ورجعه وفيء واستيلاد ورق ونسب وولاء وحد ولعان) وقالا : يستحلف في الكل إلا في الحدود واللعان لأن النكول إقرار لأنه يدل على كونه كاذباً في الإنكار على ما قدمناه فكان إقراراً أو بدلاً عنه والإقرار يجري في هذه الأشياء لكنه إقرار فيه شبهة والحدود تندريء بالشبهات واللعان في معنى الحد ولأبي حنيفة أنه بدل لأن معه لا تبقى اليمين واجبة لحصول المقصود وإنزاله باذلاً أولى كيلا يصير كاذباً في الإنكار، والبذل لا يجري في هذه الأشياء وفائدة الاستحلاف القضاء بالنكول فلا يستحلف إلا أن هذا بذل لدفع الخصومة فيملكه المكاتب والعبد المأذون بمنزلة الضيافة اليسيرة وصحته في الدين بناء على زعم المدعي وهو يقبضه حقاً لنفسه، والبذل معناه ههنا ترك المنع وأمر المال هين؛ كذا في الهداية. وفي القنية : يستحلف في دعوى الإقرار بالنكاح اهـ ظاهره بأنه اتفاق بين أبي حنيفة وصاحبيه فليتأمل. وفي الظهيرية تفسير البذل عنده ترك المنازعة والإعراض عنها، ثم الدعوى في هذه المسائل تتصور من إحدى الخصمين أيهما كان إلا بالحد واللعان والاستيلاد أن يتصور يكون المدعي فيها إلا المقذوف والمولى ؛ كذا في الشرح وهو سبق قلم والصواب والأمة دون المولى. وفي الهداية وصورة الاستيلاد أن تقول الجارية أنا أم ولد فإنه لا : أنه عينه . تكون إحدى الروايتين عنه غير صحيحة .اهـ. ما قاله في أواخر الخامس عشر . قوله : (وأما الثانية فلم أره) قال الرملي : والوجه يقتضي القضاء بالنكول فيها أيضاً إذ فائدة الاستحلاف القضاء بالنكول كما هو ظاهر تأمل قوله : (وأما المذهب فإنه لو قضى الخ) ظاهره أنه مقابل لما في المتن مع قال الزيلعي : وعن أبي يوسف ومحمد أن التكرار حتم حتى لو قضى القاضي بالنكول مرة لا ينفذ، والصحيح أنه ينفذ، والعرض ثلاثاً مستحب وهو نظير إمهال المرتد ثلاثة أيام فإنه مستحب فكذا هذا مبالغة في الإنذار اهـ. ومثله في الكفاية قوله : (والصواب والأمة دون المولى) بقي أن يقال ظاهر كلامه كغيره أنها ادعت الاستيلاد مجرداً عن دعوى اعترافه والذي في صدر الشريعة ادعت أنها ولدت منه هذا الولد وادعاه أي ادعت أنه ادعاه فهو من تتمة كلامها كما ذكره أخي جلبي. والذي يظهر أن التقييد به ليس احترازياً بل يبتني على ما هو المشهور من أنه يشترط لثبوت نسب ولد الأمة البحر الرائق ج٧/ م ٢٣

يدعي أنه لمولاي وهذا ابني منه وأنكر المولى لأنه لو ادعى المولى ثبت الاستيلاد بإقراره ولا يلتفت إلى إنكارها اهـ. وفي جامع الفصولين وصورة النكاح أنكر هو أو هي نكاحاً والرجعة ادعى على امرأة رجعة ففي العدة تثبت بقوله وإن كذبته لأن ادعى أمراً يملك استئنافه للحال وبعدها لو صدقته ثبت بتصادقهما، ولو كذبته ولا بينة فعلى قولهما يحلف لا على قوله، وكذا لو ادعت أنه راجعها وكذبها وصورة الفيء في الإيلاء قال فئت وأنكرت فلو ادعاه في مدة الإيلاء يثبت بقوله ولو بعد مضيها، فإن صدقته ثبت وإلا ولا بينة أو ادعت أنه فاء إليها في المدة أو بعدها وأنكر الزوج وصورة الرق ادعى على مجهول الحال أنه قنه أو ادعى مجهول الحال على رجل أنه عبده وأنكر المولى. وصورة النسب ادعى مجهول النسب أنه أبوه أو ابنه . وصورة أمية الولد أن تدعي أم الولد أنها ولدته من سيدها. وصورة الولاء أن مولاه الأسفل أو الأعلى .اهـ. أطلق في الولاء فشمل ولاء العتاقة وولاء الموالاة كما في الكافي وفيه : فالحاصل أن كل محل يقبل الإباحة بالإذن ابتداء يقضى عليه بنكوله وما لا فلا اهـ. وإذا لم يستحلف في النكاح عنده فلا يخلو إما أن يكون المدعي له الزوج أو المرأة، فإن كان الزوج وقال أنا أريد أن أتزوج أختها أو أربعاً سواها فإن القاضي لا يمكنه من ذلك لأنه أقر أن هذه امرأته فيقول له إن كنت تريد ذلك فطلق هذه ثم تزوج أختها أو أربعاً سواها، وإن كانت الدعوى من المرأة فعنده لو قالت إني أريد أن أتزوج فإن القاضي لا يمكنها من ذلك لأنها قد أقرت أن لها زوجاً فلا يمكنها التزوج بآخر. فإن قالت ما الخلاص عن وقد بقيت في عهدته الدهر ولا بينة لي وهذه تسمى عهدة أبي حنيفة فإنه يقول القاضي للزوج طلقها فإن أبى أجبره القاضي عليه فإن قال الزوج لو طلقتها لزمني المهر فلا أفعل ذلك، يقول القاضي له قل لها إن كنت امرأتي فأنت طالق فتطلق لو كانت امرأته وإلا فلا ولا يلزمه شيء، فإن أبى أجبره القاضي، فإن فعل تخلص عن تلك العهدة ؛ كذا في البدائع . ثم إذا لم يستحلف المنكر عنده في النسب هل تقبل بينة المدعي؟ ينظر؛ فإن كان نسباً يثبت بالإقرار تقبل بينته مثل الولد والوالد وإن لم يثبت بإقراره لا تقبل بينته مثل الجد وولد الولد والأعمام والإخوة وأولادهم لأن فيه حمل النسب على الغير بخلاف دعوى المولى الأعلى أو الأسفل حيث يقبل، وإن ادعى أنه معتق جده ونحو ذلك وتمامه في الشرح. وقوله «قال ادعى أحد هذا وجود الدعوة من السيد وعلى غير المشروع لا يشترط ذلك بل يكفي عدم نفيه، وكذا ظاهر قولهم ادعت أمة يفيد الاحتراز عن دعوى الزوجة ويخالفه فقول القهستاني بعد قول المتن «واستيلاد بأن الأمة والمولى أو الزوجة والزوج أنها ولدت منه ولداً حياً أو ميتاً كما في قاضيخان ولكن في المشاهير أن دعوى الزوج والمولى لا تتصور لأن النسب يثبت بإقراره ولا عبرة لإنكارها بعده، ويمكن أن يقال : إنه بحسب الظاهر لم يدع النسب كما يدل عليه تصويرهم اهـ. كذا في حاشية السيد أبي السعود.
من
Book of Claims. Marriage, return, return to intercourse, umm walad, slavery, lineage, patronage, hadd, imprecation; and the thief is sworn, then the loan, then found discharge and fulfillment. If you say: Is judgment given by nukul from the oath to negate suspicion like the trustee when he claims return or destruction and swore then nukul? And about the oath of precaution in the deceased's property as we presented? I said: As for the first, yes, as in al-Qunyah; as for the second, I did not see it. End. His saying: (And offering the oath three times is recommended) meaning the judge offers it on a recommended basis by saying to him: I offer you three times, if you swear otherwise I will judge against you as claimed. This warning is to inform him of the ruling since it is a place of concealment, and repetition of offer for increased caution and exaggeration in presenting excuse. As for the madhhab, if he judges by nukul after one offer it is permissible, and that is sound, and the first is better. His saying: (And he does not administer an oath in marriage, return, return to intercourse, istilad, slavery, lineage, patronage, hadd, and imprecation). And the two said: He administers an oath in all except hadd and imprecation because nukul is an admission because it indicates he is lying in denial as we presented, so it is an admission or a substitute for it, and admission applies in these matters but it is an admission with doubt, and hadd punishments are averted by doubts, and imprecation is akin to hadd. And for Abu Hanifa, it is a substitute because with it the oath is no longer obligatory as the objective is achieved, and making him a bādhil is better so he does not become a liar in denial, and badl does not apply in these matters. The benefit of administering the oath is judgment by nukul, so he does not administer oath except that this is a badl to repel litigation, so the mukatab and authorized slave are capable of it like light hospitality, and its validity in debt is based on the claimant's claim, and he takes it as a right for himself. Badl here means leaving prevention, and the matter of wealth is easy; thus in al-Hidayah. And in al-Qunyah: He administers oath in a claim of admission of marriage – its apparent meaning is that it is agreed between Abu Hanifa and his two companions, so it should be considered. And in al-Zahiriyyah, interpretation of badl according to him is leaving dispute and turning away from it. Then the claim in these matters is conceivable from either of the two litigants, except in hadd, imprecation, and istilad, the claimant can only be the one accused of slander and the master; thus in the commentary, and it is a slip of pen, and correct is the slave woman without the master. And in al-Hidayah, the form of istilad is that the slave girl says 'I am an umm walad' then it is not: that it is the same. One of the two narrations from him is not correct. End. What he said at the end of the fifteenth part. His saying: (And as for the second, I did not see it.) Al-Ramli said: The opinion requires judgment by nukul in it as well, since the benefit of administering the oath is judgment by nukul, as is apparent. Consider his saying: (And as for the madhhab, if he judges...) its apparent that it is opposite to what is in the text. Al-Zaylai said: From Abu Yusuf and Muhammad, repetition is mandatory, so if the judge judges by nukul once it is not executable, but sound is that it is executable, and offering three times is recommended, and it is similar to giving the apostate three days respite, for it is recommended, so likewise this is exaggeration in warning. End. Similar in al-Kifayah. His saying: (And correct is the slave woman without the master.) It remains that the apparent meaning of his statement like others is that she claimed istilad without a claim of his admission, while in Sadr al-Shari'ah she claimed that she gave birth to this child from him and claimed that he claimed it, so it is part of her statement as mentioned by my brother Jilabi. And what appears is that the restriction is not exclusionary but based on what is well-known that for establishing lineage of the child of a slave woman, he claims that it is for my master and this is my son from him and the master denies, because if the master claimed, istilad is established by his admission and her denial is not considered. End. And in Jami' al-Fusulayn, the form of marriage: either husband or wife denies marriage; and return: he claims return to his wife, so during the iddah it is established by his word even if she denies because he claims something he can initiate now; after iddah, if she confirms, it is established by their mutual admission; if she denies and no evidence, according to the two [Sahibayn] he must swear, not according to him; also if she claims he returned to her and he denies. Form of fay' in ila': he says 'I returned' and she denies; if he claims it during the period of ila', it is established by his word; after it passes, if she confirms it is established, otherwise and no evidence; or she claims he returned to her during the period or after and the husband denies. Form of slavery: he claims against a person of unknown status that he is his slave, or a person of unknown status claims against a man that he is his slave and the master denies. Form of lineage: a person of unknown lineage claims he is his father or his son. Form of umm walad: that the umm walad claims she gave birth from her master. Form of patronage: that his lower or higher master. End. He generalized in patronage so it includes patronage of emancipation and patronage of clientage as in al-Kafi. In it: Conclusion: every place that permits permission by authorization initially, one is judged by his nukul; what does not, then not. End. And if he does not administer oath in marriage according to him, then it is either the husband is the claimant or the woman. If the husband says 'I want to marry her sister or four others beside her,' the judge cannot allow him because he admitted that this is his wife; he says to him: if you want that, divorce her then marry her sister or four others. If the claim is from the woman, according to him if she says 'I want to marry,' the judge cannot allow her because she admitted she has a husband, so she cannot marry another. If she says 'what is the way out?' and she remains in his bond forever and she has no evidence, this is called 'Awhadah of Abu Hanifa' – the judge tells the husband: divorce her; if he refuses, the judge compels him. If the husband says: if I divorce her, the mahr becomes obligatory on me, I won't do that; the judge says to him: say to her 'if you are my wife, you are divorced' – so she is divorced if she was his wife, otherwise not and nothing is incumbent; if he refuses, the judge compels him. If he does, he is freed from that bond; thus in al-Bada'i. Then if the denier is not sworn according to him regarding lineage, is the claimant's evidence accepted? It depends: if the lineage is established by admission, his evidence is accepted, like son and father; if not established by his admission, his evidence is not accepted, like grandfather, grandson, paternal uncles, brothers and their children, because it involves attributing lineage to another, unlike the claim of higher or lower master where it is accepted; and if he claims that he is the freed slave of his grandfather etc., and its completion in the commentary. And his saying: 'he claimed one this existence of claim from the master, and according to the non-mashhoor it is not required but rather his failure to deny suffices; as also the apparent meaning of their statement 'a slave girl claimed' indicates exclusion of the wife's claim, and it is contradicted by the statement of al-Qahistani after the text 'and istilad: that the slave girl and master, or the wife and husband, claim that she gave birth from him to a live or dead child as in Qadikhan, but among the well-known, the claim of the husband and master is not conceivable because lineage is established by his admission and her denial is not considered afterwards; and it can be said that apparently he did not claim lineage as indicated by their description.' End. Thus in the gloss of Sayyid Abu al-Sa'ud. From.
Source pages p. 353

Commentary
This passage is a commentary from al-Bahr al-Raiq on Kanz al-Daqaiq covering the chapter of claims (al-Da'wa). It opens with the matn: the judge does not administer an oath in marriage, return (raj'ah), return to intercourse (fay'), istilad, slavery, lineage, patronage, hadd, and imprecation; but he does swear the thief. The commentator then poses a question: can the judge rule by nukul (refusal to swear) in cases where the oath is used to negate suspicion, such as a trustee claiming return or loss of the trust, and in the precautionary oath concerning a deceased's estate? The answer distinguishes: yes for the trustee (as in al-Qunyah), but the second case is not seen. Next, the commentary explains that offering the oath three times is recommended (nadb), not obligatory. The judge warns the defendant: 'I offer you three times; if you swear, otherwise I will judge against you.' The repeated offer is for caution and to exhaust excuses. However, the sound position in the madhhab is that if the judge rules after one offer, it is valid. Al-Zaylai reports that Abu Yusuf and Muhammad held that repetition is mandatory (hatm), such that a ruling after one offer would not be enforceable, but the correct view is that it is enforceable and three offers are merely recommended, analogous to giving an apostate three days respite. The commentary then returns to the main ruling on the list of cases where the oath is not administered according to Abu Hanifa. The two companions (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) hold that the oath is administered in all these cases except hadd and li'an. The reasoning: for the Sahibayn, nukul is treated as an iqrar (admission) because it indicates the defendant is lying in his denial, and iqrar is valid in these matters, though it carries a shadow of doubt; hadd penalties are averted by doubts, and li'an is akin to hadd. For Abu Hanifa, nukul is a badl (substitute) for the oath; when the defendant makes nukul, the oath is no longer required because the goal (removing the claimant's suspicion) is achieved, and making him a bādhil (one who disgorges) is preferable so he does not become a liar. Badl does not apply to these cases because it is about giving up property or rights, and these matters involve personal status where badl is not applicable. Therefore, the oath is not administered in these cases. The commentary then discusses various scenarios: in marriage, if the husband is the claimant and wants to marry a second, the judge prevents him until he divorces; if the wife is the claimant and wants to remarry, she is prevented; a special case called 'Awhadah of Abu Hanifa' arises where the judge compels the husband to divorce or pronounce a conditional divorce. For lineage, evidence is accepted from the claimant if lineage is established by admission (like son or father), but not if it requires attribution to another (like grandfather or brother). The passage also details forms for each type of claim: nikkah, raj'ah, fay', riqq, nasab, istilad, wala'. The overarching principle: if the matter can be initiated by permission (i.e., the defendant has the right to grant it originally), then judgment is given based on nukul; otherwise not.

Key Terms
النكول (al-nukul): Refusal of the defendant to take the oath after it is offered by the judge.
الاستحلاف (al-istihlaf): The judge's act of requiring the defendant to take an oath to deny the claim.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the sound Hanafi view, what is the ruling if a judge rules against a defendant who refused the oath after only one offer?
A) The ruling is invalid because three offers are required.
B) The ruling is valid and enforceable.
C) The ruling is valid only if the judge first warns the defendant that he will rule after one offer.
D) The ruling is invalid unless the claimant agrees.

Key Takeaway
Offering the oath three times is recommended, but a judge may validly rule after a single offer of the oath in the Hanafi school.

Shahadat — Testimony
advanced
12 min
The Cases Where Oath is Not Administered: Abu Hanifa's View
Intra-Hanafi dispute on scope of istihlaf

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to list the seven cases (plus hadd and li'an) where Abu Hanifa does not administer the oath, explain the reasoning based on nukul as badl, and contrast with the Sahibayn's view based on nukul as iqrar.

Core Idea
Abu Hanifa excludes personal status claims from oath because nukul is a substitute (badl) applicable only to property matters.

This lesson explores a significant intra-Hanafi dispute on the scope of istihlaf. The matn states that the judge does not administer an oath in several specific types of claims: marriage, return, fay', istilad, slavery, lineage, patronage, hadd, and li'an. The commentary reveals the underlying legal principle: whether nukul (refusal to swear) is treated as an admission (iqrar) or as a substitute (badl) for the oath. This distinction determines whether the oath is required in these personal status claims.

Guided Path
1
List the cases excluded from istihlaf per Abu Hanifa
The matn lists: nikkah (marriage), raj'ah (return), fay' (return to intercourse), istilad (umm walad claim), riqq (slavery), nasab (lineage), wala' (patronage), hadd (fixed punishments), and li'an (imprecation).
Hadd and li'an are agreed upon by all, including Sahibayn.
2
Identify the dispute with the Sahibayn
Abu Yusuf and Muhammad hold that the oath is administered in all these cases except hadd and li'an. They argue that nukul is an admission (iqrar), and iqrar is valid in these matters, though it carries a shade of doubt. Hudud are averted by doubts, so excepted.
3
Understand Abu Hanifa's proof: nukul as badl
Abu Hanifa treats nukul as a substitute (badl) for the oath. When the defendant refuses, he becomes a bādhil (one who gives up the right to deny), thus the objective of the oath (repelling the suit) is achieved without an oath. Badl only applies to property claims, not personal status matters.
The commentary explains: 'making him a bādhil is better so he does not become a liar' and 'badl does not apply in these matters.'
4
Analyze the Sahibayn's counter-proof
For them, nukul indicates the defendant is lying in his denial, so it is an implicit admission (iqrar). Iqrar is effective in personal status, though with shubha. Hudud are averted by shubha, so excepted. Li'an is akin to hadd.
The text says: 'for them nukul is an admission because it indicates he is lying in denial.'
5
Determine the practical consequence (thamarah al-khilaf)
In a marriage claim, if the defendant refuses to swear, Abu Hanifa does not administer an oath and does not rule by nukul; the Sahibayn would administer the oath and rule by nukul. This affects whether the judge can compel an oath and whether nukol leads to judgment.
The commentary provides detailed scenarios for each case, showing the application.

كتاب الدعوى

نكاح ورجعة وفيء واستيلاد ورق ونسب وولاء وحد ولعان ويستحلف السارق فإن القرض ثم وجد الإبراء والإيفاء .اهـ. فإن قلت : هل يقضي بالنكول عن اليمين لنفي التهمة كالأمين إذا ادعى الرد أو الهلاك فحلف فنكل وعن اليمين التي للاحتياط في مال الميت كما قدمناه؟ قلت: أما الأول فنعم كما في القنية وأما الثانية فلم أره .اهـ. قوله: (وعرض اليمين ثلاثاً ندباً) أي وعرض القاضي على وجه الاستحباب بأن يقول له القاضي إني أعرض عليك ثلاثاً فإن حلفت وإلا قضيت عليك بما ادعاه، وهذا الإنذار لإعلامه بالحكم إذ هو موضع الخفاء وتكرار العرض لزيادة الاحتياط والمبالغة في إبداء العذر وأما المذهب فإنه لو قضى بالنكول بعد العرض مرة جاز وهو الصحيح والأول أولى.

قوله : (ولا يستحلف في نكاح ورجعه وفيء واستيلاد ورق ونسب وولاء وحد ولعان) وقالا : يستحلف في الكل إلا في الحدود واللعان لأن النكول إقرار لأنه يدل على كونه كاذباً في الإنكار على ما قدمناه فكان إقراراً أو بدلاً عنه والإقرار يجري في هذه الأشياء لكنه إقرار فيه شبهة والحدود تندريء بالشبهات واللعان في معنى الحد ولأبي حنيفة أنه بدل لأن معه لا تبقى اليمين واجبة لحصول المقصود وإنزاله باذلاً أولى كيلا يصير كاذباً في الإنكار، والبذل لا يجري في هذه الأشياء وفائدة الاستحلاف القضاء بالنكول فلا يستحلف إلا أن هذا بذل لدفع الخصومة فيملكه المكاتب والعبد المأذون بمنزلة الضيافة اليسيرة وصحته في الدين بناء على زعم المدعي وهو يقبضه حقاً لنفسه، والبذل معناه ههنا ترك المنع وأمر المال هين؛ كذا في الهداية. وفي القنية : يستحلف في دعوى الإقرار بالنكاح اهـ ظاهره بأنه اتفاق بين أبي حنيفة وصاحبيه فليتأمل. وفي الظهيرية تفسير البذل عنده ترك المنازعة والإعراض عنها، ثم الدعوى في هذه المسائل تتصور من إحدى الخصمين أيهما كان إلا بالحد واللعان والاستيلاد أن يتصور يكون المدعي فيها إلا المقذوف والمولى ؛ كذا في الشرح وهو سبق قلم والصواب والأمة دون المولى. وفي الهداية وصورة الاستيلاد أن تقول الجارية أنا أم ولد فإنه لا : أنه عينه . تكون إحدى الروايتين عنه غير صحيحة .اهـ. ما قاله في أواخر الخامس عشر . قوله : (وأما الثانية فلم أره) قال الرملي : والوجه يقتضي القضاء بالنكول فيها أيضاً إذ فائدة الاستحلاف القضاء بالنكول كما هو ظاهر تأمل قوله : (وأما المذهب فإنه لو قضى الخ) ظاهره أنه مقابل لما في المتن مع قال الزيلعي : وعن أبي يوسف ومحمد أن التكرار حتم حتى لو قضى القاضي بالنكول مرة لا ينفذ، والصحيح أنه ينفذ، والعرض ثلاثاً مستحب وهو نظير إمهال المرتد ثلاثة أيام فإنه مستحب فكذا هذا مبالغة في الإنذار اهـ. ومثله في الكفاية قوله : (والصواب والأمة دون المولى) بقي أن يقال ظاهر كلامه كغيره أنها ادعت الاستيلاد مجرداً عن دعوى اعترافه والذي في صدر الشريعة ادعت أنها ولدت منه هذا الولد وادعاه أي ادعت أنه ادعاه فهو من تتمة كلامها كما ذكره أخي جلبي. والذي يظهر أن التقييد به ليس احترازياً بل يبتني على ما هو المشهور من أنه يشترط لثبوت نسب ولد الأمة البحر الرائق ج٧/ م ٢٣

يدعي أنه لمولاي وهذا ابني منه وأنكر المولى لأنه لو ادعى المولى ثبت الاستيلاد بإقراره ولا يلتفت إلى إنكارها اهـ. وفي جامع الفصولين وصورة النكاح أنكر هو أو هي نكاحاً والرجعة ادعى على امرأة رجعة ففي العدة تثبت بقوله وإن كذبته لأن ادعى أمراً يملك استئنافه للحال وبعدها لو صدقته ثبت بتصادقهما، ولو كذبته ولا بينة فعلى قولهما يحلف لا على قوله، وكذا لو ادعت أنه راجعها وكذبها وصورة الفيء في الإيلاء قال فئت وأنكرت فلو ادعاه في مدة الإيلاء يثبت بقوله ولو بعد مضيها، فإن صدقته ثبت وإلا ولا بينة أو ادعت أنه فاء إليها في المدة أو بعدها وأنكر الزوج وصورة الرق ادعى على مجهول الحال أنه قنه أو ادعى مجهول الحال على رجل أنه عبده وأنكر المولى. وصورة النسب ادعى مجهول النسب أنه أبوه أو ابنه . وصورة أمية الولد أن تدعي أم الولد أنها ولدته من سيدها. وصورة الولاء أن مولاه الأسفل أو الأعلى .اهـ. أطلق في الولاء فشمل ولاء العتاقة وولاء الموالاة كما في الكافي وفيه : فالحاصل أن كل محل يقبل الإباحة بالإذن ابتداء يقضى عليه بنكوله وما لا فلا اهـ. وإذا لم يستحلف في النكاح عنده فلا يخلو إما أن يكون المدعي له الزوج أو المرأة، فإن كان الزوج وقال أنا أريد أن أتزوج أختها أو أربعاً سواها فإن القاضي لا يمكنه من ذلك لأنه أقر أن هذه امرأته فيقول له إن كنت تريد ذلك فطلق هذه ثم تزوج أختها أو أربعاً سواها، وإن كانت الدعوى من المرأة فعنده لو قالت إني أريد أن أتزوج فإن القاضي لا يمكنها من ذلك لأنها قد أقرت أن لها زوجاً فلا يمكنها التزوج بآخر. فإن قالت ما الخلاص عن وقد بقيت في عهدته الدهر ولا بينة لي وهذه تسمى عهدة أبي حنيفة فإنه يقول القاضي للزوج طلقها فإن أبى أجبره القاضي عليه فإن قال الزوج لو طلقتها لزمني المهر فلا أفعل ذلك، يقول القاضي له قل لها إن كنت امرأتي فأنت طالق فتطلق لو كانت امرأته وإلا فلا ولا يلزمه شيء، فإن أبى أجبره القاضي، فإن فعل تخلص عن تلك العهدة ؛ كذا في البدائع . ثم إذا لم يستحلف المنكر عنده في النسب هل تقبل بينة المدعي؟ ينظر؛ فإن كان نسباً يثبت بالإقرار تقبل بينته مثل الولد والوالد وإن لم يثبت بإقراره لا تقبل بينته مثل الجد وولد الولد والأعمام والإخوة وأولادهم لأن فيه حمل النسب على الغير بخلاف دعوى المولى الأعلى أو الأسفل حيث يقبل، وإن ادعى أنه معتق جده ونحو ذلك وتمامه في الشرح. وقوله «قال ادعى أحد هذا وجود الدعوة من السيد وعلى غير المشروع لا يشترط ذلك بل يكفي عدم نفيه، وكذا ظاهر قولهم ادعت أمة يفيد الاحتراز عن دعوى الزوجة ويخالفه فقول القهستاني بعد قول المتن «واستيلاد بأن الأمة والمولى أو الزوجة والزوج أنها ولدت منه ولداً حياً أو ميتاً كما في قاضيخان ولكن في المشاهير أن دعوى الزوج والمولى لا تتصور لأن النسب يثبت بإقراره ولا عبرة لإنكارها بعده، ويمكن أن يقال : إنه بحسب الظاهر لم يدع النسب كما يدل عليه تصويرهم اهـ. كذا في حاشية السيد أبي السعود.
من
Book of Claims. Marriage, return, return to intercourse, umm walad, slavery, lineage, patronage, hadd, imprecation; and the thief is sworn, then the loan, then found discharge and fulfillment. If you say: Is judgment given by nukul from the oath to negate suspicion like the trustee when he claims return or destruction and swore then nukul? And about the oath of precaution in the deceased's property as we presented? I said: As for the first, yes, as in al-Qunyah; as for the second, I did not see it. End. His saying: (And offering the oath three times is recommended) meaning the judge offers it on a recommended basis by saying to him: I offer you three times, if you swear otherwise I will judge against you as claimed. This warning is to inform him of the ruling since it is a place of concealment, and repetition of offer for increased caution and exaggeration in presenting excuse. As for the madhhab, if he judges by nukul after one offer it is permissible, and that is sound, and the first is better. His saying: (And he does not administer an oath in marriage, return, return to intercourse, istilad, slavery, lineage, patronage, hadd, and imprecation). And the two said: He administers an oath in all except hadd and imprecation because nukul is an admission because it indicates he is lying in denial as we presented, so it is an admission or a substitute for it, and admission applies in these matters but it is an admission with doubt, and hadd punishments are averted by doubts, and imprecation is akin to hadd. And for Abu Hanifa, it is a substitute because with it the oath is no longer obligatory as the objective is achieved, and making him a bādhil is better so he does not become a liar in denial, and badl does not apply in these matters. The benefit of administering the oath is judgment by nukul, so he does not administer oath except that this is a badl to repel litigation, so the mukatab and authorized slave are capable of it like light hospitality, and its validity in debt is based on the claimant's claim, and he takes it as a right for himself. Badl here means leaving prevention, and the matter of wealth is easy; thus in al-Hidayah. And in al-Qunyah: He administers oath in a claim of admission of marriage – its apparent meaning is that it is agreed between Abu Hanifa and his two companions, so it should be considered. And in al-Zahiriyyah, interpretation of badl according to him is leaving dispute and turning away from it. Then the claim in these matters is conceivable from either of the two litigants, except in hadd, imprecation, and istilad, the claimant can only be the one accused of slander and the master; thus in the commentary, and it is a slip of pen, and correct is the slave woman without the master. And in al-Hidayah, the form of istilad is that the slave girl says 'I am an umm walad' then it is not: that it is the same. One of the two narrations from him is not correct. End. What he said at the end of the fifteenth part. His saying: (And as for the second, I did not see it.) Al-Ramli said: The opinion requires judgment by nukul in it as well, since the benefit of administering the oath is judgment by nukul, as is apparent. Consider his saying: (And as for the madhhab, if he judges...) its apparent that it is opposite to what is in the text. Al-Zaylai said: From Abu Yusuf and Muhammad, repetition is mandatory, so if the judge judges by nukul once it is not executable, but sound is that it is executable, and offering three times is recommended, and it is similar to giving the apostate three days respite, for it is recommended, so likewise this is exaggeration in warning. End. Similar in al-Kifayah. His saying: (And correct is the slave woman without the master.) It remains that the apparent meaning of his statement like others is that she claimed istilad without a claim of his admission, while in Sadr al-Shari'ah she claimed that she gave birth to this child from him and claimed that he claimed it, so it is part of her statement as mentioned by my brother Jilabi. And what appears is that the restriction is not exclusionary but based on what is well-known that for establishing lineage of the child of a slave woman, he claims that it is for my master and this is my son from him and the master denies, because if the master claimed, istilad is established by his admission and her denial is not considered. End. And in Jami' al-Fusulayn, the form of marriage: either husband or wife denies marriage; and return: he claims return to his wife, so during the iddah it is established by his word even if she denies because he claims something he can initiate now; after iddah, if she confirms, it is established by their mutual admission; if she denies and no evidence, according to the two [Sahibayn] he must swear, not according to him; also if she claims he returned to her and he denies. Form of fay' in ila': he says 'I returned' and she denies; if he claims it during the period of ila', it is established by his word; after it passes, if she confirms it is established, otherwise and no evidence; or she claims he returned to her during the period or after and the husband denies. Form of slavery: he claims against a person of unknown status that he is his slave, or a person of unknown status claims against a man that he is his slave and the master denies. Form of lineage: a person of unknown lineage claims he is his father or his son. Form of umm walad: that the umm walad claims she gave birth from her master. Form of patronage: that his lower or higher master. End. He generalized in patronage so it includes patronage of emancipation and patronage of clientage as in al-Kafi. In it: Conclusion: every place that permits permission by authorization initially, one is judged by his nukul; what does not, then not. End. And if he does not administer oath in marriage according to him, then it is either the husband is the claimant or the woman. If the husband says 'I want to marry her sister or four others beside her,' the judge cannot allow him because he admitted that this is his wife; he says to him: if you want that, divorce her then marry her sister or four others. If the claim is from the woman, according to him if she says 'I want to marry,' the judge cannot allow her because she admitted she has a husband, so she cannot marry another. If she says 'what is the way out?' and she remains in his bond forever and she has no evidence, this is called 'Awhadah of Abu Hanifa' – the judge tells the husband: divorce her; if he refuses, the judge compels him. If the husband says: if I divorce her, the mahr becomes obligatory on me, I won't do that; the judge says to him: say to her 'if you are my wife, you are divorced' – so she is divorced if she was his wife, otherwise not and nothing is incumbent; if he refuses, the judge compels him. If he does, he is freed from that bond; thus in al-Bada'i. Then if the denier is not sworn according to him regarding lineage, is the claimant's evidence accepted? It depends: if the lineage is established by admission, his evidence is accepted, like son and father; if not established by his admission, his evidence is not accepted, like grandfather, grandson, paternal uncles, brothers and their children, because it involves attributing lineage to another, unlike the claim of higher or lower master where it is accepted; and if he claims that he is the freed slave of his grandfather etc., and its completion in the commentary. And his saying: 'he claimed one this existence of claim from the master, and according to the non-mashhoor it is not required but rather his failure to deny suffices; as also the apparent meaning of their statement 'a slave girl claimed' indicates exclusion of the wife's claim, and it is contradicted by the statement of al-Qahistani after the text 'and istilad: that the slave girl and master, or the wife and husband, claim that she gave birth from him to a live or dead child as in Qadikhan, but among the well-known, the claim of the husband and master is not conceivable because lineage is established by his admission and her denial is not considered afterwards; and it can be said that apparently he did not claim lineage as indicated by their description.' End. Thus in the gloss of Sayyid Abu al-Sa'ud. From.
Source pages p. 353

Commentary
This passage is a commentary from al-Bahr al-Raiq on Kanz al-Daqaiq covering the chapter of claims (al-Da'wa). It opens with the matn: the judge does not administer an oath in marriage, return (raj'ah), return to intercourse (fay'), istilad, slavery, lineage, patronage, hadd, and imprecation; but he does swear the thief. The commentator then poses a question: can the judge rule by nukul (refusal to swear) in cases where the oath is used to negate suspicion, such as a trustee claiming return or loss of the trust, and in the precautionary oath concerning a deceased's estate? The answer distinguishes: yes for the trustee (as in al-Qunyah), but the second case is not seen. Next, the commentary explains that offering the oath three times is recommended (nadb), not obligatory. The judge warns the defendant: 'I offer you three times; if you swear, otherwise I will judge against you.' The repeated offer is for caution and to exhaust excuses. However, the sound position in the madhhab is that if the judge rules after one offer, it is valid. Al-Zaylai reports that Abu Yusuf and Muhammad held that repetition is mandatory (hatm), such that a ruling after one offer would not be enforceable, but the correct view is that it is enforceable and three offers are merely recommended, analogous to giving an apostate three days respite. The commentary then returns to the main ruling on the list of cases where the oath is not administered according to Abu Hanifa. The two companions (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) hold that the oath is administered in all these cases except hadd and li'an. The reasoning: for the Sahibayn, nukul is treated as an iqrar (admission) because it indicates the defendant is lying in his denial, and iqrar is valid in these matters, though it carries a shadow of doubt; hadd penalties are averted by doubts, and li'an is akin to hadd. For Abu Hanifa, nukul is a badl (substitute) for the oath; when the defendant makes nukul, the oath is no longer required because the goal (removing the claimant's suspicion) is achieved, and making him a bādhil (one who disgorges) is preferable so he does not become a liar. Badl does not apply to these cases because it is about giving up property or rights, and these matters involve personal status where badl is not applicable. Therefore, the oath is not administered in these cases. The commentary then discusses various scenarios: in marriage, if the husband is the claimant and wants to marry a second, the judge prevents him until he divorces; if the wife is the claimant and wants to remarry, she is prevented; a special case called 'Awhadah of Abu Hanifa' arises where the judge compels the husband to divorce or pronounce a conditional divorce. For lineage, evidence is accepted from the claimant if lineage is established by admission (like son or father), but not if it requires attribution to another (like grandfather or brother). The passage also details forms for each type of claim: nikkah, raj'ah, fay', riqq, nasab, istilad, wala'. The overarching principle: if the matter can be initiated by permission (i.e., the defendant has the right to grant it originally), then judgment is given based on nukul; otherwise not.

Key Terms
النكول (al-nukul): Refusal of the defendant to take the oath after it is offered by the judge.
البذل (al-badl): The act of the defendant disgorging or yielding the right in dispute to avoid the oath; considered a substitute for the oath in Abu Hanifa's view.
الاستحلاف (al-istihlaf): The judge's act of requiring the defendant to take an oath to deny the claim.
الإقرار (al-iqrar): Admission or confession; in this context, treating nukul as an implicit admission of the claim.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Abu Hanifa, in which of the following claims is the oath administered to the defendant?
A) Claim of marriage (nikkah)
B) Claim of lineage (nasab)
C) Claim of debt (dayn)
D) Claim of return (raj'ah)

Key Takeaway
Abu Hanifa treats nukul as a substitute (badl) for the oath, applicable only to property claims, thus excluding personal status matters from istihlaf.

Claimant with Present Evidence Not Given Oath
Intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf on oath demand when claimant has present evidence.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the positions of Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf on whether a claimant with present witnesses may demand an oath, and explain the practical consequence of their ikhtilaf.

Core Idea
The oath is the claimant's right only when he cannot produce evidence; having present witnesses removes that right.

A claimant walks into court saying 'I have a witness right here, but I want the defendant to swear an oath.' Should the judge grant the oath? The Hanafi school has an internal dispute on this very question, led by the two great imams Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf. This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq unpacks the reasoning behind each position and clarifies key distinctions about where the evidence is located.

Guided Path
1
State the matn ruling and the ikhtilaf
Identify the ruling in Kanz al-Daqa'iq that a claimant with present evidence is not given the oath. Then note that this is Abu Hanifa's view, and that Abu Yusuf disagreed.
The matn is explicit: 'لا يستحلف' – he is not made to swear.
2
Examine the proofs of each imam
Abu Yusuf relies on the well-known hadith that the oath is the claimant's right. Abu Hanifa counters that the right to the oath is contingent upon inability to produce evidence. Understand how each interprets the same hadith.
The hadith referenced is likely 'اليمين على المدعى عليه' – the oath is upon the defendant, which gives the claimant the right to demand it when he cannot prove his claim.
3
Identify Muhammad's two narrations
Note that Imam Muhammad has two positions: one with Abu Yusuf (via al-Khassaf) and one with Abu Hanifa (via al-Tahawi). Acknowledge the range of opinion within the school.
4
Apply the distinctions of location
The passage clarifies that if the witnesses are present in court, there is no ikhtilaf: the claimant is not sworn. If they are present in the city, there is ikhtilaf. If they are outside the city, the oath is given by agreement. Consider also the condition of illness.
Travel distance defines absence (مسيرة السفر).
5
Examine additional rulings
Note that if the claimant has a just witness but does not inform the judge, he has a choice. Also, the passage discusses cases where the judge may or may not administer an oath based on likelihood of refusal or perjury.
The seal (ختم) procedure is also mentioned but is a separate case.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : (ولو قال المدعي لي بينة حاضرة وطلب اليمين لم يستحلف) أي عند أبي حنيفة . وقال أبو يوسف : يستحلف لأن اليمين حقه بالحديث المعروف فإذا طالبه به يجيبه. ولأبي حنيفة أن ثبوت الحق في اليمين مرتب على العجز عن إقامة البينة بما رويناه فلا يكون حقه دونه، ومحمد مع أبي يوسف فيما ذكره الخصاف، ومع أبي حنيفة فيما ذكره الطحاوي. أطلق في حضورها فشمل حضورها في مجلس الحكم ولا خلاف أنه لا يحلف وحضورها في المصر وهو محل الاختلاف وحضورها في المصر بصفة المرض، وظاهر ما في خزانة المفتين خلافه فإنه قال : الاستحلاف يجري في الدعاوى الصحيحة إذا أنكر المدعى عليه ويقول المدعي لا شهود لي أو شهودي غيب أو مرضى اهـ . وقيد بحضورها لأنها لو كانت خارج المصر فإنه يحلف اتفاقاً. وفي المجتبى وقدرت الغيبة بمسيرة السفر .اهـ. وقيد بقوله «المدعي» لأنه لو كان له بينة عادلة حاضرة ولم يخبر القاضي بها فهو مخير بين الاستحلاف وبين إقامة البينة؛ كذا في القنية. ثم رقم بعده لآخر : إن غلب على ظنه أنه ينكل فله أن يحلفه، وإن غلب على ظنه أنه يحلف كاذباً لا يعذر في التحليف وفيها أيضاً ادعى المديون الإيصال فأنكر المدعي ولا بينة له فطلب يمينه فقال المدعي اجعل حقي في الختم ثم استحلفني فله ذلك في زماننا ثلاثة أيام فإن أبى لازمه أي دارم معه حيث دار ولو كان غريباً لازمه مقدار مجلس كما اهـ. ولو قال لا بينة لي وطلب يمين خصمه فحلفه القاضي فقال لي بينة فإن القاضي يقبل ذلك منه، وقيل لا يقبل؛ كذا في خزانة المفتين وقدمناه
His saying: (And if the claimant says 'I have a present witness' and demands the oath, he is not made to swear) i.e., according to Abu Hanifa. Abu Yusuf said: He is made to swear, because the oath is his right by the well-known hadith, so if he demands it, he must respond. For Abu Hanifa, the establishment of the right to the oath is contingent upon inability to produce evidence, as we have narrated, so his right is not prior to that. Muhammad is with Abu Yusuf according to what al-Khassaf mentioned, and with Abu Hanifa according to what al-Tahawi mentioned. He (the author) made it absolute regarding its presence, so it includes its presence in the court, and there is no disagreement that he is not sworn; and its presence in the city is the point of disagreement, and its presence in the city with the condition of illness. The apparent content of Khazanat al-Muftin is contrary to this, for he said: Administering the oath occurs in valid claims when the defendant denies and the claimant says 'I have no witnesses' or 'my witnesses are absent or ill.' End quote. And he restricted it by its presence, because if they were outside the city, he is sworn by agreement. In al-Mujtaba: Absence is defined by the travel distance. End quote. And he restricted it by his saying 'the claimant', because if he has a just present witness and does not inform the judge, he has the choice between demanding the oath and presenting the witness; as in al-Qunyah. Then he numbered after it another: If he thinks it likely that he will refuse, he may have him sworn; if he thinks it likely that he will swear falsely, he is not excused in having him sworn. And in it also: The debtor claimed payment, and the claimant denied, and he had no evidence, so he demanded his oath; the claimant said: place my right in a seal then have me sworn; he may do that in our time for three days; if he refuses, he obliges him, that is, he keeps company with him wherever he is, and if he is a stranger, he obliges him for the duration of a session, as in the text. And if he says 'I have no evidence' and demands the oath of his opponent, and the judge swears him, then he says 'I have evidence', the judge accepts that from him, and it is said: he does not accept; as in Khazanat al-Muftin, and we have presented it earlier.
Source pages p. 358

Commentary
This passage is a commentary on the matn of Kanz al-Daqa'iq. The matn states: 'And if the claimant says, I have a present witness, and demands the oath, he is not made to swear.' The commentator explains that this is Abu Hanifa's position. Abu Yusuf argues that the claimant should be given the oath because the oath is his right based on a well-known hadith ('The oath is upon the defendant'? Actually the hadith is 'اليمين على من أنكر' - but here it says 'اليمين حقه', meaning the claimant has a right to demand an oath from the defendant). Abu Hanifa counters that the right to the oath is conditioned upon the claimant's inability to produce evidence; if he has present witnesses, he must present them, and his right to the oath is secondary. Muhammad al-Shaybani has two positions: one with Abu Yusuf (related by al-Khassaf) and one with Abu Hanifa (related by al-Tahawi). The commentary then discusses nuances: if the claimant's witnesses are present in the court, there is no disagreement that he is not given the oath; if they are present in the city, there is ikhtilaf; if they are outside the city, he is given the oath by agreement. The passage also mentions that if the claimant has a just present witness but does not inform the judge, he has a choice between demanding the oath and presenting the witness. Additional rulings: if the judge thinks the defendant might refuse to swear, he may have him sworn; if he might swear falsely, the judge should not. The passage ends with an example about a debtor claiming payment and the claimant demanding an oath after placing the right in a seal, with a three-day period.

Key Terms
البينة الحاضرة (al-bayyinah al-hadirah): Evidence that is present in the city or in the court at the time of the claim.
اليمين (al-yamin): Oath taken by the defendant to deny the claim, or demanded by the claimant.
الاستحلاف (al-istihlaf): The act of administering the oath to the defendant.
الختم (al-khatm): A seal placed on the right as a form of security.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is Abu Hanifa's ruling when the claimant says 'I have a present witness' and demands the oath?
A) He is given the oath.
B) He is not given the oath.
C) He is given the oath only if the witness is absent from the city.
D) The judge has discretion.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi fiqh, the right to demand an oath is contingent upon the inability to produce evidence; when evidence is present, the oath is not permitted.

Repelling Claim by Proving Deposit for Known Absent Person
Ruling with proof on repelling claim by deposit evidence.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi rule for repelling a plaintiff's ownership claim by proving deposit, and identify the required specification of the absent depositor.

Core Idea
The defendant can repel a plaintiff's claim by proving the property is a deposit for a known absent person.

In Hanafi qada, a defendant holding property can dismiss a plaintiff's ownership suit by proving it is a deposit (wadi‘ah) for a specific absent person. This lesson examines the basic rule, the necessity of identifying the depositor, and the intra-Hanafi dispute over whether witnesses must know the absent person by name or only by face.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and ruling
What is the legal act? The defendant is repelling the plaintiff’s claim. The ruling is that if the defendant proves the property is a deposit for a known absent person, the claim is dismissed (the judge rules daf‘ al-khusumah).
This is a procedural ruling, not a substantive property right.
2
Determine the necessary condition for the absent person
The absent depositor must be identified. If the defendant says 'a man I do not know deposited it', the claim is not repelled. The identification can be by name or, per Abu Hanifa, by face alone.
The passage explicitly states that a claim from an unknown person is not repelled by consensus.
3
Locate the intra-Hanafi dispute
Abu Hanifa holds that witnesses knowing the absent person by face only is sufficient. Muhammad al-Shaybani requires knowledge of name and lineage. The text indicates the relied-upon view (al-sahih) is Muhammad's.
The dispute is only when the plaintiff claims from a specific named person; if the gha’ib is completely unknown, testimony is unacceptable by consensus.
4
Apply the ruling to a partial claim
If the defendant claims half is his and half is a deposit for another, and proves the deposit, the entire claim is repelled because separation is impossible.
This shows the holistic effect of the deposit proof.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
